مما أسقط عن ذمة الآمر ، ألا ترى أن الوجوب كان من أحكام الآخرة دون الدنيا، ولو ثبت الرجوع بمطلق الأمر لرجع بحق مضمون في الدنيا والآخرة ولا يجوز أن يرجع بأكثر مما أسقط وفي البزازية من كتاب الوكالة ذكر ضابطاً حسناً لما يرجع بلا شرط وما يرجع بشرط الرجوع فانظره ثمة قيد بالإطعام لأنه لو أمر أجنبياً أن يعتق عنه فأعتق لا يجزئه عندهما خلافاً لأبي يوسف والفرق على قولهما أن التمليك بغير بدل هبة ولا جواز لها بدون القبض ولم يوجد القبض في الإعتاق ووجد في الإطعام والكسوة في كفارة اليمين كالإطعام؛ كذا في البدائع وإن كان بجعل سماه أجزأه اتفاقا، وإن أعتق عنه بغير أمره لم يجز اتفاقاً لوقوعه عن المعتق ؛ كذا في الولوالجية. وخرج الصوم أيضاً فلو أمره أن يصوم عنه فصام لا يجزئه ؛ كذا في غاية البيان وقيد الإطعام بالأمر لأنه لو عن ذمته ا هـ . السابق بقوله على وجه الإباحة قوله : (وقد فرق في العناية الخ قال في النهر : ولا يجوز في سائر الكفارات أن يعطي الواحد أقل من نصف صاع وفي الفطرة ،خلاف وقدمنا أن الجواز جزم به غير واحد وأنه صحيح. وعليه فالفرق أن العدد منصوص عليه في الكفارة بخلاف غيره. وقوله في البحر أن هذا الفرق مفرع على القول الضعيف ممنوع .اهـ. وقال المقدسي في شرحه : وقدمنا في باب صدقة الفطر أن الأصح جواز دفع فرد الجمع وجمع لفرد ونقلناه عن الخانية والمحيط وغيرهما اهـ. قلت : والعجب من المؤلف حيث يقول إنه ضعيف وقد قال في باب صدقة الفطر بعده نقله عن عدة كتب فكان هو المذهب .
... [from zihar] and he does it, it suffices him; and ibaha is valid in expiations and ransoms but not in charities and tithes. Whoever repeats: if he gave sixty poor people each a mudd of wheat, it is not valid and he must give [again] to a poor person. If he does not find the first ones, then gives sixty others each a mudd, it is not valid; they differed about an additional mudd to each. In al-Muhit: it is agreed that if he gave ten poor people each a mudd, then the poor became independent, then needy again, and he gave them again a mudd, it is not valid. Similarly if he gave to mukatibs each a mudd, then they returned to slavery and their masters were rich, then they were made mukatibs again, then he gave them again, it is not valid because they became in a state in which giving to them is not permitted, so they became like another genus. His saying: 'If he commanded someone else to feed on his behalf for zihar, and he does it, it suffices him' because he released from him tamlik in meaning, and the poor person first grasps for him then for himself, so his ownership then his tamlik is realized, like the gift of a debt from the debtor when authorized to collect. Since the request for tamlik varies between gift and loan, and the origin is disconnection, there is no recourse on the commander in apparent narration. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: if the commander says 'with no recourse for the agent', then no recourse; if he says 'with recourse on me', then recourse; if the commander is silent, then in debt there is recourse, but in expiation and zakat there is no recourse according to Abu Hanifa, and according to Abu Yusuf there is recourse. The gist: they distinguished between commanding debt repayment and commanding zakat and expiation, although all are obligatory on the commander. I saw the distinction in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj from the book of agency attributed to Imam al-Karkhi: if he had recourse without condition, he would recoup more than what he discharged from the commander's liability. Do you not see that the obligation was part of the rulings of the afterlife, not this world? If recourse were established by absolute command, he would recoup with a guaranteed right in this world and the afterlife, and it is not permitted to recoup more than what he discharged. In al-Bazzaziyya from the book of agency, a good criterion is mentioned for what requires recourse without condition and what requires recourse by condition; see it there. He restricted it to feeding because if he commanded a stranger to free a slave on his behalf and he freed it, it does not suffice according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) contrary to Abu Yusuf. The distinction according to them: tamlik without compensation is a gift, and it is not valid without possession, and possession is not realized in emancipation, but it is realized in feeding and clothing. In expiation of an oath, it is like feeding. Similarly in al-Bada'i. If it was with a named fee (ju'l), it suffices by agreement. If he freed on his behalf without his command, it does not suffice by agreement because it occurs on behalf of the freed. Similarly in al-Walwalijiyya. Fasting is also excluded; if he commanded him to fast on his behalf, and he fasted, it does not suffice. Similarly in Ghayat al-Bayan. And he restricted it to feeding with command because if [he does it] on his own liability... End. The preceding [text] with his saying 'on the basis of ibaha'. His saying: 'And he distinguished in al-‘Inaya...' He said in al-Nahr: It is not permissible in all expiations to give a single person less than half a sa', but in fitrah there is disagreement. We have previously stated that permissibility is affirmed by more than one and that it is correct. Accordingly, the distinction: the number is prescribed in expiation unlike others. His saying in al-Bahr that this distinction is based on the weak opinion is not accepted. And al-Maqdisi said in his commentary: We have previously stated in the chapter on sadaqat al-fitr that the stronger view is the permissibility of giving one person the share of a group and vice versa, and we transmitted it from al-Khaniyya, al-Muhit, and others. End. I say: It is surprising from the author that he says it is weak, whereas he said in the chapter on sadaqat al-fitr later, transmitting from several books, that it is the madhhab.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage covers two main issues: (1) feeding sixty poor people in expiation, and (2) agency in performing expiation. Regarding feeding sixty: if a person gives each of sixty poor a mudd of wheat, it is not valid because the required quantity is half a sa' each. If he cannot find the original recipients, giving to sixty new ones does not fulfill the obligation. The text also discusses the effect of changes in the recipients' status (e.g., becoming wealthy then poor again) — repeating the gift to the same persons does not suffice because they are considered a different category. Regarding agency: if a person commands another to feed on his behalf for zihar, and the agent does so, it is valid because the agent acts as a conduit for tamlik. The poor person takes possession first on behalf of the original owner then for himself. The passage also discusses the issue of recourse (ruju'): according to Abu Hanifa, the agent cannot claim reimbursement from the commander for expiation or zakat without an explicit condition, because the obligation is purely religious (ukhravi); Abu Yusuf allows recourse. The text then compares with the case of freeing a slave by agency, which is not valid because possession (qabd) is not achieved. Finally, the passage returns to the distinction between expiation and fitrah regarding giving less than half a sa', concluding that the stronger view in the madhhab is the permissibility in fitrah.

Key Terms
المد (al-mudd): A measure of volume, approximately 0.5 liters in Hanafi fiqh.
الصاع (al-ṣā‘): A measure of volume, approximately 4 mudds or 3 liters in Hanafi fiqh.
التمليك (al-tamlīk): Transfer of ownership to the recipient.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person gives each of sixty poor people a mudd of wheat for zihar expiation, what must he do?
A) It is valid.
B) He must give an additional mudd to each.
C) He must give each a total of half a sa‘ to the same people.
D) He must repeat the expiation with a new set of sixty poor, each receiving half a sa‘.

Key Takeaway
For zihar expiation, each of the sixty poor must be given at least half a sa‘ of wheat; giving less invalidates the act and requires repetition with a new set.

Agency in Expiation: The Rujū‘ Dispute and Limitations
Explains agency in expiation and the recourse dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position on agency in expiation, identify the dispute between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf on the agent's right of recourse, and state the limitations (feeding vs. freeing vs. fasting).

Core Idea
The agent in expiation has no recourse against the commander without an explicit condition, because the obligation is ukhrawi, not worldly.

This passage addresses the validity of appointing an agent to perform expiation. While it is valid for feeding and clothing, it is not valid for freeing slaves or fasting. The passage also resolves a key intra-madhhab dispute: whether the agent can demand reimbursement from the commander. Understanding this distinction is crucial for proper fatwa-giving and for distinguishing between worldly debts and purely religious obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is appointed agency (amr) to perform expiation on behalf of another. The general ruling is that it is valid for feeding and clothing, but not for freeing slaves or fasting.
The text restricts to feeding (qayyada bi'l-it'am).
2
Analyze the rationale for validity
Agency in feeding is valid because tamlik (transfer of ownership) is realized: the poor person first takes possession on behalf of the commander, then for himself. This is analogous to appointing someone to collect a debt.
The text gives the example of gift of debt (hibat al-dayn).
3
Understand the limitation for freeing and fasting
For freeing slaves, agency is not valid according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because tamlik without compensation (gift) requires possession, which is not achieved in emancipation. Fasting cannot be delegated at all because it is a purely personal act.
Abu Yusuf allows agency in freeing as well.
4
Examine the recourse dispute
If the agent feeds the poor without a condition of recourse, can he claim reimbursement? According to Abu Hanifa: no, because the obligation is ukhrawi (related to the afterlife); allowing recourse would give the agent more than what he discharged. According to Abu Yusuf: yes, because it is a financial obligation. The later Hanafi position (mufta bihi) follows Abu Hanifa.
Imam al-Karkhi's reasoning: 'if recourse were established, the agent would recoup more than what he discharged.'
5
Apply the distinction between debt and expiation
Contrast this with agency for debt repayment, where the agent automatically has recourse. The distinction: debt is a worldly obligation with known value; expiation is a purely religious obligation that cannot be quantified in this world.
This resolves the apparent contradiction in rulings.

Kaffarah Feeding: Quantity Requirements and Changing Recipients
Ruling on the invalidity of giving one mudd each to 60 poor people and the issue of repeating when recipients change.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum quantity for kaffarah feeding and explain why giving one mudd per person is invalid, including cases when recipients change.

Core Idea
One mudd per person is insufficient for kaffarah; each must receive half a sa'.

The proper fulfillment of kaffarah requires precise adherence to the prescribed quantities. This lesson examines a common error: giving only one mudd per person. Understanding this ruling protects the validity of your expiation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is giving one mudd per person to 60 poor people for expiation. The ruling is that it is invalid (la yajuz).
The required quantity per person is half a sa' (approximately 1.75 kg) of staple food.
2
Recognize the consequence of deficiency
If the quantity is insufficient, the donor must give each person an additional mudd to reach the required amount.
Giving one mudd does not fulfill the obligation at all; it must be supplemented.
3
Analyze the case of changing recipients
If the original recipients become ineligible (e.g., wealthy) or cannot be found, giving the same deficient amount to new recipients is still invalid.
The obligation is not satisfied by distributing the same insufficient amount to different people.
4
Extend the ruling to similar cases
The text gives an example of mukatibs who later return to slavery and then become mukatibs again. The ruling remains the same: the deficient payment does not become valid due to changes in status.
The principle is that once the recipients are in a state where payment to them is invalid, they are treated as a new category.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لو أعطى ستين مسكيناً كل مسكين مداً من الحنطة لم يجز، وعليه أن يعيد على كل مسكين مداً آخر. فإن لم يجد الأولين فأعطى ستين آخرين كل مسكين مداً لم يجز. وفي المحيط: لو أعطى عشرة مساكين كل مسكين مداً مداً ثم استغنى المساكين ثم افتقروا فأعاد عليهم مداً لا يجوز، وكذا لو أدى إلى المكاتبين مداً مداً ثم ردوا إلى الرق ومواليهم أغنياء ثم كوتبوا ثانياً ثم أعاد عليهم لم يجز لأنهم صاروا بحال لا يجوز الأداء إليهم فصاروا كجنس آخر.
If he gave sixty poor persons each one mudd of wheat, it is not valid, and he must give each poor person another mudd. If he cannot find the first ones and gave another sixty each one mudd, it is not valid. And in al-Muhit: If he gave ten poor persons each one mudd, then the poor persons became wealthy, then became needy, and he gave them again a mudd, it is not valid. Similarly, if he gave to the mukatibs each one mudd, then they returned to slavery and their masters were wealthy, then they were made mukatib again, then he gave them again, it is not valid, because they came to a state in which giving to them is not permissible, so they became like another category.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining the invalidity of a common mistake in expiation feeding. The ruling is that giving each poor person only one mudd (approximately 750 grams) of staple food does not fulfill the requirement of kaffarah. Each poor person must be given a sufficient quantity; the minimum is half a sa' (approximately 1.75 kg) or two mudds. If the first recipients later become ineligible (e.g., they become wealthy or die), the donor cannot simply repeat the same insufficient amount to them or give it to others; he must start over with a proper amount to new recipients. The analogy of 'like another category' means that once the original recipients change status, they are treated as different individuals for the purpose of the obligation.

Key Terms
مد (mudd): A measure of volume approximately 750 grams of wheat or equivalent staple food.
مسكين (miskin): A poor person who is entitled to receive zakat or expiation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a person gives sixty poor people each one mudd of wheat for kaffarah, is his expiation valid according to the Hanafi school?
A) Valid, because he fed sixty people.
B) Invalid, because he must give each person at least half a sa'.
C) Valid, because one mudd is sufficient per person.
D) Invalid, because he must feed them for two meals.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi kaffarah, each poor person must receive at least half a sa' of staple food; giving one mudd invalidates the expiation.

Condition of Two Filling Meals in Kaffarah Feeding via Ibaha
Fiqh ruling: condition for valid expiation feeding.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition for valid ibaha feeding in kaffarah and apply it to scenarios combining ibaha and tamlik.

Core Idea
Ibaha in kaffarah requires two filling meals per poor person; tamlik is optional but valid.

The Hanafi school distinguishes between ibaha (permission to eat) and tamlik (ownership transfer) in expiation feeding. While some might assume that ownership transfer is required, the relied-upon position is that enabling the poor to eat two filling meals suffices. This lesson unpacks the condition of two meals, how ibaha differs from sadaqah, and the acceptable combinations of ibaha and tamlik.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling and Its Basis
The matn states that ibaha is valid in kaffarah and fidya but not in sadaqat and ushr. Recognize that the obligatory act is 'tamkin min al-ta'am' (enabling to taste food), not ownership transfer.
The term 'ibaha' is key: it permits consumption without transferring ownership.
2
Distinguish Ibaha from Tamlik
Ibaha: giver allows eating, ownership does not transfer; food ceases to be owned upon consumption. Tamlik: ownership is transferred to the poor person. Both are valid in kaffarah, but ibaha is the primary method.
In sadaqah, only tamlik is valid because the Quran uses 'ita' (giving) implying ownership.
3
State the Condition
The condition for ibaha is that each poor person receives two filling meals, either two lunches, two dinners, or one of each. Suhur counts as lunch.
One meal alone does not suffice; the expiation remains unfulfilled.
4
Apply to Combined Scenarios
The text addresses three scenarios: (1) combining ibaha and tamlik for the same person (valid), (2) giving ibaha to some and tamlik to others (valid), (3) completing one type with another (valid). The obligation is on a per-person basis: each must get two meals, but the method can vary.
Feeding different people different meals (e.g., lunch to some, dinner to others) does not suffice unless each gets two meals from the same type.
5
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
A narration from Abu Hanifa (via al-Hasan ibn Ziyad) requires tamlik for fidya, but the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah) treats fidya like kaffarah. The mufta bihi is that ibaha suffices for fidya as well.
This difference does not affect the condition of two meals; it concerns the method only.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتصح الإباحة في الكفارات) أي في إطعام الكفارات قوله : ( والفدية دون الصدقات والعشر) لورود الإطعام في الكفارات والفدية هو حقيقة في التمكين من الطعم. وإنما جاز التمليك باعتبار أنه تمكين، أما الواجب في الزكاة الإيتاء وفي صدقة الفطر الأداء وهما للتمليك حقيقة. فإن قلت : هل يجوز الجمع بين الإباحة والتمليك لرجل واحد أو لبعض المساكين دون البعض أو أن يعطي نوعاً للبعض ونوعاً للبعض؟ قلت : أما الأول ففي التتارخانية : إذا غداه وأعطاه مداً ففيه روايتان. واقتصر في البدائع على الجواز لأنه جمع بين شيئين حائزين على الانفراد وإن غداهم وأعطاهم قيمة العشاء أو عشاهم وأعطاهم قيمة الغداء يجوز . وأما الثانية كما إذا ملك ثلاثين وأطعم ثلاثين غداء وعشاء فهو جائز وأما الثالثة فقال في الكافي : ويجوز تكميل أحدهما بالآخر. فإن قلت : هل المباح له الطعام يستهلكه على ملك المبيح أو على ملك نفسه؟ قلت : إذا صار مأكولاً زال ملك المبيح عنه ولم يدخل في ملك أحد ؛ ذكره في البدائع. قيدنا بالإطعام لأن الإباحة في الكسوة في كفارة اليمين لا تجوز كما لو أعار عشرة مساكين كل مسكين ثوباً؛ كذا في المحيط. وجعل الفدية كالكفارة ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن عن الإمام أنه لا بد من التمليك لأنها تنبئ عنه كفدية العبد الجاني لا بد فيها من تمليك الأرش. قوله : (والشرط غدآن أو عشا آن مشبعان أو غداء وعشاء) أي الشرط في طعام الإباحة أكلتان مشبعتان لكل مسكين والسحور كالغداء، فلو غداهم يومين أو عشاهم كذلك أو غداهم وسحرهم أو سحرهم يومين أجزأه . ولو غدى ستين مسكيناً وعشى ستين غيرهم لم يجزه إلا أن يعيد على أحد النوعين منهم غداء أو عشاء، ولو غدى واحداً وعشى آخر لم يجز .
His statement: 'And permittance to eat is valid in expiations' i.e., in feeding of expiations. His statement: 'and the fidya, excluding sadaqat and ushr' because the term 'feeding' in expiations and fidya is literally 'enabling to taste food'. Ownership transfer is permitted only because it is a form of enabling. As for the obligation in zakat, it is 'giving' and in sadaqat al-fitr, it is 'payment', and both are truly ownership transfer. If you ask: Is it permissible to combine permission (ibaha) and ownership transfer for one man, or for some poor persons without others, or to give one type to some and another type to others? I say: As for the first, in al-Tatar Khaniyyah: If he fed him lunch and also gave him a mudd, there are two narrations. Al-Bada'i restricted to permissibility because it combines two things individually permissible. If he fed them lunch and gave them the value of dinner, or fed them dinner and gave them the value of lunch, it is permissible. As for the second, like if he gave ownership to thirty and fed thirty lunch and dinner, it is permissible. As for the third, al-Kafi said: It is permissible to complete one with the other. If you ask: Does the one permitted the food consume it from the property of the permitter or from his own property? I say: When it becomes eaten, the permitter's ownership ceases and it does not enter into anyone's ownership; mentioned in al-Bada'i. We restricted to feeding because permission in clothing is not valid for the expiation of an oath, like if he lent ten poor persons each a garment; thus in al-Muhit. The fidya is made like kaffarah in the apparent narration. Al-Hasan narrated from the Imam that ownership transfer is necessary because it indicates like fidya of the offending slave, which requires transfer of the compensation. His statement: 'And the condition is two lunches or two dinners filling, or a lunch and a dinner.' i.e., the condition in the food of permission (ibaha) is two filling meals for each poor person, and suhur (pre-dawn meal) is like lunch. So if he fed them lunch for two days or dinner similarly, or fed them lunch and suhur, or suhur for two days, it suffices. If he fed sixty poor persons lunch and fed another sixty dinner, it does not suffice unless he repeats for one of the two types—lunch or dinner—for them. And if he fed one poor person lunch and another dinner, it does not suffice.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage explains the condition of 'ibaha' (permission to eat) in expiation feeding, which is a legal mechanism distinct from ownership transfer. The matn states that ibaha is valid in kaffarah and fidya but not in sadaqat and ushr, because sadaqat require actual ownership transfer (tamlik). The sharh clarifies that the mandatory method in kaffarah is to enable the poor person to eat the food (tamkin min al-ta'am), not to give it as property. However, giving ownership is also valid because it implies enabling. The author then addresses three scenarios: combining ibaha and tamlik for one person (acceptable), giving ibaha to some and tamlik to others (acceptable), and completing one type with the other (acceptable). A key point: when food is consumed via ibaha, it does not become owned by the poor person but ceases to be owned by the giver. The condition is that each poor person must receive two filling meals, either two lunches, two dinners, or one of each. Suhur (pre-dawn meal) counts as lunch. The ruling specifies that feeding different poor people different meals (e.g., lunch to some, dinner to others) does not fulfill the obligation unless additional meals are provided. This lesson also notes a difference of opinion within the Hanafi school: some narrations from Imam Abu Hanifa require tamlik (ownership transfer) for fidya.

Key Terms
الإباحة (al-ibāhah): A legal mechanism where the giver permits the poor person to eat the food, but ownership does not transfer; the food is consumed and ceases to be owned.
التملك (al-tamalluk): The act of the poor person taking ownership of the food, as opposed to merely being permitted to eat.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum requirement for feeding in kaffarah via ibaha according to the Hanafi school?
A) One meal per poor person.
B) Two filling meals per poor person.
C) Two mudds of wheat per poor person.
D) Ownership of the food transferred to the poor person.

Key Takeaway
In kaffarah feeding via ibaha, each poor person must receive two filling meals; otherwise, the expiation is invalid.

Ibaha in Kaffarat: Enabling Access vs. Transferring Ownership
Explaining the ruling that ibaha is valid in kaffarat and fidyah but not in zakat

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that ibaha is valid in kaffarat and fidyah, and explain the linguistic proof distinguishing it from zakat.

Core Idea
Ibaha (permitting consumption) suffices in kaffarat because 'it'am' means enabling, not ownership.

In this lesson, we examine a key fiqhi distinction: why the Hanafi school allows simply allowing the poor to eat (ibaha) in expiations (kaffarat) and redemption payments (fidyah), but requires actual transfer of ownership (tamlik) in zakat and sadaqat al-fitr. The basis lies in the Quranic vocabulary used in each obligation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The ruling is that ibaha is valid in kaffarat and fidyah but not in sadaqat and 'ushr.
The base text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq states this.
2
Locate the Quranic proof
The word 'it'am (feeding) appears in verses on kaffarat and fidyah, e.g., Surah al-Ma'idah:89.
The Hanafi school uses this as the primary dalil.
3
Analyze the linguistic interpretation
'It'am literally means enabling access to food, not transferring ownership. Therefore ibaha fulfills the command.
This is a linguistic (lughawi) argument.
4
Contrast with zakat and fitr
Zakat uses 'ita and sadaqat al-fitr uses 'ada, both of which inherently imply tamlik.
The difference in words leads to different hukm.
5
Note the intra-school difference
Some narrations from Abu Hanifa require tamlik even in kaffarat, but the relied-upon position is ibaha.
Al-Hasan's riwayah is an exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وتصح الإباحة في الكفارات) أي في إطعام الكفارات قوله : ( والفدية دون الصدقات والعشر) لورود الإطعام في الكفارات والفدية هو حقيقة في التمكين من الطعم. وإنما جاز التمليك باعتبار أنه تمكين، أما الواجب في الزكاة الإيتاء وفي صدقة الفطر الأداء وهما للتمليك حقيقة . فإن قلت : هل يجوز الجمع بين الإباحة والتمليك لرجل واحد أو لبعض المساكين دون البعض أو أن يعطي نوعاً للبعض ونوعاً للبعض؟ قلت : أما الأول ففي التتارخانية : إذا غداه وأعطاه مداً ففيه روايتان. واقتصر في البدائع على الجواز لأنه جمع بين شيئين حائزين على الانفراد وإن غداهم وأعطاهم قيمة العشاء أو عشاهم وأعطاهم قيمة الغداء يجوز . وأما الثانية كما إذا ملك ثلاثين وأطعم ثلاثين غداء وعشاء فهو جائز وأما الثالثة فقال في الكافي : ويجوز تكميل أحدهما بالآخر. فإن قلت : هل المباح له الطعام يستهلكه على ملك المبيح أو على ملك نفسه؟ قلت : إذا صار مأكولاً زال ملك المبيح عنه ولم يدخل في ملك أحد ؛ ذكره في البدائع. قيدنا بالإطعام لأن الإباحة في الكسوة في كفارة اليمين لا تجوز كما لو أعار عشرة مساكين كل مسكين ثوباً؛ كذا في المحيط. وجعل الفدية كالكفارة ظاهر الرواية، وروى الحسن عن الإمام أنه لا بد من التمليك لأنها تنبئ عنه كفدية العبد الجاني لا بد فيها من تمليك الأرش.
He said: (The permissibility of ibaha in kaffarat) i.e., in feeding of kaffarat. He said: (and the fidyah apart from sadaqat and 'ushr) because the word 'it'am occurs in kaffarat and fidyah, and it is literal for enabling of food. Tamlik is permitted because it is a form of enabling. As for the obligation in zakat, it is 'ita' (giving), and in sadaqat al-fitr, it is 'ada' (payment), and both are literally for tamlik. If you say: Is it permissible to combine ibaha and tamlik for one man, or for some misakin and not others, or to give one type to some and another type to others? I say: As for the first, in al-Tatarkhaniyyah: If he fed him lunch and gave him a mudd, there are two narrations. Al-Bada'i' restricted to permissibility because it combines two things valid individually, and if he fed them lunch and gave them the value of dinner, or fed them dinner and gave them the value of lunch, it is valid. As for the second, like if he gave ownership to thirty and fed thirty lunch and dinner, it is valid. As for the third, al-Kafi said: It is valid to complete one with the other. If you say: Does the one permitted the food consume it on the ownership of the permittor or on his own ownership? I say: When it becomes eaten, the ownership of the permittor ceases and it does not enter into anyone's ownership; mentioned in al-Bada'i'. We restricted to feeding because ibaha in clothing in kaffarah of oath is not valid, like if he lent ten misakin each a garment; so in al-Muhit. And making fidyah like kaffarah is the apparent riwayah, and al-Hasan reported from the Imam that tamlik is necessary because it indicates like fidyah of the slave who commits an offense, where tamlik of the compensation is essential.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the permissibility of ibaha (permitting consumption without ownership) in kaffarat and fidyah. The key distinction is that the Quranic word 'it'am' (feeding) in these contexts means enabling access to food, not transferring ownership. Therefore, one may simply allow the poor to eat, rather than giving them ownership of the food. In contrast, zakat and sadaqat al-fitr require tamlik (ownership) because the texts use 'ita' (giving) and 'ada' (payment), which imply transfer of ownership. The passage then discusses various scenarios: combining ibaha and tamlik for the same person (valid with two narrations), giving different types to different recipients, and the issue of on whose ownership the food is consumed (it ceases to be owned by the permittor without entering the recipient's ownership). The Hanafi school follows the apparent riwayah that ibaha is valid, though a rivayah from al-Hasan ibn Ziyad reports that tamlik is required based on analogy with the fidyah of a slave's offense.

Key Terms
الإباحة (al-ibahah): Permitting the poor to consume food without transferring ownership.
التمليك (al-tamlik): Transferring ownership of the food to the poor.
الفدية (al-fidyah): Redemption payment in lieu of fasting or other obligations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, why is ibaha (permitting use) sufficient in kaffarat but not in zakat?
A) Because kaffarat are lighter sins than zakat.
B) Because the Quranic word 'it'am' means enabling access, not ownership, while zakat requires tamlik.
C) Because the poor are more deserving in kaffarat.
D) Because kaffarat can only be done by ibaha.

Key Takeaway
In kaffarat and fidyah, the Quranic term 'it'am' allows ibaha (enabling access) without ownership; in zakat and fitr, 'ita' and 'ada' require tamlik.

Subsidiary Rulings on Ibaha: Combining Modes and Ownership Status
Examining subsidiary issues: combining ibaha and tamlik, ownership, clothing exception

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rules for combining ibaha and tamlik in kaffarat, identify the ownership status of consumed food, and state the exception for clothing.

Core Idea
Ibaha and tamlik can be combined in kaffarat, and food consumed under ibaha ceases to be owned without entering the recipient's ownership.

Having established that ibaha is valid in kaffarat, the commentator now addresses practical questions: Can one combine ibaha and tamlik for the same poor person? Can one give ibaha to some and tamlik to others? What happens to the ownership of food that is consumed under ibaha? And is ibaha valid for clothing? These subsidiary rulings clarify the scope and limits of ibaha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three questions posed
The text asks about combining ibaha and tamlik for one person, for different groups, and giving different types to different groups.
The commentator uses a question-and-answer format.
2
Examine the first scenario: combining for one person
If a person feeds a poor person lunch (ibaha) and also gives a mudd of grain (tamlik), two narrations exist; the majority view in al-Bada'i' deems it valid.
Combining is permissible because each method is valid individually.
3
Examine the second and third scenarios
Giving ibaha to some and tamlik to others is valid. Giving different types (e.g., feeding some, owning to others) is also valid.
The text cites al-Kafi that it is allowed to complete one with the other.
4
Analyze the ownership question
When food is consumed under ibaha, the permittor's ownership ceases, and the food does not become owned by the eater.
This avoids any ambiguity about dual ownership.
5
Note the exception for clothing
Ibaha in clothing (e.g., lending a garment) does not fulfill kaffarah because the Quran commands 'feeding', not 'clothing'.
This is a restriction based on the text.

Source Text

Agent's Right to Reimbursement Without Stipulation
Clarifying when an agent can claim reimbursement without explicit stipulation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish when an agent can claim reimbursement without stipulation and apply the Hanafi rule based on whether the payment is in exchange for ownership.

Core Idea
An agent can reclaim expenses without stipulation only when the recipient obtains the property in exchange for ownership, as in zakat and debt payment.

In Hanafi agency law, the right to reimbursement depends on the nature of the transaction. A common question is whether an agent who pays on behalf of his commander can automatically recover the amount. This lesson clarifies the key distinction: reimbursement is automatic when the payment is compensatory (like zakat or debt), but not when it is a pure gift. We will examine the text from al-Bazzaziyyah that establishes this rule.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two categories of payments
Read the passage and note the two types: (1) payments where the recipient obtains property in exchange for ownership (e.g., zakat, kaffarah, debt repayment), and (2) payments where the recipient obtains it without exchange (e.g., a pure gift).
The text uses the phrase 'muqabil bi-milk al-mal' for exchange-based payments.
2
State the ruling for each category
For exchange-based payments, the agent can reclaim without a stipulation. For gift-based payments, the agent cannot reclaim unless a condition was made.
This is the core legal consequence.
3
Understand the underlying reasoning (talil)
The reasoning is that in exchange-based payments, the commander becomes the owner of what was given in exchange, so the agent's payment is effectively made on the commander's behalf and must be reimbursed. In gifts, the commander does not receive ownership, so the agent is considered a donor.
The text explains: 'the ownership also becomes established for the commander in exchange for ownership'.
4
Apply the rule to new scenarios
Given a new scenario (e.g., agent pays a debt, agent gives a gift), classify it as exchange or gift and then state whether reimbursement is automatic.
Practice with the tasks below.

Source Text

قوله : (وقد رأيت الفرق في السراج الخ قال في النهر : مقتضاه أنه لا علمت أنه يرجع .اهـ. وأجاب بعض الفضلاء بأنه لما قبل الشرط فقد التزمه باختياره قوله : (وفي البزازية من كتاب الوكالة الخ) عبارتها : أمر غيره بأن ينفق عليه أو يقضي دينه ففعل يرجع بلا شرط الرجوع، ولو قال عوض عن هبتي أو أعطه عن كفارتي أو أد زكاة مالي أوهب لفلان عني أ ألفاً لا بلا شرط الرجوع ففي كل موضع ملك المدفوع إليه المال المدفوع مقابلاً بملك المال فالمأمور يرجع بلا شرط الرجوع، وفي كل موضع ملك المدفوع إليه غير مقابل بملك المال لا : يرجع بلا شرط لأن الدافع يملك المدفوع عن الآمر أولاً في ضمن التمليك من المدفوع حتى تقضي الزكاة والتعويض والكفارة، فإذا ملكه المدفوع إليه مقابلاً بالملك كان الملك ثابتاً للآمر أيضاً مقابلاً للملك فرجع عليه المأمور لأن بذلك الملك يجب على من يجب له الملك، أما إذا ملك المدفوع إليه المدفوع لا مقابلاً بالملك يرجع
He said: (And I saw the difference in al-Siraj...) He said in al-Nahr: Its implication is that I do not know that he can reclaim. A certain virtuous person answered that since he accepted the condition, he has committed to it by his choice. He said: (And in al-Bazzaziyyah from the Book of Agency...) Its expression: He ordered someone else to spend on him or pay his debt, and he did it, he can reclaim without a condition of reimbursement. And if he said: 'Compensate for my gift, or give it for my kaffarah, or pay the zakat of my wealth, or give to so-and-so on my behalf a thousand', then no, without a condition of reimbursement. So in every case where the recipient owns the paid property in exchange for ownership of property, the agent can reclaim without condition of reimbursement. And in every case where the recipient owns it not in exchange for ownership, he does not reclaim without condition, because the giver owns what is paid on behalf of the commander initially within the tamlik from the recipient until the zakat, compensation, and kaffarah are fulfilled. So when the recipient owns it in exchange for ownership, the ownership also becomes established for the commander in exchange for ownership, so the agent has recourse against him because by that ownership, it is obligatory upon the one for whom ownership is due. As for when the recipient owns the paid property not in exchange for ownership, he can reclaim? (the text ends ambiguously).
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on when an agent acting on behalf of another can claim reimbursement without an explicit stipulation. The distinction is based on whether the recipient receives the property in exchange for something (e.g., payment of a debt, zakat, kaffarah) or as a pure gift. In exchange-based cases, the agent can reclaim because the commander ultimately becomes the owner of what was given in exchange. In gift cases, the agent is considered a donor and cannot reclaim unless there is a stipulation. The passage quotes from al-Bazzaziyyah and al-Siraj, and includes a discussion about accepting a condition.

Key Terms
الرجوع (al-ruju'): Reimbursement or recourse against the commander for expenses incurred.
مقابل بملك المال (muqabil bi-milk al-mal): In exchange for ownership of property; used for payments like zakat, kaffarah, debt repayment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When an agent gives zakat on behalf of another, can the agent claim reimbursement without a stipulation?
A) Yes, always.
B) No, never.
C) Yes, because zakat is considered a compensatory payment.
D) No, because zakat is a gift to the poor.

Key Takeaway
The agent's right to reimbursement without stipulation depends on whether the recipient obtains property in exchange for ownership; if yes, reimbursement is automatic; if no, it requires stipulation.

Condition of Two Filling Meals in Kaffarah Feeding
Specifies the requirement that each poor person must receive two filling meals.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition of two filling meals per poor person in kaffarah feeding and apply it to scenarios involving different meal arrangements and food types.

Core Idea
For kaffarah feeding, each poor person must receive two filling meals; satiety matters, not a fixed quantity.

In the Hanafi school, the condition for feeding in kaffarah (e.g., for broken oaths or zihar) is that each poor person must receive two meals that are filling. This lesson unpacks what constitutes valid meals, the role of satiety, and special cases like mixing groups or using barley bread. We will analyze the key conditions and their practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic condition
Read the opening statement: the condition is two filling meals per poor person – either two lunches, two dinners, or one lunch and one dinner. Note that suhoor is considered a lunch.
2
Understand the satiety criterion
The text emphasizes that satiety (shib') is the measure, not a fixed weight. Even a small amount that fills suffices. Check the example of four loaves for ten people.
Barley and corn bread require a condiment (idam) to achieve satiety.
3
Analyze the mixing rule
If you feed one group lunch and a different group dinner, it does not suffice. Each poor person must receive two meals from the same day. Only feeding the same group both meals works.
Feeding 120 people one meal each counts as half; you must repeat to 60 to complete one day's kaffarah.
4
Consider exceptions and ikhtilaf
The mashayikh differed on feeding a person already full or a non-discerning minor, and on using barley bread without condiment. Al-Halwani required satiety from the start; others accepted it. The stronger view is that satiety is the criterion and barley bread with condiment is valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والشرط غدآن أو عشا آن مشبعان أو غداء وعشاء أي الشرط في طعام الإباحة أكلتان مشبعتان لكل مسكين والسحور كالغداء، فلو غداهم يومين أو عشاهم كذلك أو غداهم وسحرهم أو سحرهم يومين أجزأه . ولو غدى ستين مسكيناً وعشى ستين غيرهم لم يجزه إلا أن يعيد على أحد النوعين منهم غداء أو عشاء، ولو غدى واحداً وعشى آخر لم يجز . وقيد بالشبع لأنه لو كان فيهم من هو شبعان قبل الأكل أو ليس بمراهق لا يجزئه، واختلف المشايخ فيه ومال الحلواني إلى عدم الجواز وفي المصباح: الأكل معروف ... وأشار به إلى أنه لا معتبر بعد الشبع إلى مقدار الطعام حتى روي عن أبي حنيفة في كفارة اليمين لو قدم أربعة أرغفة إلى عشرة مساكين وشبعوا أجزاه وإن لم يبلغ ذلك صاعاً أو نصف صاع ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وإلى أنه لا بد من الإدام في خبز الشعير والذرة ليمكنهم الاستيفاء إلى الشبع بخلاف خبز البر. وقد اختلف المشايخ في جواز إطعام خبز الشعير بالإدام بناء على أن محمداً نص على خبز البر في الزيادات فقال البعض لا يجوز بخبز الشعير، وبعضهم جوزه مع الإدام وإليه مال الكرخي كما في التتارخانية. وفي الينابيع : لو أطعم مائة وعشرين مسكيناً في يوم واحد أكلة واحدة مشبعة لم يجز إلا عن نصف الإطعام فإن أعاده على ستين مسكيناً أجزأه ا وفي البدائع : أوصى بأن يكفر عنه فأطعم الوصي الغداء للعدد المنصوص عليه ثم ماتوا قبل العشاء يستأنف فيغدي ويعشي غيرهم لأنه لا سبيل إلى التفريق ولا يضمن الوصي شيئاً لأنه غير متعد إذ لا صنع له في الموت ا هـ. وينبغي أن المكفر إذا غدى العدد ثم غابوا أن ينتظر حضورهم أو يعيد الغداء العشاء على عدد غيرهم، وينبغي في الوصي أن ينتظر لرجاء حضورهم
The condition is two lunches, or two dinners, both filling, or lunch and dinner. That is, the condition in food of ibaha is two filling meals for each miskin, and suhoor is like lunch. So if he fed them lunch for two days, or dinner similarly, or fed them lunch and suhoor, or suhoor for two days, it suffices. And if he fed sixty miskin lunch and fed sixty others dinner, it does not suffice unless he repeats one of the two types to them, lunch or dinner. And if he fed one lunch and another dinner, it does not suffice. It is restricted by satiety, because if among them there is one who is full before eating, or is not a discerning minor, it does not suffice. The mashayikh differed on this, and al-Halwani leaned towards non-permissibility. In al-Misbah: eating is known... And he indicated by it that after satiety, the quantity of food is not considered, such that it is narrated from Abu Hanifa concerning kaffarah of oath: if he presented four loaves to ten misakin and they were satiated, it suffices even if that does not amount to a sa' or half a sa'; so in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And that a condiment is necessary in barley bread and corn bread to enable them to reach satiety, unlike wheat bread. The mashayikh differed on the permissibility of feeding barley bread with condiment based on the fact that Muhammad explicitly mentioned wheat bread in al-Ziyadat. Some said it is not permissible with barley bread; some permitted it with condiment, and al-Karkhi leaned towards this, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. In al-Yanabi': If he fed one hundred and twenty misakin in one day one filling meal, it does not suffice except for half of the feeding; if he repeats it to sixty misakin, it suffices. In al-Bada'i': If he bequeathed that kaffarah be performed for him, and the executor fed the prescribed number lunch, then they died before dinner, he starts anew and feeds and dinners others, because there is no way to split, and the executor is not liable for anything because he did not transgress, as he has no hand in death. It is suitable that the one performing kaffarah, if he fed the number lunch and then they disappeared, he should wait for their return or repeat the lunch and dinner to a different number. And it is suitable for the executor to wait hoping for their return.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement that specifies the condition for feeding in kaffarah: each poor person must receive two filling meals in a day, either two lunches, two dinners, or one lunch and one dinner. Suhoor is considered like lunch. The commentary then provides details: feeding the same meals for multiple days is valid, but mixing different groups for lunch and dinner is not valid unless the same group receives both meals. The condition of satiety is emphasized; even a small amount that satisfies suffices, and barley bread requires a condiment to achieve satiety. There is ikhtilaf among Hanafi scholars about feeding barley bread. The passage also addresses cases of feeding 120 poor people in one day (counts as half) and the situation of an executor for a deceased person's kaffarah.

Key Terms
غداء (ghada'): Lunch meal.
عشاء ('asha'): Dinner meal.
شبع (shib'): Satiety; the condition that the poor person is filled by the meal.
إدام (idam): Condiment or side dish to make bread more filling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because each gets one meal.
B) No, because each poor person must receive two meals.
C) Yes, if both groups are poor.
D) No, unless he repeats one of the meals to the same group.

Key Takeaway
The condition for valid kaffarah feeding is that each poor person must receive two filling meals in one day; satiety, not quantity, is the measure.

Giving Kaffarah Food to One Poor Person for Two Months
Ruling that giving kaffarah food to a single poor person for two months is valid.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on giving kaffarah food to a single poor person over multiple days and explain the legal reasoning of ta'dadan hukman.

Core Idea
Feeding one poor person for two months counts as feeding sixty poor persons because the need renews daily.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi ruling: giving kaffarah food to a single poor person over an extended period. While one might think that kaffarah requires sixty distinct recipients, Hanafi jurists argue that the purpose is to fulfill need, and since need is renewed each day, the recipient is legally counted as multiple. This ruling hinges on a subtle distinction between tamlik (ownership) and ibaha (permission), with an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf that we will explore.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is being ruled upon? The act of giving kaffarah food to a single poor person for two months. The ruling is that it is valid (sahih).
The ruling is explicitly stated in the matn: 'صح'.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
What is the proof for this ruling? The author states: 'because the purpose is to fill the need of the needy, and need is renewed with the renewal of days.' This is a rational proof based on the maqsad (purpose) of kaffarah.
This is a dalil aqli (rational proof) rather than a textual one.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How exactly does the proof lead to the ruling? The need (khallah) is the operative cause. Since need recurs daily, each day's feeding satisfies a separate instance of need, thereby legally counting as a separate poor person. This is the principle of ta'dadan hukman (counting in effect).
The legal fiction allows repetition over time to substitute for multiple recipients.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
What is the intra-Hanafi dispute? Abu Yusuf in his later opinion holds that feeding one poor person for sixty days does not suffice for ibaha (permission to eat), but the relied-upon view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is that it suffices regardless of tamlik or ibaha.
The dispute revolves around the condition of tamlik (ownership) vs ibaha.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
Which position is mufta bihi? The majority view (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) is the operative ruling. Al-Bada'i' and al-Tatarkhaniyyah support this tarjih.
The later Hanafi masters adopt the view that no distinction between tamlik and ibaha is needed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وإن أعطى فقيراً شهرين (صح) لأن المقصود سد خلة المحتاج والحاجة تتجدد بتجدد الأيام فتكرر المسكين بتكرر الحاجة حكماً فكان تعداداً حكماً قيد بالتمليك لأنه لو أطعم مسكيناً غداه ستين يوماً لا يجزئه في قول أبي يوسف الأخير كما في التتارخانية فيحتاج إلى الفرق بين الإباحة والتمليك في حق الواحد والحق أن لا فرق على المذهب لما في البدائع : لو أعطى طعام عشرة مساكين في كفارة اليمين في عشرة أيام لمسكين واحد غداه وعشاه عشرة أيام أجزأه عندنا وفي المصباح: الخلة بالفتح الفقر والحاجة قوله : (ولو في يوم لا إلا عن يومه) مع عشاه من حنطة فالأمر يملكه أيضاً لا مقابلاً بالملك فيكون متبرعاً فلا يرجع بلا شرط الضمان
He said: (And if he gives to a poor person for two months, it is valid) because the purpose is to fill the need of the needy, and need is renewed with the renewal of days, so the miskin is repeated by the repetition of need in effect, and thus it is a counting in effect. He restricted it with tamlik, because if he fed a miskin lunch for sixty days, it does not suffice in the later opinion of Abu Yusuf, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah, so one needs to differentiate between ibaha and tamlik regarding the same person. But the truth is that there is no difference according to the madhhab, as in al-Bada'i': If he gave the food of ten misakin in kaffarah of oath over ten days to one miskin, feeding him lunch and dinner for ten days, it suffices according to us. In al-Misbah: al-khallah (need/poverty) is poverty and need. He said: (And if in one day, only for that day) with his dinner of wheat, then the person in command also owns it not in exchange for ownership, thus he is a donor and cannot claim reimbursement without a stipulation of compensation.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on giving kaffarah food to a single poor person for two months. The reasoning is that the purpose is to fulfill need, and need is renewed daily. Therefore, feeding the same person daily counts (hukman) as feeding different persons. This applies to tamlik (ownership). There is an ikhtilaf: in the later opinion of Abu Yusuf, feeding one person for sixty days does not suffice for ibaha, but the relied-upon view is that it does suffice. The commentary on the phrase 'ولو في يوم لا إلا عن يومه' explains that if the food is given in one day, it only counts for that day. The additional sentence about wheat and ownership seems to be a separate note about agency and reimbursement, indicating that if the agent gives wheat, he does so as a donor and cannot reclaim without stipulation.

Key Terms
خلة (khallah): Poverty or need; the purpose is to fill the need of the poor.
تعداداً حكماً (ta'dadan hukman): Legally counted as multiple (even if physically one person).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a person gives kaffarah food to one poor person for two months, is this valid?
A) Yes, because need is renewed daily.
B) No, because kaffarah requires 60 different poor persons.
C) Yes, only in the opinion of Abu Yusuf.
D) No, because the food must be given all at once.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates giving kaffarah food to one poor person over multiple days because the daily renewal of need makes the recipient legally count as multiple persons.

Rulings on Feeding (It'am) in Kaffarah: Conditions and Counting
Commentary on multiple rulings regarding feeding expiation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi conditions for valid feeding in kaffarah and apply the ruling on feeding one poor person over multiple days.

Core Idea
Feeding one poor person over multiple days counts as multiple expiations because need renews with each day.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq by Ibn Nujaym details essential rulings on feeding as expiation. It clarifies the condition of satiation, the type of bread and need for condiment, and resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute on whether feeding one poor person multiple times suffices. Understanding these rules ensures the expiation is valid and fulfills the obligation correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition of satiation
Note that feeding must cause satiation. If the poor person is already full or not an adolescent, it does not suffice. Also, after satiation, the amount of food is irrelevant; even a small amount that fills is sufficient.
Refer to the example of four loaves for ten poor from Abu Hanifa.
2
Analyze the type of bread and condiment requirement
For barley or corn bread, a condiment (idam) is necessary to enable satiation. For wheat bread, it is not needed. There is an ikhtilaf among scholars on whether barley bread with condiment is permissible; the relied-upon view allows it.
Al-Karkhi inclined to permissibility.
3
Understand the counting rule: one poor over multiple days
Giving one poor person food for multiple days (e.g., thirty sa' over thirty days) suffices for multiple expiations because the need is renewed daily. This applies only when the food is given as tamlik (ownership). In ibaha (mere permission), the later view of Abu Yusuf differs, but the correct Hanafi view makes no distinction.
The key evidence is the hadith or rational principle of renewed need.
4
Compare tamlik vs ibaha and the ikhtilaf
The dispute: Abu Yusuf's later view holds that ibaha does not count for multiple days, while Abu Hanifa and the correct view affirm it does. The authors of al-Bada'i' and al-Muhit support Abu Hanifa.
The practical difference is in cases of feeding without ownership transfer.
5
Apply the rule to combined expiations
When feeding for two zihars, one must feed 120 poor (60 each). Feeding 60 poor only suffices for one. But if the expiations are of different types (zihar and iftar), feeding 60 poor with proper intention suffices for both.
Intention matters when types differ; deficiency in number is not allowed.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صبي وقيد بالشبع لأنه لو كان فيهم من هو شبعان قبل الأكل أو ليس بمراهق لا يجزئه، واختلف المشايخ فيه ومال الحلواني إلى عدم الجواز وفي المصباح: الأكل معروف والأكل بضمتين وإسكان الثاني للتخفيف المأكول والأكلة بالفتح المرة وبالضم اللقمة. والغداء بالمد طعام الغداة والعَشاء بالفتح وبالمد طعام العشاء بالكسر. والسَّحور بفتح السين ما يؤكل في السحر ما قبل الصبح وبالضم الأكل وقته. وأشار به إلى أنه لا معتبر بعد الشبع إلى مقدار الطعام حتى روي عن أبي حنيفة في كفارة اليمين لو قدم أربعة أرغفة إلى عشرة مساكين وشبعوا أجزاه وإن لم يبلغ ذلك صاعاً أو نصف صاع ؛ كذا في التتارخانية. وإلى أنه لا بد من الإدام في خبز الشعير والذرة ليمكنهم الاستيفاء إلى الشبع بخلاف خبز البر. وقد اختلف المشايخ في جواز إطعام خبز الشعير بالإدام بناء على أن محمداً نص على خبز البر في الزيادات فقال البعض لا يجوز بخبز الشعير، وبعضهم جوزه مع الإدام وإليه مال الكرخي كما في التتارخانية. وفي الينابيع : لو أطعم مائة وعشرين مسكيناً في يوم واحد أكلة واحدة مشبعة لم يجز إلا عن نصف الإطعام فإن أعاده على ستين مسكيناً أجزأه. وفي البدائع : أوصى بأن يكفر عنه فأطعم الوصي الغداء للعدد المنصوص عليه ثم ماتوا قبل العشاء يستأنف فيغدي ويعشي غيرهم لأنه لا سبيل إلى التفريق ولا يضمن الوصي شيئاً لأنه غير متعد إذ لا صنع له في الموت. وينبغي أن المكفر إذا غدى العدد ثم غابوا أن ينتظر حضورهم أو يعيد الغداء العشاء على عدد غيرهم، وينبغي في الوصي أن ينتظر لرجاء حضورهم. قوله : (وإن أعطى فقيراً شهرين (صح) لأن المقصود سد خلة المحتاج والحاجة تتجدد بتجدد الأيام فتكرر المسكين بتكرر الحاجة حكماً فكان تعداداً حكماً قيد بالتمليك لأنه لو أطعم مسكيناً غداه ستين يوماً لا يجزئه في قول أبي يوسف الأخير كما في التتارخانية فيحتاج إلى الفرق بين الإباحة والتمليك في حق الواحد والحق أن لا فرق على المذهب لما في البدائع : لو أعطى طعام عشرة مساكين في كفارة اليمين في عشرة أيام لمسكين واحد غداه وعشاه عشرة أيام أجزأه عندنا. وفي المصباح: الخلة بالفتح الفقر والحاجة. قوله : (ولو في يوم لا إلا عن يومه) أي لو أعطى فقيراً ثلاثين صاعاً في يوم لا يجزئه إلا عن واحد لفقد التعدد حقيقة وحكماً لعدم تجدد الحاجة. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا أعطاه بدفعة واحدة أو متفرقاً على الصحيح كما في المحيط. وفي طعام الإباحة لا يجوز في يوم واحد وإن فرق بلا خلاف كما في التتارخانية. والكسوة في كفارة اليمين كالإطعام حتى لو أعطى مسكيناً واحداً عشرة أثواب في عشرة أيام يجوز في كفارة اليمين لتجدد الحاجة حكماً باعتبار تجدد الزمان. وفي البدائع في كفارة اليمين : لو غدى رجلاً واحداً عشرين يوماً أو عشى واحداً عشرين يوماً أجزأه عندنا. وفي المحيط : لو أعطى مسكيناً عن فدية صوم يومين عليه فعن أبي يوسف روايتان؛ وفي رواية يجزئه عنهما، وفي رواية لا يجزئه. قيل: وهذا قول أبي حنيفة كما في كفارة اليمين. قوله : (ولا يستأنف بوطئها في خلال الإطعام لأن الله تعالى إنما شرط في التحرير والصوم أن يكون قبل التماس ولم يشترطه في الإطعام ولا يحمل المطلق على المقيد وإن وردا في حادثة واحدة بعد أن يكونا حكمين - كذا في الكافي - إلا أنه منع من الوطء قبله لجواز أن يقدر على الصوم والإعتاق فتنتقل الكفارة إليهما فيتبين أن الوطء كان حراماً. قوله : (ولو أطعم عن ظهارين ستين فقيراً كل فقير صاعا . صح عن واحد وعن إفطار وظهار صح عنهما) لأنه في الأول زاد في قدر الواجب ونقص عن المحل فلا يجوز إلا بقدر المحل لأن النية في الجنس الواحد لغو وفي الجنسين معتبرة، وكذلك لو أطعم عشرة مساكين عن يمينين لكل مسكين صاعاً فهو على هذا الخلاف؛ كذا في البدائع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الظهاران لامرأتين أو لواحدة والحاصل أن النقصان عن العدد لا يجوز فالواجب في الظهارين إطعام مائة وعشرين فلا يجوز صرف الواجب إلى الأقل كما لو أطعم ثلاثين مسكيناً لكل واحد صاعاً فإنه لا يكفي عن ظهار واحد، والمراد بالمدفوع البر إذ لو كان تمراً أو شعيراً فموضوع المسألة أعطى لكل فقير صاعين ولا بد من تقييد المسألة بأن يكون دفعها دفعة واحدة، أما لو كان بدفعات جاز اتفاقاً كما في الكافي معللاً بأنه في المرة الثانية كمسكين آخر. ورجح في فتح القدير قول محمد بأنه كما يحتاج إلى نية التعيين عند اختلاف الجنس يحتاج إليها لتمييز بعض أشخاص ذلك الجنس وقد اعتبروا ذلك في العتق فإنه لو كان عليه كفارتا ظهار
A boy... and it is restricted by satiation because if among them there is one who is full before eating or is not an adolescent, it does not suffice. The scholars differed on it, and al-Halwani inclined towards non-permissibility. In al-Misbah: 'al-akl' (eating) is known, and 'al-ukul' with two dammas and the second made light is the eaten thing, and 'al-aklah' with fatha is one instance, and with damm is a mouthful. 'Al-ghada' with madd is the morning meal, and 'al-asha' with fatha and madd is the evening meal. 'Al-sahur' with fatha on the seen is what is eaten at the pre-dawn time, and with damm it is the time of eating. He indicated by this that after satiation no consideration is given to the amount of food, such that it is narrated from Abu Hanifa concerning the expiation of an oath: if one presented four loaves to ten poor people and they became full, it suffices even if that does not reach a sa' or half a sa'; thus in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And that condiment (idam) is necessary in barley and corn bread to enable them to reach satiation, unlike wheat bread. And the mashayikh differed on the permissibility of feeding barley bread with condiment, based on the fact that Muhammad explicitly mentioned wheat bread in al-Ziyadat; some said it is not permissible with barley bread, and some permitted it with condiment, and al-Karkhi inclined to that, as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. In al-Yanabi': if one fed 120 poor people in one day one satiating meal, it is not valid except for half of the feeding; if he repeats it on 60 poor people, it suffices. In al-Bada'i': if he bequeathed that expiation be made for him, and the executor fed the specified number the morning meal, then they died before the evening meal, he starts anew and feeds others morning and evening, because there is no way to separate, and the executor is not liable because he did not transgress, as he had no hand in their death. It is fitting that the expiator, if he feeds the number the morning meal and then they disappear, should wait for their presence or repeat the evening meal on a different number, and it is fitting for the executor to wait hoping for their presence. His statement: (And if he gives to a poor person for two months (it is valid)) because the purpose is to fill the need of the needy, and need is renewed with the renewal of days, so the poor person is repeated by the repetition of need as a matter of legal fiction, so it is a legal counting. It is restricted to tamlik (ownership) because if he feeds a poor person his morning meal for sixty days, it does not suffice in the later opinion of Abu Yusuf as in al-Tatarkhaniyya, so one needs to differentiate between ibaha (permission) and tamlik in regard to one person; the correct view is that there is no difference in the madhhab, as in al-Bada'i': if he gives the food of ten poor people in expiation of an oath over ten days to one poor person, feeding him morning and evening for ten days, it suffices in our school. In al-Misbah: 'al-khilla' with fatha is poverty and need. His statement: (And if in one day, it is only for that day) i.e., if he gives a poor person thirty sa' in one day, it does not suffice except for one, because multiplicity is lacking both in reality and by legal fiction, due to the lack of renewal of need. This is absolute and includes whether he gives it in one payment or separately according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. And in food given as ibaha (permission), it is not allowed in one day even if distributed, without dispute as in al-Tatarkhaniyya. And clothing in expiation of an oath is like food, such that if he gives one poor person ten garments in ten days, it is valid in expiation of an oath due to the legal renewal of need as per the renewal of time. In al-Bada'i' concerning expiation of an oath: if he fed one man for twenty mornings or one man for twenty evenings, it suffices in our school. In al-Muhit: if he gives a poor person for the ransom of two days' fast that are obligatory on him, then from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations; in one narration it suffices for both, and in another it does not suffice. It is said: this is the saying of Abu Hanifa as in expiation of an oath. His statement: (And he does not resume by having intercourse with her during the feeding) because Allah only stipulated in emancipation and fasting that it be before the consummation, and He did not stipulate it in feeding, and the unqualified is not restricted to the qualified even if they occur in one incident when they are two different rulings - thus in al-Kafi - except that he is prohibited from intercourse before it because it is possible that he becomes able to fast or emancipate, so the expiation transfers to them, and then it becomes clear that intercourse was forbidden. His statement: (And if he feeds for two zihars sixty poor people each a sa', it is valid for one; and for iftar and zihar, it is valid for both) because in the first he increased the amount of the obligation and decreased the recipients, so it is not valid except for the amount of the recipient because intention in a single type is futile, but in two types it is effective. Similarly, if he feeds ten poor people for two oaths each a sa', it follows this difference; thus in al-Bada'i'. This is absolute and includes whether the two zihars are for two women or one. The result is that deficiency in number is not allowed; the obligatory for two zihars is feeding 120, so it is not allowed to apply the obligation to fewer, such as if he fed 30 poor people each a sa' - it does not suffice for one zihar. What is meant by the given amount is wheat, for if it were dates or barley, then the subject matter would be that he gave each poor person two sa'. It is necessary to restrict the issue to his giving them in one payment; however, if it is in separate payments, it is valid by agreement, as in al-Kafi, with the reasoning that in the second time it is like another poor person. In Fath al-Qadir, the view of Muhammad is preferred that just as he needs the intention of specification when the types differ, he needs it to distinguish some individuals of that type, and they have considered that in manumission: if he owes two expiations for zihar...
Source pages p. 184

Commentary
This passage is a commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explaining various rulings on feeding (it'am) in kaffarah. The author, Ibn Nujaym, discusses multiple issues. First, he addresses the condition of satiation: feeding must cause satiation; if some are already full, it does not count. He then discusses the type of food, noting that barley bread requires condiment (idam) to reach satiation, and there is an ikhtilaf among scholars on this. The relied-upon position is that barley bread with idam is permissible, as al-Karkhi inclined. Next, he discusses feeding 120 poor in one day vs 60 poor over two days, concluding that feeding 120 in one day only counts for half the obligation. He then addresses the case of a bequest for expiation where the recipients die before the evening meal; the executor must start anew. The central ruling concerns giving food to one poor person over multiple days: it is valid in kaffarah because the need is renewed with each day, so legally it is as if multiple poor are fed. However, this applies only when the food is given as tamlik (ownership transfer); in ibaha (mere permission to eat), it does not count for multiple days according to Abu Yusuf's later view, but the correct Hanafi view is that there is no difference. The passage also covers a woman's intercourse during the feeding period of zihar: it is not prohibited before completion of feeding, but it is discouraged because if he later becomes able to fast or emancipate, the expiation changes and the intercourse would have been haram. Finally, he discusses combining two expiation obligations: if one feeds for two zihars but only feeds 60 poor, it counts for only one; but if one expiation is for zihar and another for breaking a fast, feeding 60 poor suffices for both because the types differ and intention is effective. The key principle is that deficiency in the number of recipients is not allowed; the full number (60 for one zihar, 120 for two) must be fed, though combining two different types of expiation in one feeding act is valid with proper intention.

Key Terms
الإطعام (al-it'am): Feeding the poor as expiation for zihar, oath, or breaking fast. It requires giving a specific amount of food (sa' or mudd) to a specific number of poor.
التمليك (al-tamlik): Transfer of ownership of the food to the poor person, as opposed to merely allowing him to eat (ibaha). In kaffarah, tamlik is required for the feeding to count for multiple days.
الإدام (al-idam): Condiment or something eaten with bread to make it palatable, e.g., salt, oil, meat. Required for barley or corn bread to reach satiation.
الشبع (al-shab'): Satiation; the condition that the poor person becomes full from the food given.
الإباحة (al-ibaha): Mere permission to eat without transferring ownership; as opposed to tamlik.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, if a person gives one poor person thirty sa' of wheat over thirty days (one sa' per day) for expiation of thirty oaths, does it suffice?
A) Yes, because the need is renewed daily, so it is like feeding thirty different poor.
B) No, because feeding must be to different poor people each day.
C) Yes, only if the poor person is a different person each day.
D) No, because the food must be given as ownership (tamlik).

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, feeding one poor person over multiple days counts as multiple expiations due to the renewal of need, and this applies whether the food is given as ownership or permission, according to the relied-upon view.

Multiplicity in Expiation Feeding: One Recipient Over Time vs. Multiple Recipients
Explains rules for feeding one poor person over multiple days and multiple poor people at once, with comparisons between expiation types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle of multiplicity (ta'addud haqiqatan wa hukman) to determine the validity of expiation feeding for zihar, missed fasts, and oath breaking.

Core Idea
For zihar and fast expiation, feeding one poor person does not suffice; multiplicity requires multiple recipients per day.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key distinction in Hanafi fiqh regarding expiation feeding. While giving a large amount of food to one poor person might seem sufficient, the law requires actual multiplicity in recipients for certain expiations. For oath expiation, however, giving to the same person over multiple days is acceptable because time renews the need. This lesson will walk you through the reasoning and the intra-madhhab disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their expiation requirements
Determine the required number of recipients for each expiation: zihar and fast expiation require feeding 60 poor people (each one sa'), while oath expiation requires feeding 10 poor people (or clothing/or freeing).
The focus is on the feeding option.
2
Grasp the principle of multiplicity (ta'addud)
Multiplicity can be actual (different individuals) or notional/legal (same individual over different time units, due to renewal of need). Distinguish between ta'addud haqiqatan and ta'addud hukman.
The key is whether the shari'ah requires distinct individuals or allows repetition over time.
3
Apply the principle to zihar and fast expiation
Giving 30 sa' to one poor person in one day does not fulfill the obligation because the act lacks actual multiplicity (60 different people). Even if given over multiple days, it is still lacking as per the correct view (al-Muhit).
The text emphasizes that the need is not renewed in this case.
4
Apply the principle to oath expiation
For oath expiation, giving one poor person 10 garments over 10 days is permissible because the passage of time creates a legal renewal of need (tajaddud al-haja hukman).
This is a distinct ruling based on the nature of oath expiation.
5
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Regarding giving food for two days of fidya (missed fasts) to one poor person: Abu Yusuf has two narrations (one valid, one not). The relied-upon view is that it does not suffice, similar to the zihar ruling.
This disagreement shows the internal ijtihad within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطلاق فصل في الكفارة يوم لا إلا عن يومه ولا يستأنف بوطئها في خلال الإطعام ولو أطعم عن ظهارين ستين فقيراً كل فقير صاعاً صح عن واحد وعن افطار وظهار صح عنهما ولو حرر أي لو أعطى فقيراً ثلاثين صاعاً في يوم لا يجزئه إلا عن واحد لفقد التعدد حقيقة وحكماً لعدم تجدد الحاجة. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا أعطاه بدفعة واحدة أو متفرقاً على الصحيح كما في المحيط. وفي طعام الإباحة لا يجوز في يوم واحد وإن فرق بلا خلاف كما في التتارخانية . والكسوة في كفارة اليمين كالإطعام حتى لو أعطى مسكيناً واحداً عشرة أثواب في عشرة أيام يجوز في كفارة اليمين لتجدد الحاجة حكماً باعتبار تجدد الزمان. وفي البدائع في كفارة اليمين : لو غدى رجلاً واحداً عشرين يوماً أو عشى واحداً عشرين يوماً أجزأه عندنا. وفي المحيط : لو أعطى مسكيناً عن فدية صوم يومين عليه فعن أبي يوسف روايتان؛ وفي رواية يجزئه عنهما، وفي رواية لا يجزئه . قيل: وهذا قول أبي حنيفة كما في كفارة اليمين .
Book of Divorce, Chapter on Expiation. [If he feeds a poor person thirty sa' in one day, it does not suffice except for one day?] And he does not resume by having intercourse with her during the feeding period. If he feeds for two zihars sixty poor people, each poor person one sa', it is valid for one [zihar]. And for a missed fast and a zihar, it is valid for both. If he frees [a slave]... Meaning: if he gives a poor person thirty sa' in one day, it does not suffice except for one, due to lack of multiplicity in reality and in ruling, because the need is not renewed. This is unrestricted, so it includes whether he gave it in one payment or separately according to the correct view as in al-Muhit. As for food that is permissible, it is not allowed in one day even if he distributes it, without disagreement as in al-Tatarakhaniyyah. Clothing in the expiation of an oath is like food, such that if he gave one poor person ten garments in ten days, it is permissible in the expiation of an oath due to the renewal of need in ruling by consideration of the renewal of time. In al-Bada'i' concerning the expiation of an oath: if he fed one man for twenty days [morning and evening?] or fed one man for twenty evenings, it suffices according to us. In al-Muhit: if he gave a poor person for the fidya of two days of fast, then from Abu Yusuf there are two narrations; in one narration it suffices for both, in another it does not suffice. It is said: this is the view of Abu Hanifah as in the expiation of an oath.
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf about the distribution of food in expiation. The author begins by discussing a case where someone gives a large amount of food to a single poor person in one day. For expiation of zihar or breaking a fast, this does not suffice because the requirement is to feed sixty poor people, each one sa'. Giving to one person lacks the multiplicity (ta'addud) in reality and in ruling, as the need is not renewed. The commentary clarifies that this ruling is the same whether the food is given in one go or separately according to the correct view in al-Muhit. For 'permissible food' (perhaps food given as a gift or in a contract), it is not allowed even if distributed. For oath expiation, the rule is different: giving one poor person clothing over multiple days suffices because time creates a notional renewal of need. Al-Bada'i' confirms this for feeding. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: from Abu Yusuf, two narrations about giving food for two days of fidya to one poor person. The passage notes that Abu Hanifah's view aligns with the oath expiation rule. The key principle is that for zihar and fast expiation, the act of feeding must involve multiple recipients in a single day to satisfy the requirement of 'feeding sixty poor people'.

Key Terms
كفارة اليمين (kaffarat al-yamin): Expiation for breaking a sworn oath, which involves feeding ten poor people, clothing them, or freeing a slave.
التعدد حقيقة وحكماً (al-ta'addud haqiqatan wa hukman): Multiplicity in reality (multiple individuals) and in ruling (notional multiplicity through time).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi school, why does giving one poor person thirty sa' of food in one day not fulfill the expiation for zihar?
A) Because the poor person must be fed more than once
B) Because the expiation requires feeding sixty different poor people, and giving to one person lacks multiplicity
C) Because the food must be given over multiple days
D) Because the poor person must be a relative

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, multiplicity of recipients is crucial for zihar and fast expiation; legal multiplicity through time suffices for oath expiation.
