Feeding for Multiple Expiations: Intention and Number of Recipients
Rules on using one act of feeding for multiple expiations and the role of intention

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on feeding for two zihar expiations and identify when intention is required for the act to be valid.

Core Idea
Feeding sixty poor people for two zihars only counts as one; you need 120 recipients unless the expiations are of different types.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rules on fulfilling multiple expiations through a single act of feeding. The key is the number of recipients and the role of intention when the expiation categories are the same or different. We will also see an intra-madhhab disagreement about whether intention of specification is needed for the same category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Read the matn: if a person feeds sixty poor people for two zihars (each requiring sixty), it only counts for one zihar. This is because the obligation is for 120 recipients, and decreasing the number is not permissible.
The same applies whether the two zihars are for one wife or two.
2
Understand the principle of intention
When the expiations are of the same type (jins wahid), intention to fulfill both is futile because the obligation is the same. When they are of different types (e.g., a missed fast and a zihar), intention is effective and both can be fulfilled.
This is why feeding sixty people for a missed fast and a zihar works for both.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that even for the same type, if the individuals (e.g., different wives causing the zihar) are different, intention of specification (niyyat al-ta'yin) is necessary. Other Hanafis may not require it.
The passage cites Fath al-Qadir preferring Muhammad's view.
4
Apply the tarjih
The mufta bihi is that feeding for two zihars only counts for one unless 120 recipients are fed. For different categories, intention is effective. When in doubt, specify intention to avoid deficiency.
This ruling is based on Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ولا يستأنف بوطئها في خلال الإطعام لأن الله تعالى إنما شرط في التحرير والصوم أن يكون قبل التماس ولم يشترطه في الإطعام ولا يحمل المطلق على المقيد وإن وردا في حادثة واحدة بعد أن يكونا حكمين - كذا في الكافي - إلا أنه منع من الوطء قبله لجواز أن يقدر على الصوم والإعتاق فتنتقل الكفارة إليهما فيتبين أن الوطء كان حراماً قوله : (ولو أطعم عن ظهارين ستين فقيراً كل فقير صاعا . صح عن واحد وعن إفطار وظهار صح عنهما) لأنه في الأول زاد في قدر الواجب ونقص عن المحل فلا يجوز إلا بقدر المحل لأن النية في الجنس الواحد لغو وفي الجنسين ،معتبرة ،وكذلك لو أطعم عشرة مساكين عن يمينين لكل مسكين صاعاً فهو على هذا الخلاف؛ كذا في البدائع. أطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان الظهاران لامرأتين أو لواحدة والحاصل أن النقصان عن العدد لا يجوز فالواجب في الظهارين إطعام مائة وعشرين فلا يجوز صرف الواجب إلى الأقل كما لو أطعم ثلاثين مسكيناً لكل واحد صاعاً فإنه لا يكفي عن ظهار واحد، والمراد بالمدفوع البر إذ لو كان تمراً أو شعيراً فموضوع المسألة أعطى لكل فقير صاعين ولا بد من تقييد المسألة بأن يكون دفعها دفعة واحدة، أما لو كان بدفعات جاز اتفاقاً كما في الكافي معللاً بأنه في المرة الثانية كمسكين آخر. ورجح في فتح القدير قول محمد بأنه كما يحتاج إلى نية التعيين عند اختلاف الجنس يحتاج إليها لتمييز بعض أشخاص ذلك الجنس وقد اعتبروا ذلك في العتق فإنه لو كان عليه كفارتا ظهار أنه منع من الوطء قبله الخ قال في الفتح وفيه نظر فإن القدرة حال قيام العجز بالفقر والكبر والمرض الذي لا يرجى زواله أمر موهوم وباعتبار الأمور الموهومة لا تثبت الأحكام ابتداء بل يثبت الاستحباب ،ورعاً، فالأولى الاستدلال بما ذكرنا أول الفصل من النص. قوله : (وقد اعتبروا ذلك في العتق الخ ذكر في العناية الفرق بين مسألتي العتق والإطعام بأن
His statement: 'And he does not resume by having intercourse with her during the feeding period' because Allah only stipulated for emancipation and fasting that they be before physical contact, but He did not stipulate it for feeding, and the unrestricted [text] is not carried to the restricted even if they occur in one incident after being two rulings. As in al-Kafi: except that he is prevented from intercourse before it because it is possible that he will be able to fast and emancipate, so the expiation transfers to them, and then it becomes clear that the intercourse was forbidden. His statement: 'And if he feeds for two zihars sixty poor people, each poor person one sa', it is valid for one. And for a missed fast and a zihar, it is valid for both.' Because in the first, he increased in the amount of the obligation and decreased in the [number of] recipients, so it is not permissible except according to the [number of] recipients, because intention in the same type is futile, and in two types it is considered. Similarly, if he fed ten poor people for two oaths, each poor person one sa', it is subject to this disagreement. As in al-Bada'i'. This is unrestricted, so it includes whether the two zihars were for two women or one. The conclusion is that decrease in number is not permissible. So the obligation for two zihars is feeding one hundred and twenty [poor people]; it is not permissible to divert the obligation to a lesser [number] just as if he fed thirty poor people each one sa', it does not suffice for one zihar. The intended [type of food] is wheat; if it were dates or barley, then the subject of the issue is that he gave each poor person two sa', and it is necessary to restrict the issue to giving them in one go. But if he gave in multiple installments, it is permissible by agreement as in al-Kafi, justified because in the second time it is like another poor person. And he preferred in Fath al-Qadir the view of Muhammad that just as he needs the intention of specification when the types differ, he needs it to distinguish some individuals of that type, and they have considered that in emancipation, for if he owes two zihars... that he was prevented from intercourse before it etc. He said in al-Fath: there is consideration, because ability while inability due to poverty, old age, and incurable illness is a imaginary matter, and by considering imaginary matters, rulings are not established at the beginning, rather recommendation is established out of caution. So it is better to use the proof we mentioned at the beginning of the chapter. His statement: 'And they have considered that in emancipation...' Mentioned in al-'Inayah the difference between the two issues of emancipation and feeding: that
Source pages p. 185

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with an intra-Hanafi dispute about using one act of feeding for multiple expiations. The commentary first addresses the matn statement about not resuming intercourse during the feeding period. The reason is that Allah conditioned emancipation and fasting to be before contact, but not feeding. However, she is prevented from intercourse during feeding because he might become able to fast or emancipate, and then the expiation would transfer, revealing that the intercourse was forbidden. This is a precautionary measure. Then the main ruling: if someone feeds sixty poor people for two zihars (which each require sixty), it only counts for one zihar because he increased the amount per person but decreased the number of recipients. The required number of recipients is 120. For two different expiations (like a missed fast and a zihar), it is valid for both because the categories differ, and intention is effective when categories are different. The commentator notes that this applies whether the zihars are for one woman or two. The key principle: decreasing the number of recipients is not permissible. The food must be wheat; if it were dates or barley, the amount per person would be two sa' instead of one, but the issue is still about number of recipients. If the food is given in installments, it is permissible by agreement because each installment is like a separate charity. Fath al-Qadir prefers Muhammad al-Shaybani's view that intention of specification is needed to distinguish individuals of the same type, just as in emancipation. Then there is a criticism by the commentator (possibly Ibn al-Humam) that the prevention from intercourse is based on an imaginary possibility, which does not establish a prohibition but rather a recommendation. The preferred proof is from the beginning of the chapter. Finally, al-'Inayah mentions the difference between emancipation and feeding.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): Intention to specify which expiation is being fulfilled when multiple are owed.
الجنس الواحد (al-jins al-wahid): The same category of expiation (e.g., two zihars).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man owes two separate zihar expiations and feeds sixty poor people intending both, does it fulfill both?
A) Yes, because intention is valid for both
B) Yes, if he feeds them twice
C) No, because the required number of recipients is 120; it only fulfills one
D) No, because zihar expiation must be fasting

Key Takeaway
Feeding for multiple expiations of the same type requires the full number of recipients (60 per expiation); intention alone cannot merge them, but for different types, intention with a single act suffices.

Freeing Slaves and Feeding for Multiple Zihar Expiations
Ruling on freeing slaves for multiple expiations with an intra-Hanafi debate on notional distribution.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on using a single expiation act (freeing a slave or feeding) to cover multiple zihar violations and explain why intention of distribution is futile in the same category.

Core Idea
One slave covers one zihar; double food quantity cannot replace double recipients.

Zihar expiation requires either freeing a slave or feeding sixty poor. But what if a person incurs multiple zihar violations? Can a single act fulfill two obligations? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the crucial distinction between quantity (qadr) and recipients (mahall), and then opens a debate about whether notional distribution over time can suffice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two expiation acts
The passage discusses two types of expiation for zihar: freeing a slave and feeding sixty poor. For each, we examine whether one act can cover two zihar violations.
2
Distinguish quantity (qadr) from place (mahall)
Quantity refers to the amount of food or the number of slaves. Place (mahall) refers to the recipients – the slaves freed or the poor fed. The same act cannot serve two places simultaneously.
This is the key analytical tool.
3
Apply the rule to freeing a slave
Freeing one slave has both quantity and place matching one zihar. It cannot cover two because each zihar requires its own slave (own place).
Thus, intention to cover two is futile.
4
Apply the rule to feeding sixty poor
Giving 120 sa' of food (double quantity) may seem sufficient for two zihars, but if given to only sixty poor, the place is still sixty – insufficient for two. Thus, it only counts for one.
The total food must be distributed to 120 distinct poor if given in one day.
5
Analyze the debate on notional distribution
The commentator al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah questions why notional distribution (e.g., feeding one poor over 60 days) is not accepted for zihar, given that it suffices for oaths. The preferred view rejects this, requiring actual multiplicity of recipients.
The origin of this discussion is Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
إعتاق الرقبة يصلح كفارة عن أحد الظهارين قدراً ومحلاً فصحت نيته فأما إطعام ستين مسكيناً كل مسكين صاعاً فإن صلح عن الظاهرين قدراً لم يصلح لهما محلاً لأن محلهما مائة وعشرون مسكيناً عند عدم التفريق، فإذا زاد في الوظيفة ونقص عن المحل وجب أن يعتبر قدر المحل احتياطاً كما لو أعطى ثلاثين مسكيناً كل واحد صاعاً .اهـ. قال في الحواشي السعدية فيه بحث فإنه لم لا يكفي التفرق الحكمي بنية التوزيع كما كفى التعدد الحكمي فيما إذا أطعم مسكيناً واحداً ستين يوماً اهـ. وأصل البحث للمحقق ابن الهمام ذكره في الفتح :قوله لأن نية التعيين في الجنس الواحد لغو) قال في العناية : قيل معناه نوى التوزيع في الجنس الواحد فكانت لغواً وإذا لغت صار كأنه أعتق رقبة عن
The emancipation of a slave is valid as expiation for one of the two zihars in quantity and in place, so his intention was valid. But feeding sixty poor people each with one sa', although it is valid for the two [zihars] in quantity, it is not valid for them in place because their place is one hundred and twenty poor people when there is no distribution. So when he increased in the function and decreased in the place, it is necessary to consider the quantity of the place as a precaution, just as if he gave thirty poor people each one sa'. End. And the origin of the discussion is from the researcher Ibn al-Humam; he mentioned it in al-Fath: 'Because the intention of specification in the same type is futile.' He said in al-'Inayah: it is said its meaning is that he intended distribution in the same type, so it was futile, and when it becomes futile, it is as if he freed one slave for...
Source pages p. 186

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with a refined discussion about the difference between freeing slaves and feeding in expiation. The author explains that freeing one slave suffices for one zihar because both quantity and place match. For feeding, giving sixty poor people one sa' each is sufficient in quantity for two zihars (since each needs sixty), but not in place because the place (recipients) for two is 120. Thus, if the number of recipients is less than 120, it only counts for one. The commentator from al-Hawashi al-Sa'diyyah raises a critique: why is notional distribution (giving to one person over multiple days) not sufficient when the intention is to distribute, just as notional multiplicity (time) was sufficient for oath expiation? This echoes the earlier debate. The origin is from Ibn al-Humam in Fath al-Qadir. Then the text quotes al-'Inayah explaining that intention of specification in the same type is futile; if one intends distribution for the same expiation, it is like intending nothing, so it is as if he freed one slave for one expiation.

Key Terms
التفرق الحكمي (al-tafarruq al-hukmi): Notional distribution, e.g., giving to the same poor person over multiple days, considered as separate acts in ruling.
المحل (al-mahall): The recipients of the expiation (the place where the expiation is applied).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
For multiple zihar expiations, a single act of freeing a slave or feeding the poor only fulfills one obligation; the recipient (mahall) must match the number of expiations.

Intention for Multiple Expiations: Same vs Different Types
Explains the ruling on intention for multiple expiations of same vs different types.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on intention when discharging multiple expiations of the same type and distinguish when specification is required for different types.

Core Idea
For expiations of the same type, a single act covers only one obligation; intention to distribute is void (laghw).

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a common scenario: a person owes multiple expiations, such as two dhiar expiations. Is it valid to perform one act intending to cover both? The answer hinges on whether the expiations are of the same 'jins' (type) or different. The Hanafi school draws a clear distinction, and this lesson unpacks the rule, the reasoning, and the internal disagreements among Hanafi imams.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the question
Consider a person who owes two kaffarah for dhiar (same type). They perform a single act of emancipation or fasting intending it to cover both. Is this valid? The text begins by addressing this case.
The key is to determine if the act can satisfy multiple obligations simultaneously.
2
Understand the rule for united type (al-jins al-muttahid)
The text states that if one performs an act that by its nature can cover one unit (like freeing one slave or fasting two months), it only suffices for one expiation. The intention to distribute it across two of the same type is considered 'laghw' (void). The debtor may later assign which expiation it counts for.
This is because the type is united, so specification is unnecessary and the act inherently can only cover one obligation.
3
Distinguish when types are different
If the expiations are of different types (e.g., dhiar and killing), the same act does not suffice for either unless specific intention is made. The text gives the example: freeing one slave for a dhiar and a killing expiation is not valid for either because the types differ.
Different causes (asbab) make the obligations distinct, requiring separate acts or clear assignment.
4
Examine Zufar's objection and the Hanafi response
Zufar argued that distributing a single act across two expiations of the same type should be invalid for both, similar to different types. The Hanafi response relies on istihsan: since the type is united, it is analogous to fasting two months for two dhiars—no specification needed.
The majority view (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) holds that the act is valid for one, and the debtor chooses later.
5
Analyze the internal dispute on conflicting intentions (Abu Yusuf vs Muhammad)
The passage then expands to cases where a person intends both an obligatory and voluntary act simultaneously (e.g., dhuhr and nafl prayer, qada and voluntary fast). Abu Yusuf says the stronger (obligatory) prevails; Muhammad says both are invalid, and the act becomes voluntary (or invalid for salah).
This dispute shows how the principle of intention interacts with different types of worship, and the relied-upon position is often the one that best preserves the obligation.

Source Text

Book of Divorce, Chapter on Expiation. Two slaves for two dhiars without specifying, and similarly fasting and feeding. If he emancipates one slave or fasts two months, it is valid for one, but for a dhiar and a killing it is not. For twenty poor people (?) Unity of type? For two women, he emancipates a slave intending one of them, his specification is valid and not void, and it is permissible for him to have intercourse with the one he specified. If he emancipates a disbelieving slave for a dhiar and a killing, it is for the dhiar even though the type differs, because a disbelieving slave is not suitable for the expiation of killing. In al-Bada'i, he made a good analogy: the case of marrying a woman and her daughter or sister together; if both are free, the contract for each is invalid; if one is married, the contract for the free one is valid. The principle is that what differs in cause is different, and what has a unified cause is united. All prayers are of the different type, even two dhuhr prayers from two days; fasting the days of Ramadan is of the united type if in one year, but if from two years, it is of the different type. If he intends dhuhr or asr or funeral prayer, he has not started any of them due to contradiction and lack of preponderance. If he intends dhuhr and supererogatory prayer, he has not started at all according to Muhammad due to contradiction; according to Abu Yusuf, it occurs as obligatory because it is stronger. If he intends make-up fasting and supererogatory, or zakat and voluntary, or vowed hajj and voluntary, it becomes voluntary according to Muhammad because both are invalidated by contradiction, so it turns to voluntary; from Abu Yusuf, it occurs as the stronger, giving preponderance in case of contradiction. If he intends obligatory hajj and voluntary, it is definitely the obligatory due to its strength according to the second view, or because the intention becomes void by contradiction and the obligation is fulfilled by the absolute intention. Commentary
This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, discusses the ruling on multiple expiations (kaffarat) and the effect of intention (niyyah) when discharging them. The author explains that when two expiations are of the same type (e.g., both from dhiar), performing an act that suffices for both (such as emancipating two slaves) without specifying which is for which is valid. This is because the 'jins' (type) is unified, so there is no need to specify individual obligations. However, if the act is a single unit (like freeing one slave or fasting two months) intended for two expiations, it only counts for one, because the single act cannot cover multiple obligations of the same type. The discussion then extends to cases where expiations are of different types (e.g., dhiar and killing), where specification becomes necessary for validity. The text compares this to other acts of worship like prayers, fasting, zakat, and hajj, and presents the disagreements between Imam Muhammad and Imam Abu Yusuf on whether the stronger obligation prevails or both are invalidated. The author concludes by clarifying that the phrase 'intention of specification in a united type is void' means intending to distribute the act across multiple obligations, not specifying a particular one. This resolution addresses an objection raised in Fath al-Qadir.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyah al-ta'yin): The intention to specify which particular obligation (e.g., which dhiar expiation) the act is meant to fulfill.
الجنس المتحد (al-jins al-muttahid): A category of obligations that share the same nature and ruling, such as multiple expiations for dhiar (all requiring the same action).
لغو (laghw): Void, having no legal effect. Here, the intention to distribute one act across multiple obligations of the same type is considered laghw.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If someone owes two kaffarah for dhiar (from two wives) and he emancipates one slave intending both, what is the ruling according to the relied-upon Hanafi position?
A) The emancipation is invalid for both.
B) It is valid for one, and he may choose which dhiar it applies to.
C) It is valid for both because the type is united.
D) It is valid only if he specifies the wife's name.

Key Takeaway
For expiations of the same type, a single unit act covers only one; intention to distribute is void, and the debtor may later assign which obligation it fulfills.

Intention for Multiple Expiation Acts
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intention for multiple expiations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule on intention (niyyah) when performing a single act for multiple expiations of the same genus, and distinguish the positions of Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Core Idea
A single act suffices for multiple expiations if they share the same genus, by istihsan.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq delves into a nuanced issue within Hanafi fiqh: when a person owes multiple expiations (kaffarat) of different causes but similar form, can one act fulfill them all? The author navigates between strict qiyas and istihsan, citing positions of key Hanafi imams and resolving a potential contradiction with a clarification from al-Nihayah.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
The Hanafi position held by the majority is that intention to specify (niyyat al-ta'yin) is futile when the expiations are of the same genus (jins muttahid). Thus, one act can fulfill multiple expiations of the same type.
This is based on istihsan, overriding Zufar's strict qiyas.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Compare the views of Zufar (invalid), Abu Yusuf (stronger obligation prevails), and Muhammad (depends on whether the act can be performed with absolute intention).
The author ultimately favors the view that specification in the same genus is futile, following Qadikhan and al-Zayla'i.
3
Apply the rule to different categories
If both intentions are for obligatory acts, it is invalid by agreement. If one is obligatory and one supererogatory, Abu Yusuf holds the stronger prevails; Muhammad restricts this to acts that can be performed with absolute intention (like fasting/Hajj).
For acts requiring specification (like prayer), Muhammad's view leads to invalidity.
4
Examine the exception for prayer
Prayer requires specification due to the obligation of sequential order (tartib). Hence, intending multiple prayers in one act is invalid, unlike expiation where order is not required.
If order falls away due to many missed prayers, a general intention suffices.
5
Resolve the objection regarding specifying individuals
The clarification from al-Nihayah states that futile specification means trying to specify multiple individuals of the same genus at once; specifying one particular individual is valid.
This aligns with the mufta bihi view and repels the objection from Fath al-Qadir.

Source Text

كتاب الطلاق فصل في الكفارة

عن إحداهن وأطعم عن أخرى وكسا عن أخرى أو أعتق عنها عبداً ولا ينوي كل واحدة بعينها جاز استحساناً خلافاً لزفر نظراً إلى أنهما مختلفان ونحن نقول: الجنس متحد فهو كالصوم بخلاف صلاة الظهر لأن نية التعيين ثمة لم تشترط باعتبار أن الواجب مختلف متعدد بل باعتبار أن مراعاة الترتيب واجبة عليه ولا يمكنه مراعاة الترتيب إلا بنية التعيين حتى لو سقط الترتيب بكثرة الفوائت تكفيه نية الظهر لا غير كذا في المحيط وهو تفصيل حسن في الصلوات ينبغي حفظه .

والحاصل أنه إذا نوى شيئين فإن كانا فرضين لم يصح اتفاقاً، وإن كان أحدهما فرضاً والآخر نفلاً فعند أبي يوسف يقع عن الأقوى، سواء كان الأقوى يتأدى بمطلق النية كالصوم والحج أو لا كالصلاة وعند محمد في الأول يقع عن الفرض لأنه لما بطلت النيتان للتعارض بقي مطلق النية وفي الثاني لم يصح. وفي فتح القدير : ومما يعكر على الأصل الممهد ما أبي يوسف في المنتقى : لو تصدق عن يمين وظهار فله أن يجعله. أحدهما استحساناً وقدمنا في باب شروط الصلاة مسائل من هذا النوع فارجع إليه. وقولهم هنا لو نوى ظهراً وعصراً وصلاة جنازة بواو العطف في صلاة الجنازة لأنها لو كانت بـ ( أو ) لم يصح لأنهم قالوا : لو نوى ظهراً أو صلاة جنازة كان عن الظهر كما قدمناه ثم اعلم أن قولهم إن نية التعيين في الجنس الواحد لغو يرد عليه ما لو كان عليه كفارتا ظهار لامرأتين فأعتق عبداً . صح التعيين وله أن يطأ التي كفر عنها دون الأخرى ولم يجب عنه في فتح القدير وهو بناء على ما فهمه من ظاهر العبارة أن المراد أن نية تعيين بعض الأفراد في الجنس المتحد لغو، وقد قرر المراد في النهاية بما يدفع الإيراء فقال : أراد به تعميم الجنس بالنية ألا ترى أنه إذا عين ظهار إحداهما للتكفير صح وحل له قربانها كذا في الفوائد الظهيرية. والله أعلم.

عن إحداهما الظهارين ولم ينو عنهما وذلك جائز، وله أن يصرفها إلى أيهما شاء فكذلك ها هنا بخلاف ما إذا كانت الكفارتان من جنسين مختلفين لأنه نوى التوزيع في الجنس المختلف فكانت معتبرة فلا يكون عن واحد منهما قوله : (وهو تفصيل حسن الخ قال الزيلعي في مسائل شتى آخر الكتاب بعد نقله كلام المحيط : وهذا مشكل وما ذكره أصحابنا مثل قاضيخان وغيره خلاف ذلك وهو المعتمد لما ذكرنا من المعنى أي من أن التعيين في الجنس الواحد لغو الخ . قال : ولأن الأمر لو كان كما قاله . المحيط لجاز مع وجوب الترتيب أيضاً لإمكان صرفه إلى الأول إذ لا يجب التعيين عند الترتيب ولا يفيد اهـ .

في قوله : (وقد قرر المراد في النهاية الخ ومثله في الكفاية. وحاصله أن المراد بالتعيين اللغو تعيين جميع أفراد الجنس لا فرد خاص وهذا معنى ما قدمناه عن العناية من تفسيره بالتوزيع، وبهذا التقرير يندفع ما رجح به في الفتح قول محمد رحمه الله في المسألة المارة .
Book of Divorce, Section on Expiation. ... (He said) If he feeds one of them and feeds another and clothes another, or frees a slave for her and does not intend each one specifically, it is permissible by istihsan, contrary to Zufar, who considers that they are different. We say: the genus is unified, so it is like fasting, unlike the Zuhr prayer because the intention of specification there is not required because the duty is different and multiple, but rather because observing order is obligatory upon him and he cannot observe order except by intention of specification; so if order falls due to many missed prayers, the intention of Zuhr alone suffices. This is a good detail in prayers that should be memorized. The summary is: if he intends two things, if both are obligatory, it is invalid by agreement; if one is obligatory and the other supererogatory, according to Abu Yusuf it falls for the stronger, whether the stronger is fulfilled by absolute intention like fasting and Hajj or not like prayer; according to Muhammad, in the first case it falls for the obligatory because when the two intentions are invalid due to conflict, absolute intention remains, and in the second case it is not valid. In Fath al-Qadir: Among things that disturb the laid foundation is what Abu Yusuf narrated in al-Muntaqa: if he gives charity for an oath and zihar, he may make it for one of them by istihsan. We have presented in the chapter on conditions of prayer issues of this type, so refer to it. Their statement here: if he intended Zuhr and Asr and Janazah prayer with the conjunction 'waw' in Janazah prayer because if it were with 'aw' it would not be valid, because they said: if he intended Zuhr or Janazah, it would be for Zuhr as we presented. Then know that their statement that the intention of specification in a single genus is futile is objected to by the case where he owes two zihar expiations for two women and frees a slave; specification is valid and he may have intercourse with the one for whom he expiated but not the other. This was not answered in Fath al-Qadir, and it is based on his understanding from the apparent wording that the meaning is that intending some individuals in a unified genus is futile. The intended meaning has been clarified in al-Nihayah in a way that repels the objection: he said, 'He intended to generalize the genus with the intention; do you not see that if he specifies the zihar of one of them for expiation, it is valid and intercourse with her becomes permissible?' So in al-Fawa'id al-Zahiriyyah. And Allah knows best. Regarding the two zihars, he did not intend for them both, and that is permissible; he may allocate it to whichever he wishes, similarly here, unlike the case where the two expiations are of different kinds because he intended distribution in the different genus, so it is considered and thus it is not for either of them. His statement: 'This is a good detail...' al-Zayla'i said in different issues at the end of the book after quoting the discourse of al-Muhit: This is problematic, and what our companions like Qadikhan and others mentioned is contrary to it, and it is the relied upon view due to the meaning we mentioned, i.e., that specification in a single genus is futile. He said: Because if the matter were as al-Muhit said, it would be permissible even with the necessity of order, because it is possible to allocate it to the first since specification is not required when order exists, and it does not benefit. In his statement: 'And the intended meaning has been clarified in al-Nihayah...' and similarly in al-Kifayah. The summary is that the intended futile specification is specifying all individuals of the genus, not a particular individual, and this is the meaning of what we presented from al-Inayah by interpreting it as distribution. By this clarification, what was preferred in Fath al-Qadir regarding Muhammad's view in the passing issue is repelled.
Source pages p. 187

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of intention when expiating multiple kaffarat (expiation acts) simultaneously. The author discusses the positions of Zufar, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad. Zufar held that if one does a single act (e.g., feeding or freeing a slave) for two different types of expiation without separate intentions, it is invalid. But the author, following istihsan, says it is valid if the expiations are of the same genus, like two types of kaffarah that both involve feeding or freeing. The analogy is drawn to fasting: if one owes two consecutive months of fasting for two different reasons, one fast suffices for both because the genus is one. The distinction from prayer is explained: in prayer, the obligation of sequential order requires specifying which prayer you are making up; thus intending multiple prayers in one act fails. However, if the order falls away due to many missed prayers, a general intention of Zuhr suffices. When one intention is for an obligation and another for a supererogatory act, Abu Yusuf says the stronger (obligation) prevails; Muhammad says only if the stronger can be performed with absolute intention (like fasting/Hajj) does it fall for the obligation, otherwise not. The response to an objection: if one owes two zihar expiations for two different wives and frees a slave without specifying, it is permissible and he can later assign it to either, because the genus is one. But if the expiations are of different types (like feeding vs. freeing), then distributing intention fails, and the act is not valid for either. The author then notes that the clarification in al-Nihayah resolves the confusion: futile specification means trying to specify multiple individuals of the same genus at once; specifying one particular individual of that genus is valid. This aligns with the view that Muhammad's position is not upheld.

Key Terms
نية التعيين (niyyat al-ta'yin): The intention to specify which particular obligation one is fulfilling with the act.
استحسان (istihsan): A juristic preference that overrides strict qiyas in favor of ease or custom, used to validate the single act for multiple expiations.
جنس متحد (jins muttahid): A single genus; that the legal acts share the same category, e.g., both involve feeding or freeing a slave, even if from different causes.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a person intends both a fard (obligatory) act and a nafil (supererogatory) act, what is the ruling according to Muhammad?
A) The fard always suffices.
B) Both are invalid.
C) The fard suffices only if the fard can be performed with absolute intention.
D) The nafil suffices.

Key Takeaway
One act can fulfill multiple expiations of the same genus by istihsan, but not if they are of different types, and not for prayers due to order requirements.

Definition and Basis of Li'an
Introducing the chapter on li'an with linguistic definition and Quranic proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definition of li'an and identify the Quranic verses that establish it as a substitute for hadd al-qadhf.

Core Idea
Li'an is a sworn testimony procedure that replaces the hadd penalty for a husband who accuses his wife without witnesses.

This lesson opens the chapter on li'an (mutual imprecation), a unique procedure in Islamic family law. You will discover that li'an is not a divorce but a testimonial mechanism grounded directly in the Quran. By examining the linguistic root and the revealed verses, you will understand how it averts the fixed punishment for slander (hadd al-qadhf) when a husband has no witnesses.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its legal purpose
Locate in the passage the definition of li'an. What is it? What does it replace? The text says it 'stands in place of the hadd penalty for qadhf' for the husband.
Note that the definition uses 'shahadat' (testimonies), emphasizing testimony, not punishment.
2
Locate the primary dalil
Find the Quranic verses cited. They are from Surah al-Nur, verses 6-10. Read them carefully to see the prescribed oaths.
These verses are the main proof (dalil) and are considered qat'i (definitive) in transmission and meaning.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How do these verses prove the li'an procedure? Look at the structure: the husband swears four times and a fifth curse; the wife swears four times and a fifth invocation of wrath. This detailed description mandates the procedure as an alternative to hadd.
The imperative form and detailed steps indicate obligation (wujub) of following this procedure.
4
Examine the sabab al-nuzul
The passage includes two incidents: Hilal ibn Umayyah and 'Uwaymir. Understand how these historical contexts explain why the verses were revealed: to avoid the hadd when a husband has strong suspicion but no evidence.
These hadiths illustrate the practical need for li'an and confirm the Prophet's practice.
5
Assess the authority weight
Since the dalil is the Quran (mutawatir), the authority is zahir al-riwayah. The procedure is undisputed among all schools (muttafaq alayh) in its basic form.
Later details may have ikhtilaf, but the core is firmly established.

باب اللعان

هي شهادات مؤكدات بالإيمان مقرونة باللعن قائمة مقام حد القذف في حقه مصدر
باب اللعان
لا ملاعنة ولعاناً. يقال لا عن امرأته ملاعنة ولعاناً وتلاعناً. والتعنا لعن عن بعض بعضاً، ولا عن الحاكم بينهما لعاناً ،حكم، والتلعين التعذيب، ولعنه كجعله طرده وأبعده فهو لعين وملعون والجمع ملاعين والاسم اللعان واللعانية. واللعن بالضم من يلعنه الناس، واللعنة كهمزة الكثير اللعن لهم، واللعين من يلعنه كل واحد كالملعن والشيطان والممسوخ والمشؤم والمسيب وما يتخذ في المزارع كهيئة الرجل والمنخري المهلك؛ كذا في القاموس والأصل فيه الآيات التي في سورة النور وهو قوله تعالى والذين يرمون أزواجهم ولم يكن لهم شهداء إلا أنفسهم فشهادة أحدهم أربع شهادات بالله إنه لمن الصادقين والخامسة أن لعنت الله عليه إن كان من الكاذبين ويدرؤوا عنها العذاب أن تشهد أربع شهادات بالله إنه لمن الكاذبين والخامسة أن غضب الله عليها إن كان من الصادقين ولولا فضل الله عليكم ورحمته وأن الله تواب حكيم [النور: ٦ - ١٠] وقد اختلف في سبب نزولها فروى البخاري عن ابن عباس رضي الله عنهما أن هلال بن أمية قذف امرأته عند رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بشريك ابن سحماء فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : البيئة وإلا حدّ في ظهرك. فقال : يا رسول الله إذا رأى أحدنا على امرأته رجلاً ينطلق يلتمس البينة فجعل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : البينة وإلا حد في ظهرك . فقال هلال والذي بعثك بالحق إني لصادق ولينزلن الله تعالى ما يبرىء ظهري من الحد . فنزل جبريل فأنزل الله والذين يرمون أزواجهم حتى بلغ إن كان من الصادقين فانصرف النبي له فأرسل إليهما فجاء هلال فشهد والنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول: الله يعلم أن أحدكما كاذب فهل منكما تائب. ثم قامت فشهدت فلما كانت عند الخامسة وعظها وقال إنها موجبة فتلكأت ونكصت حتى ظننا أنها ترجع ثم قالت لا أفضح قومي سائر اليوم فمضت فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : أبصروها فإن جاءت به أكحل العينين شائع الأليتين خدلج الساقين فهو لشريك ابن سحماء فجاءت به كذلك فقال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم : لولا ما مضى من كتاب الله تعالى لكان لي ولها شأن في المصباح : خدلج أي ضخم. وأخرج البخاري أيضاً عن سهل بن سعد قال : جاء عويمر إلى عاصم بن عدي فقال : سل رسول الله أرأيت رجلاً وجد امرأته رجلاً مع فقتله أيقتل به أم كيف يصنع ؟ فسأل عاصم رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فعاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فلقيه عويمر
باب اللعان
قوله : (وتفرع على هذا الشرط أي كونها ممن يحد قاذفها. وقوله لو قذفها أي بنفي الولد كما هو في التتارخانية. وقوله فادعى الولد الأول كذا في التتارخانية وفي بعض النسخ الأول «الولد»
Chapter of Li'an

They are testimonies strengthened by oaths, coupled with curses, standing in place of the hadd penalty for qadhf in his right. Source: Bab al-Li'an. It is said: he performed li'an with his wife (la'ana), li'an and tala'un. They cursed each other, and the judge performed li'an between them. At-ta'lin is torture. La'anahu: he drove him away, banished him, so he is la'in and mal'un, plural mala'in. The noun is li'an and la'aniyyah. Al-la'n (with damma) is the one whom people curse. Al-la'nah (like humzah) is the one who curses much. Al-la'in is the one whom everyone curses, like al-mul'an, the devil, the deformed, the wretched, the disgraced, and what is taken in farms like the figure of a man, and al-munkhuri al-muhlik. This is in al-Qamus. The basis for it is the verses in Surah al-Nur, which is His saying: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves – then the testimony of one of them (shall be) four testimonies by Allah that indeed he is of the truthful, and the fifth that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is of the liars. And it will avert the punishment from her if she testifies four testimonies by Allah that indeed he is of the liars, and the fifth that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he was of the truthful.' (Quran 24:6-10). There is difference of opinion about the cause of its revelation. Al-Bukhari narrated from Ibn Abbas that Hilal ibn Umayyah accused his wife before the Prophet of (committing adultery with) Sharik ibn Sahma'. The Prophet said: 'The evidence, or else the hadd on your back.' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, if one of us sees a man with his wife, should he go looking for evidence?' The Prophet kept saying: 'The evidence, or else the hadd on your back.' Hilal said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth, I am truthful, and Allah will certainly send down something to clear my back from the hadd.' Then Jibril came down and revealed (the verses) until 'if he is of the truthful'. The Prophet left and sent for them. Hilal came and testified, while the Prophet said: 'Allah knows that one of you is lying; is there any of you who repents?' Then she stood and testified. When it was the fifth, he admonished her and said that it is binding. She hesitated and recoiled until we thought she would recant. Then she said, 'I will not disgrace my people for the rest of the day,' and went ahead. The Prophet said: 'Look at her; if she gives birth to a child with black eyes, large buttocks, and thick calves, then he is for Sharik ibn Sahma'.' She gave birth to such a child. The Prophet said: 'Had it not been for the Book of Allah, I would have had an affair with her.' In al-Misbah: khudluj means thick. Al-Bukhari also narrated from Sahl ibn Sa'd: 'Uwaymir came to 'Asim ibn 'Adi and said: 'Ask the Messenger of Allah: if a man finds his wife with another man and kills him, should he be killed for him or what should he do?' 'Asim asked the Messenger of Allah, and the Messenger of Allah disapproved of the question. Then 'Uwaymir met him... Chapter of Li'an: His statement: 'And this condition branches off' – i.e., that she is one whose accuser would be flogged (for qadhf). And his statement: 'if he accuses her' – i.e., by denying the child, as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah. And his statement: 'and he claimed the first child' – as in al-Tatarkhaniyyah; in some copies 'the child'.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage introduces the chapter on li'an (mutual imprecation). It begins with a linguistic definition: li'an is a series of sworn testimonies strengthened by oaths and curses, which substitute for the hadd penalty of slander (qadhf) when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses. The author then cites the Quranic basis from Surah al-Nur (24:6-10), which prescribes the procedure: the husband swears four times that he is truthful, and the fifth time invokes a curse on himself if he lies; the wife swears four times that he is lying, and the fifth time invokes Allah's wrath on herself if he is truthful. This averts the hadd punishment from the husband and the punishment for the wife (stoning) if she completes the oath. The passage then narrates the historical causes of revelation: the case of Hilal ibn Umayyah, who accused his wife of adultery with Sharik ibn Sahma'. The Prophet demanded evidence, but Allah revealed the li'an verses instead. Also the incident of 'Uwaymir, who asked about a husband finding a man with his wife. The chapter then continues with a commentary on conditions (though the OCR cuts off). The key point is that li'an is a special procedure that replaces the normal proof requirement for slander in marriage, allowing the husband to avoid the hadd punishment by swearing.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): A set of sworn testimonies between spouses when the husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses, replacing the hadd punishment.
قذف (qadhf): The crime of falsely accusing a married person of adultery, which carries a hadd penalty of 80 lashes.
حد القذف (hadd al-qadhf): The fixed corporal punishment for unlawful accusation of adultery.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Li'an is a Quranically mandated procedure of sworn testimony that spares the husband from the hadd penalty for slander when he lacks witnesses against his wife.

Definition and Proof of Li'an
Definition and proof of li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define li'an and cite its primary Quranic evidence (Surah An-Nur 6-10) as proof.

Core Idea
Li'an substitutes the hadd penalty when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses.

Li'an is a unique legal institution in Islamic law, resolving spousal accusations of adultery without requiring four witnesses. This lesson establishes its definition and the Quranic basis, showing how the procedure of mutual oaths and imprecations replaces the hadd penalty. We will also examine the prophetic context that confirms this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Define li'an linguistically and legally.
Read the opening lines of the passage for the linguistic root and the legal definition: 'testimonies emphasized by oaths, coupled with cursing, standing in place of the hadd penalty for qadhf.' Understand that li'an is a substitute for the husband's hadd.
The term comes from 'la'n' meaning curse; the mutual cursing is the core.
2
Identify the Quranic proof.
Locate the verses of Surah An-Nur (6-10) in the passage. Note that these verses are the primary dalil. The passage quotes them verbatim.
The verses prescribe the exact procedure: four oaths from the husband and a fifth invoking the curse, and similarly for the wife with the wrath of Allah.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah.
Analyze how the Quranic text indicates the ruling. The imperative 'fashahadatu' (then his testimony) shows obligation. The structure of the verses mandates the procedure, establishing li'an as a legal institution.
The dalala is zanni because the imperative could be interpreted as guidance rather than obligation, but Hanafi usul treats it as wajib.
4
Confirm with Sunnah context.
Read the hadith of Hilal ibn Umayyah and Uwaymir. These reports show the practical application and confirm that li'an was revealed in response to real scenarios. The Prophet performed li'an between the couples and established the separation.
These hadith also clarify that after li'an, the couple cannot remain together and the child follows the mother.

Chapter of Li'an. It is testimonies emphasized by oaths, coupled with cursing, standing in place of the hadd penalty for slander (qadhf) in his right. Source: Chapter of Li'an. It is said: he performed li'an with his wife, li'an and li'an, and they performed li'an. And the two performed li'an, each cursing the other. And the ruler performed li'an between them as a ruling. And al-tal'een is punishment. And la'anahu: he banished and distanced him, so he is la'een and mal'un, plural mala'een, noun al-li'an and al-la'aniyyah. And al-la'n (with damm): one whom people curse. And al-la'nah (like humzah): one who curses them a lot. And al-la'een: one whom everyone curses, like the devil, the deformed, the ominous, the left alone, and what is taken in fields like a scarecrow and the hollow ruin; thus in al-Qamus. The basis for it is the verses in Surah al-Nur: 'And those who accuse their wives and have no witnesses except themselves - then the witness of one of them [shall be] four testimonies by Allah that he is of the truthful, And the fifth [oath] that the curse of Allah be upon him if he is of the liars. And it will prevent the punishment from her if she gives four testimonies by Allah that he is of the liars, And the fifth [oath] that the wrath of Allah be upon her if he was of the truthful. And if not for the favor of Allah upon you and His mercy... and Allah is Accepting of repentance, Wise.' [An-Nur 6-10]. And there is disagreement regarding the reason for their revelation. Al-Bukhari narrated from Ibn 'Abbas that Hilal ibn Umayyah accused his wife before the Messenger of Allah of (committing adultery with) Sharik ibn Sahma'. The Prophet said: 'Evidence, or the hadd on your back.' He said: 'O Messenger of Allah, if one of us sees a man with his wife, should he go seeking evidence?' The Prophet kept saying: 'Evidence, or the hadd on your back.' Hilal said: 'By Him who sent you with the truth, I am truthful, and Allah will send down what will clear my back from the hadd.' Then Jibril descended and revealed: 'And those who accuse their wives...' until 'if he is of the liars.' The Prophet left and sent for them. Hilal came and testified while the Prophet said: 'Allah knows that one of you is lying, so is there any repentant among you?' Then she stood and testified. When it came to the fifth (oath), he admonished her and said: 'It is binding.' She hesitated and drew back until we thought she would recant, then she said: 'I will not disgrace my people for the rest of the day,' and went ahead. The Prophet said: 'Look at her; if she gives birth to a child with black-lined eyes, wide buttocks, and thick calves, then it belongs to Sharik ibn Sahma'.' She gave birth to a child like that. The Prophet said: 'Were it not for what has passed of the Book of Allah, I would have had an affair with her.' In al-Misbah: 'khadlij' means bulky. And al-Bukhari also narrated from Sahl ibn Sa'd: 'Uwaymir came to 'Asim ibn 'Adi and said: 'Ask the Messenger of Allah: If a man finds his wife with another man and kills him, should he be killed for it, or what should he do?' 'Asim asked the Messenger of Allah, and the Messenger of Allah disapproved of the question. 'Uwaymir met him and said: 'What have you done? You did not bring good; you asked the Messenger of Allah and he disapproved of the questioner.' 'Uwaymir said: 'By Allah, I will go to the Messenger of Allah and ask him.' He went and found that revelation had been sent down to him. He called for her and performed li'an between them. 'Uwaymir said: 'O Messenger of Allah, if I keep her, I would have lied about her.' So he separated from her before the Prophet ordered him. That became the sunnah for the two who perform li'an. The Messenger of Allah said: 'Look at her; if she gives birth to a child with dark eyes and large buttocks, then I think he (Uwaymir) has spoken the truth; and if she gives birth to a child like a reddish lizard, then I think he is a liar.' She gave birth to a child like the disliked description. And al-Biqa'i mentioned that it is not impossible for a single verse to have multiple causes together or separately. The full accounts with their different chains are in al-Durr al-Manthur by al-Jalal al-Suyuti.
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is a definition and proof for the law of li'an (mutual cursing) in Hanafi fiqh. The author begins by defining li'an linguistically and then presents its basis in the Quran (Surah An-Nur 6-10) and Sunnah (the hadiths of Hilal ibn Umayyah and Uwaymir). The Quranic verses explicitly prescribe the procedure when a husband accuses his wife of adultery without witnesses: the husband swears four oaths that he is truthful, and the fifth oath invokes the curse of Allah if he is lying; the wife then swears four oaths that he is lying, and the fifth invokes Allah's wrath. The hadiths provide the practical context for the revelation: Hilal ibn Umayyah accused his wife, and the Prophet initially demanded evidence or the hadd penalty, but revelation then established li'an. Similarly, the story of Uwaymir shows that after li'an, the couple cannot remain together, and the child's paternity follows the mother. The author notes that the same verse may have multiple occasions of revelation, as both Hilal and Uwaymir are sound reports. The passage firmly establishes li'an as a divinely ordained institution that replaces the hadd penalty for the husband and protects the wife from punishment.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual cursing between spouses in a specific procedure of oaths and imprecations to resolve a defamation charge without witnesses.
قذف (qadhf): Accusation of adultery or illegitimate birth; its hadd penalty is 80 lashes.

Li'an: Definition, Conditions, and Legal Effects
Expands on pillars, conditions, and legal consequences of li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define li'an, state its pillar (rukn), identify the condition of ahliyyat al-shahada required for both spouses, and explain its legal effects including the prohibition of intercourse and resulting irrevocable separation.

Core Idea
Li'an substitutes for hadd penalties and requires spouses to be competent witnesses, not mere oath-takers.

Li'an is a unique procedure in Islamic law that allows a husband to avoid the hadd penalty for false accusation (qadhf) when he accuses his wife of zina without witnesses. This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq expands on the definition of li'an, the conditions for its validity, and its legal consequences. Understanding li'an requires careful attention to the Hanafi distinction between competence for testimony versus mere oath-taking, and the specific effects that follow its completion.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Pillar (Rukn) of Li'an
Locate the phrase 'شهادات مؤكدات بالأيمان مقرونة باللعن' and explain why the author calls this the pillar. Understand that the four oaths (shahadat) from each spouse are the core components.
The pillar is the testimonies (shahadat) themselves, emphasized by oaths and coupled with cursing.
2
Determine the Required Competence
Notice that the author states 'فدل على اشتراط أهليتهما للشهادة' — this establishes that both spouses must possess ahliyyat al-shahada (competence for testimony). Contrast this with the Shafi'i view of merely requiring competence for oaths.
Hanafi conditions for witnesses: Islam, adulthood, sanity, probity.
3
Analyze the Substitution for Hadd
Examine how li'an stands in place of the hadd for qadhf (for the husband) and the hadd for zina (for the wife). The text clarifies that this substitution is not absolute but specific to each case.
If absolute, the husband's testimony would be permanently rejected — which is not the case.
4
Trace the Legal Effects
List the effects mentioned: prohibition of intercourse after mutual cursing even before separation, mandatory separation, and the resulting ba'in divorce. Also note that li'an cannot be pardoned or settled for money, like hadd penalties.
Delegation (tawkil) is only allowed for establishing li'an, according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
5
Apply the Condition to Multiple Wives
Understand the rule: if a man accuses multiple wives with one statement, he must perform separate li'an for each. If he is not eligible for li'an, one hadd suffices for all due to overlap.
The purpose of repelling disgrace is not achieved with a single li'an for multiple wives.

Chapter of Li'an. His saying: (And derived from this condition) i.e., that she be one whose accuser would be subject to hadd. And his saying: 'If he accuses her' i.e., by denial of lineage as in al-Tatarakhaniyyah. And his saying: 'And he claims the first child' - thus in al-Tatarakhaniyyah, and in some copies: 'the child'. His saying: 'It is testimonies emphasized by oaths, coupled with cursing, standing in place of the hadd for qadhf in his right and the hadd for zina in her right.' This is an explanation of the pillar, so it indicates the condition of competence for testimony in each right, not competence for oath as al-Shafi'i held. And it indicates that if they perform li'an before a judge and he does not separate them until he dies or is removed, then the successor repeats the li'an, just as if they testified before him and he died or was removed before judgment; thus in al-Bada'i'. And the meaning of it standing in place of the hadd for qadhf in his right is that it is with respect to her specifically, not absolutely, because if it were absolute, his testimony would never be accepted, whereas it is accepted as the commentator mentioned in the chapter on qadhf. And in al-Ikhtiyar, his testimony is never accepted after li'an. And if he accuses with one word or with words four of his wives of zina, one li'an is not sufficient for all of them; rather, he must perform li'an for each one separately, unlike if he accuses her repeatedly, where one li'an is required, just as if he accuses a foreign woman repeatedly or foreign women with one word or words, one hadd is required, because the purpose is achieved, which is repelling disgrace from them, and that is not achieved in li'an except with respect to each one individually. And if he accuses them and is not among those eligible for li'an, one hadd suffices for all due to overlap; thus in al-Bada'i'. And the meaning of it standing in place of the hadd for zina in her right is that it is with respect to the husband. Li'an is not established by testimony upon testimony, nor by a judge's letter to another judge, nor by the testimony of women. And if someone accuses her after li'an: if her husband accused her of zina, then he or another accuses her, [the latter] is subject to hadd because his li'an is like his hadd, confirming her chastity. And if he accused her by denial of lineage, then he or another accuses her, he is not subject to hadd due to the existence of an indication of zina. And if he retracts his own statement after li'an, then he or another accuses her, the accuser is subject to hadd, whether the li'an was for zina or denial of lineage. Its cause is his accusation of his wife with an accusation that would necessitate hadd in a foreign woman. Its prerequisite is competence for performance of testimony. Its ruling is the prohibition of intercourse after the mutual cursing, even before separation, and the obligation of separation between them, and the occurrence of an irrevocable (ba'in) separation by the separation. And it is derived from it being standing in place of the hadd, whether with respect to him or her, that it does not admit pardon, release, or settlement for money, such that if he settles with her for money to abandon (the li'an), the money is returned, and she has the right to demand after pardon. And that it does not admit delegation except in its establishment according to the saying of the Imam, like the hadd penalties; thus in al-Bada'i'. And know that the meaning is not that li'an stands in place of two hadd penalties in one situation; rather, it stands
Source pages p. 188

Commentary
This passage is an expanded commentary on the conditions and effects of li'an. The author begins by clarifying that the condition for li'an is that the wife must be someone whose accuser would receive the hadd penalty (i.e., she is chaste and adult). Then he elaborates on the definition from the matn: li'an consists of testimonies (shahadat) emphasized by oaths, coupled with cursing, and it stands in place of the hadd for qadhf for the husband and the hadd for zina for the wife. This indicates that the spouses must be competent for testimony (i.e., Muslim, adult, sane, upright) - not merely competent for oath as al-Shafi'i held. The Hanafi position requires the same conditions as for witnesses. If the judge dies or is removed before separating them, the new judge must repeat the li'an. The substitution for hadd means only regarding that specific spouse, not absolutely; otherwise the husband's testimony would never be accepted, which is not the case. However, according to al-Ikhtiyar, after li'an the husband's testimony is never accepted (concerning that wife). If a man accuses multiple wives with one statement, he must perform separate li'an for each wife. If he is not eligible for li'an (e.g., because he is not a competent witness), then one hadd suffices for all. Li'an cannot be established through indirect testimony (shahada 'ala shahada), a judge's letter, or women's testimony. After li'an, if another person accuses the wife of zina, that person is subject to hadd because the husband's li'an has confirmed her chastity. But if the original accusation was denial of lineage, then a subsequent accuser is not subject to hadd due to the ongoing indication of zina (the child's lineage is negated). If the husband retracts his accusation after li'an, then subsequent accusers are subject to hadd. The cause of li'an is the husband's accusation that would incur hadd if made against a non-relative. The prerequisite is that both spouses are competent to testify. The ruling includes: prohibition of intercourse immediately after li'an even before formal separation, mandatory separation, and the separation results in ba'in (irrevocable) divorce. Like hadd penalties, li'an cannot be pardoned, settled for money, or delegated except for its establishment according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The author finally clarifies that li'an does not substitute for both hadd penalties simultaneously but rather for each in its appropriate context.

Key Terms
شهادات (shahadat): Testimonies in the form of oaths; the four oaths sworn by each spouse during li'an.
قائم مقام حد القذف (qa'im maqam hadd al-qadhf): Li'an substitutes for the hadd penalty of eighty lashes that would be imposed on the husband if he could not prove his accusation.
أهلية الشهادة (ahliyyat al-shahada): Legal capacity to give testimony; required for both spouses in li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what condition is required for the spouses in li'an?
A) Competence for oaths (yamin)
B) Competence for testimony (shahada)
C) Both must be of sound mind
D) They must be free from any legal impediment

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a unique procedure requiring witness-competent spouses, with effects like hadd substitution and irrevocable separation.

Definition and Standing of Li‘an as Substitute for Hadd
Defines li‘an and explains its substitution for hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define li‘an according to the Hanafi school, state its legal effect as a substitute for hadd, and identify the condition of eligibility for testimony required for its validity.

Core Idea
Li‘an is testimonies, not mere oaths, and replaces the hadd penalty for the truthful spouse.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra’iq explains the definition of li‘an and its unique legal standing. The commentator shows that li‘an is a set of sworn testimonies that substitute for the fixed punishment (hadd) in cases of spousal accusation. Understanding this definition is essential because it drives many derived rulings, such as the requirement that both spouses must be eligible to testify, not merely to swear oaths. Let us unpack the definition and its implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of li‘an
The matn defines li‘an as 'shahadat' (testimonies) emphasized by oaths and curses. Note the key components: testimonies, oaths, curses.
This distinguishes li‘an from mere oaths.
2
Understand the conditional substitution of hadd
Li‘an stands in place of hadd al-qadhf for the husband if he is lying, and in place of hadd al-zina for the wife if she is lying. The substitution is not simultaneous.
If husband truthful, he avoids hadd; if wife truthful, she avoids hadd.
3
Explore the requirement of eligibility for testimony
The definition implies both parties must be of those whose testimony is accepted (ahl al-shahada). Contrast with Shafi‘i view that oath eligibility suffices.
A fasiq whose testimony is rejected cannot perform li‘an in Hanafi school.
4
Survey derived rulings
From the definition flow: no pardoning or settlement, separate li‘an for multiple wives, effects on future testimony, etc.
These rulings reinforce the hadd-like nature of li‘an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (هي شهادات مؤكدات بالأيمان مقرونة باللعن قائمة مقام حد القذف في حقه ومقام حد الزنا في حقها) وهذا بيان للركن فدل على اشتراط أهليتهما للشهادة في حق كل لا أهلية اليمين كما ذهب إليه الشافعي ودل على أنهما لو التعنا عند قاض فلم يفرق بينهما حتى مات أو عزل فإن الثاني يعيد اللعان كما لو شهدا عنده فمات أو عزل قبل القضاء ؛ كذا في البدائع والمراد بكونه قائماً مقام حد القذف في حقه أن يكون بالنسبة إليها لا مطلقاً، إذا لو كان مطلقاً لم تقبل شهادته أبداً مع أنها مقبولة كما ذكره الشارح في حد القذف، وفي الاختيار لا تقبل شهادته بعد اللعان أبداً، ولو قدف بكلمة أو بكلمات أربع زوجات له بالزنا لا يكفيه لعان واحد لهن بل لا بد من أن يلاعن كلاً منهن على حدة بخلاف ما إذا قذفها مراراً حيث يجب لعان واحد كما لو قذف أجنبية مراراً أو أجنبيات بكلمة أو كلمات يجب حد واحد لحصول المقصود وهو دفع العار عنهن ولا يحصل ذلك في اللعان إلا بالنسبة إلى كل واحدة ولو قذفهن ولم يكن من أهل اللعان اكتفى بحد واحد للكل للتداخل ؛ كذا في البدائع والمراد بكونه قائماً مقام حد الزنا في حقها أن يكون بالنسبة إلى الزوج لا يثبت اللعان بالشهادة على الشهادة ولا بكتاب القاضي إلى القاضي ولا بشهادة النساء، وإذا قذفها إنسان بعد اللعان إن رماها زوجها بالزنا ثم قذفها هو أو غيره حد لأن لعانه كحده مؤكد لعفتها، وإن قذفها بنفي الولد ثم قذفها هو أو غيره لا يحد لوجود أمارة الزنا، وإن أكذب نفسه بعد اللعان ثم قذفها هو أو غيره حد القاذف، سواء كان اللعان بالزنا أو بنفي الولد. وسببه قذفه لزوجته قذفاً الحد يوجب في الأجنبية، وأهله أهل الأداء للشهادة وحكمه حرمة الوطء بعد التلاعن ولو قبل التفريق بينهما ووجوب التفريق بينهما ووقوع البائن بالتفريق واستفيد من كونه قائماً مقام الحد سواء كان بالنسبة إليه أو إليها أنه لا يحتمل العفو والإبراء والصلح على مال حتى لو صالحها على الترك بمال ردت المال ولها المطالبة بعد العفو، وأنه لا يحتمل التوكيل إلا في إثباته على قول الإمام كالحدود؛ كذا في البدائع. واعلم أنه ليس المراد أن اللعان قائم مقام الحدين في حالة واحدة وإنما المراد أنه قائم مقام حد القذف في حقه إن كان كاذباً وهي صادقة وقائم مقام حد الزنا في حقها إن كانت كاذبة وهو صادق فافهم.
His statement: (It is testimonies emphasized by oaths coupled with curse, standing in place of the hadd of qadhf for him and in place of the hadd of zina for her). This is an explanation of the integral, so it indicates the condition of their eligibility for testimony for each, not eligibility for oath as al-Shafi‘i held. And it indicates that if they performed li‘an before a judge and he did not separate them until he died or was dismissed, then the second judge must repeat the li‘an, just as if they testified before him and he died or was dismissed before giving judgment; as in al-Bada‘i‘. And the meaning of it standing in place of the hadd of qadhf for him is that it is relative to her, not absolute – if it were absolute, his testimony would never be accepted, whereas it is accepted as the commentator mentioned in the chapter of qadhf. According to al-Ikhtiyar, his testimony is never accepted after li‘an. If he accused his four wives of zina with one word or with four words, one li‘an does not suffice for them; rather he must perform li‘an for each one separately, unlike if he accused her multiple times, where one li‘an is required, just as if he accused a non-relative female multiple times or multiple non-relative females with one word or multiple words, one hadd is required because the goal – repelling disgrace from them – is achieved, and that is not achieved in li‘an except for each one. If he accused them and he was not qualified for li‘an, one hadd suffices for all due to overlap; as in al-Bada‘i‘. And the meaning of it standing in place of the hadd of zina for her is that it is relative to the husband: li‘an is not established by testimony upon testimony, nor by a judge’s letter to another judge, nor by women’s testimony. If someone accuses her after li‘an – if her husband had accused her of zina and then he or another accused her, he is punished with hadd because his li‘an, like his hadd, confirms her chastity. If he accused her by denying the child and then he or another accused her, he is not punished because there is an indication of zina. If he retracted his own accusation after li‘an and then he or another accused her, the accuser is punished with hadd, whether the li‘an was for zina or denial of paternity. Its cause is his accusation of his wife with an accusation that would necessitate hadd for a non-relative woman; its prerequisite is capacity to perform testimony; its ruling is prohibition of intercourse after li‘an even before separation, obligation of separation between them, and occurrence of irrevocable divorce by the separation. And from its standing in place of hadd – whether relative to him or to her – it is derived that it does not permit pardon, release, nor settlement for property, such that if he settled with her to abandon it for property, the property is returned and she may demand after pardon; and that it does not permit agency except for its establishment according to Imam Abu Hanifa, like hudud; as in al-Bada‘i‘. Know that it is not meant that li‘an stands in place of both hadds in one situation; rather it stands in place of the hadd of qadhf for him if he is lying and she is truthful, and stands in place of the hadd of zina for her if she is lying and he is truthful – understand.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage is an expansion of the matn defining li‘an. The commentator explains that li‘an consists of testimonies (shahadat), not mere oaths, and is strengthened with oaths and curses. It substitutes the hadd punishment for qadhf (false accusation of zina) by the husband, and substitutes the hadd punishment for zina by the wife. The commentator clarifies that this substitution is conditional: if the husband is lying and the wife truthful, li‘an saves him from the hadd of qadhf; if the wife is lying and the husband truthful, li‘an imposes the hadd of zina on her. The passage then details many rulings derived from this definition: both parties must be eligible for testimony (ahl al-shahada) according to the Hanafi school, not just for oaths as the Shafi‘i school holds. It discusses repetition of li‘an if the judge dies, the non-acceptance of the husband’s testimony after li‘an, the need for separate li‘an for accusations of multiple wives, the inadmissibility of testimony-on-testimony or judge’s letter for li‘an, the effect of post-li‘an accusations by others, the prohibition of intercourse, the irrevocability of divorce, and that li‘an cannot be waived or settled for money, nor can it be delegated except for its establishment according to Abu Hanifa. The commentator emphasizes that li‘an substitutes only one of the two hadds at a time, as explained.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li‘an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when husband accuses wife of zina or denies paternity; consists of testimonies strengthened with oaths and curses.
قائم مقام حد القذف (qa'im maqam hadd al-qadhf): Standing in place of the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf). When the husband is lying and wife truthful, li‘an substitutes the hadd that would have been inflicted on him as a false accuser, saving him from the physical penalty.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the standing of li‘an regarding the hadd punishment for the husband if he is lying?
A) Li‘an stands in place of the hadd of qadhf, saving him from punishment.
B) Li‘an stands in place of the hadd of zina, punishing him.
C) Li‘an does not affect the hadd; he is punished separately.
D) Li‘an imposes a new penalty independent of hadd.

Key Takeaway
Li‘an is a set of testimonies that substitutes the hadd punishment, conditional on who is truthful, and requires both spouses to be eligible for testimony.
