Shurut al-Li‘an: Who Can Perform It and When
Enumerates conditions for li‘an with Shafi‘i dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the obligation and validity of li‘an and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi‘i position on li‘an over a deceased wife.

Core Idea
Li‘an requires capacity to testify (ahl al-ada‘), not acceptance; even a fasiq or blind person may perform it.

This lesson examines the detailed conditions for li‘an as enumerated in al-Bada‘i‘, classifying them into categories relating to the accuser, accused, both, the accusation, the place, and the act of qadhf. A key point is that eligibility for li‘an is based on having the capacity to testify (ahl al-ada‘), not on whether one's testimony is actually admissible. We also explore a major inter-madhhab dispute with the Shafi‘i school regarding li‘an for a deceased wife, and an intra-Hanafi difference concerning accusations of sodomy.

Guided Path
1
Identify the classification of conditions
The passage groups conditions into six categories: those related to the accuser, the accused, both, the accusation (madhmun bihi), the place (madhmun fih), and the act of qadhf itself. List each category and note the specific conditions under each.
The condition 'not having established proof of truthfulness' is for the accuser; 'denial and chastity' for the accused.
2
Determine the condition of capacity (ahl al-ada‘)
The text states that both spouses must be 'righteous for performance (salihan li al-ada‘), not for bearing testimony.' This means they must have the capacity to swear oaths and testify, even if their testimony is rejected due to sin (fisq) or blindness. Compare this with the requirement for witnesses in regular court cases.
A fasiq or blind person can perform li‘an because they belong to ahl al-ada‘.
3
Analyze the Hanafi-Shafi‘i dispute on li‘an over a deceased wife
The Hanafi school holds that accusing a deceased wife does not entail li‘an, because the required mutual presence and legal consequences (like separation) cannot be realized. Imam al-Shafi‘i allows li‘an over her grave to protect the husband from hadd. Identify the core reasoning of each school and the practical difference.
The Hanafi position is explicit: 'لا لعان بقذف زوجته الميتة' (no li‘an for accusing his deceased wife).
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on sodomy (liwat)
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that accusing one's wife of sodomy does not necessitate li‘an, because the hadd for sodomy is not established exactly like zina. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that it does require li‘an, analogizing it to zina in requiring hadd. Understand the basis of each view.
The text cites al-Bada‘i‘ for this ikhtilaf but does not give a clear tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي البدائع : وأما شرائط إلى القاذف اللعان فبعضها وجوب خاصة، وبعضها إلى المقذوف خاصة، وبعضها إليهما جميعاً، وبعضها إلى المقذوف به، وبعضها إلى المقذوف فيه وبعضها إلى نفس القذف. أما الأول فواحدة وهو عدم إقامة البينة على صدقه، وأما الثاني فإنكارها وجود الزنا منها وعفتها عنه وأما الثالث فالزوجية بينهما والحرية والعقل والإسلام والبلوغ والنطق وعدم الحد في قذف، فلا لعان في قذف المنكوحة فاسداً، ولا بقذف المبانة ولو واحدة بخلاف قذف المطلقة رجعياً، ولو قذف زوجته بزنا كان قبل الزوجية وجب اللعان ولا لعان بقذف زوجته الميتة . وقال الشافعي: يلاعن على قبرها . وأما ما يرجع إلى المقذوف به فهو الزنا، وأما المقذوف فيه فدار الإسلام، وأما نفس القذف فالرمي بصريح الزنا وسيأتي في الحدود. قوله : (ولو قذف زوجته بالزنا وصلحا شاهدين وهي ممن يحد قاذفها أو نفى نسب الولد وطالبته بموجب القذف اللعان) أي بصريح الزنا الموجب للحد في الأجنبية، فلو قدفها وجب بعمل قوم لوط فلا لعان عنده وعندهما يجب اللعان بناء على الحد كما في البدائع. وفي التتارخانية : رجل قذف امرأة رجل فقال الزوج صدقت هي كما قلت كان قاذفاً يلاعن، ولو قال صدقت مطلقاً من غير زيادة لم يكن قاذفاً هـ. وضمير «صلحاً» للزوجين . وأطلقها فشمل غير المدخولة والمراد صلاحيتهما لأدائها على المسلم لا للتحمل فلا لعان بين كافرين وإن قبلت شهادة بعضهم على بعض عندنا لأن اللعان شهادات مؤكدات بالأيمان فلا يكتفي بأهلية الشهادة بل لا بد معها من أهلية اليمين والكافر ليس من أهل الكفارة؛ كذا في البدائع. ولا بين كافرة ومسلم ولا بين مملوكين ولا إذا كان أحدهما مملوكاً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً أو محدوداً في قذف ولا يرد عليه لعان الأعمى والفاسق فإنه يجري بين الأعميين والفاسقين مع أنهما لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما من أهل الأداء إلا أنه لا تقبل للفسق في الفاسق ولعدم التمييز في الأعمى حتى لو قضى قاض بشهادة الفاسق والأعمى صح قضاؤه بخلاف ما إذا قضى بشهادة المملوك أو الصبي فإنه لا يصح، ولم يحتج إلى التمييز لأن المشهود عليه الزوجية قادر على أن يفصل بين نفسه وامرأته. وروى ابن المبارك عن الإمام الأعمى لا يلاعن . وهو وقيد بكونها ممن يحد يقاذفها احترازاً عما لو كانت وطئت بنكاح فاسد او كان لها ولد وليس له أب معروف أو زنت في عمرها ولو مرة أو وطئت وطئاً حراماً ولو مرة بشبهة لا يجري
And in al-Bada‘i‘: As for the conditions of li‘an relating to the accuser, some are specific to obligation, some to the accused, some to both, some to the accusation, some to the place, and some to the qadhf itself. As for the first, it is one: not establishing proof of his truthfulness. As for the second, it is her denial of having committed zina and her chastity regarding it [or: her denial of the existence of zina from her and her chastity from him?]. As for the third, it is marital relationship between them, freedom, sanity, Islam, puberty, speech, and not having been punished with hadd for qadhf. Thus no li‘an for qadhf of a woman married with a fasid contract, nor for qadhf of a permanently divorced woman even if one, unlike qadhf of a revocably divorced woman. If he accuses his wife of zina that occurred before marriage, li‘an is obligatory. There is no li‘an for accusing his deceased wife. Al-Shafi‘i said: He performs li‘an over her grave. As for what relates to the accusation, it is zina. As for the place, it is the abode of Islam. As for the qadhf itself, it is casting with explicit zina; it will come in the chapter of hudud. His statement: (And if he accused his wife of zina, both being righteous witnesses, and she is one whose accuser would be subject to hadd, or he denied the paternity of the child and she demanded the consequence of the accusation) i.e., with explicit zina that necessitates hadd for a non-relative woman. If he accused her of the act of the people of Lut, there is no li‘an according to him (Abu Hanifa?) and according to them (the Sahibayn?) li‘an is obligatory based on the hadd, as in al-Bada‘i‘. In al-Tatarkhaniyya: A man accused another man’s wife; the husband said 'you have spoken the truth; she is as you said' – he is an accuser and must perform li‘an. If he said 'you have spoken the truth' absolutely without addition, he is not an accuser. The pronoun in 'both righteous' refers to the spouses. He used it absolutely, including the non-consummated wife, and the meaning is their righteousness for performance on a Muslim, not for bearing testimony. Thus there is no li‘an between two disbelievers, even if the testimony of some of them is accepted against others according to us, because li‘an is testimonies emphasized by oaths; eligibility for testimony alone is insufficient; along with it eligibility for oath is necessary, and the disbeliever is not eligible for expiation; as in al-Bada‘i‘. Nor between a disbelieving woman and a Muslim, nor between two slaves, nor if one of them is a slave, a minor, insane, or has been punished for qadhf. And no objection is made against li‘an of the blind and the fasiq because it occurs between two blind persons and two fasiqs even though their testimony is not accepted, because they are of the people of capacity (ahl al-ada‘); but it is not accepted due to sin in the fasiq and lack of discrimination in the blind. If a judge gives judgment based on testimony of a fasiq or a blind person, his judgment is valid, unlike if he gives judgment based on testimony of a slave or minor; it is not valid. And discrimination is not needed because the person against whom testimony is given (the husband) is able to distinguish between himself and his wife. Ibn al-Mubarak reported from the Imam that the blind does not perform li‘an. And the restriction 'she is one whose accuser would be subject to hadd' is a precaution against cases where she was intercourse with a fasid marriage, or she had a child with no known father, or she committed zina even once in her life, or she had intercourse even once with a doubtful act – then li‘an does not take place.
Source pages p. 189

Commentary
This passage presents the conditions for li‘an drawn from al-Bada‘i‘. The conditions are classified into categories: conditions relating to the accuser (the husband), the accused (the wife), both, the allegation, the place, and the form of accusation. For the husband, the main condition is that he cannot have four witnesses to prove his claim; if he does, he must bring them instead of li‘an. For the wife, she must deny the accusation and claim chastity. Both must be spouses, free, sane, Muslim, adult, speaking, and the husband must not have been punished for qadhf. Specific cases are excluded: no li‘an if the marriage was invalid (fasid), if she is irrevocably divorced, but if revocably divorced it is allowed. Accusation of zina before marriage does require li‘an. The Shafi‘i school allows li‘an over the grave of a deceased wife, but Hanafis do not. The accusation must be explicit zina; accusing of sodomy (luti) does not require li‘an according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad it does. The spouses must be righteous (salih) for performance, not for bearing witness, so a fasiq and a blind person whose testimony is not accepted can still perform li‘an because they have capacity (ahl al-ada‘). Even a judge’s judgment based on their testimony is valid. However, slaves and minors cannot perform li‘an. The wife must be such that if a stranger accused her, he would be liable for hadd. Thus, if she has a history that removes the hadd from a false accuser (like she had a child without a known father, or she herself committed zina), then no li‘an.

Key Terms
شرائط اللعان (shurut al-li‘an): Conditions necessary for the obligation and validity of li‘an; divided into categories relating to accuser, accused, accusation, place, and the act of qadhf itself.
أهل الأداء (ahl al-ada‘): People who have the capacity to testify, even if their testimony is not accepted due to a defect like sin or blindness. They can still perform li‘an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, can a fasiq (sinner) husband perform li‘an if his testimony would be rejected in court?
A) Yes, because li‘an requires only capacity to testify (ahl al-ada‘), not acceptance.
B) No, because his testimony is invalid, so he cannot perform li‘an.
C) Only if he repents first.
D) Yes, but only if the wife is also a fasiqa.

Key Takeaway
Li‘an conditions hinge on capacity for testimony (ahl al-ada‘), not admissibility, and no li‘an for a deceased wife.

The Obligation and Conditions of Li'an with the Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Sodomy
Commentary expanding on li'an conditions with intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which li'an becomes wajib and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding accusation of sodomy.

Core Idea
Li'an substitutes for hadd; its obligation hinges on explicit zina accusation, but sodomy creates an intra-Hanafi dispute.

Li'an (mutual imprecation) is a unique procedure in Islamic law that settles accusations of zina or paternity denial between spouses. The Hanafi school lays out detailed conditions for its obligation. This lesson examines the core ruling and a key internal dispute over whether accusing one's wife of sodomy triggers li'an.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Read the opening statement: li'an becomes wajib when the husband accuses his wife of zina or denies paternity and she demands the consequence. Note that refusal leads to imprisonment.
The obligation is conditional on the wife's demand.
2
Enumerate the conditions from al-Bada'i'
The text categorizes conditions by who they relate to: the accuser (lack of evidence), the accused (denial and chastity), both (marriage, freedom, sanity, etc.), the object (zina), the place (abode of Islam), and the accusation (explicit zina).
These conditions ensure li'an only applies when the hadd would otherwise be required.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on sodomy
The text presents a dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that accusing the wife of the act of the people of Lut (sodomy) does not trigger li'an because the accusation is not explicit zina. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (Sahibayn) say li'an is wajib because such an accusation would necessitate hadd.
The later mufta bihi follows the Sahibayn view.
4
Contrast with al-Shafi'i's position on the deceased
The Shafi'i school allows li'an over the grave of a deceased wife, which the Hanafi school rejects. This is an inter-madhhab difference.
Hanafis restrict li'an to living spouses.
5
Derive the legal consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical difference: under Abu Hanifa, an accusation of sodomy yields no li'an, so the husband faces hadd for qadhf if he cannot prove it; under the Sahibayn, li'an is performed, which prevents hadd.

ولم تشترط عفته لأنه لو كان فاسقاً بالزنا جرى اللعان بينه وبينها وإن كان لا يحد قاذفه لما قدمنا من جريانه بين الفاسقين فهذا وجه تخصيصها بهذا الشرط كما حققه الشارح رداً على صاحب النهاية. وأراد بكونها ولدها، وأطلقه فشمل ولدها منه أو من غيره بأن يقول هذا الولد من الزنا أو هذا الولد ليس مني وما إذا صرح معه بالزنا أو لم يصرح على مختار صاحب الهداية والشارح خلافاً لما في المحيط والمبتغى. والحق الإطلاق لأن قطع النسب من كل وجه يستلزم الزنا فلا عبرة باحتمال كون الولد من غيره بوطء بشبهة ولهذا قال في البدائع : هذا الاحتمال ساقط بالإجماع للإجماع على أنه إن نفاه عن الأب المشهور بأن قال له لست لأبيك يكون قاذفاً لأمه حتى يلزمه حد القذف مع وجود هذا الاحتمال وقد ظهر لي أن قول من قال لا يجب حد ولا لعان بنفي الولد عن أبيه إذا لم يصرح بالزنا محمول على حالة الرضا، وقول من أوجبه وإن لم يصرح به محمول على حالة الغضب وبه يندفع إلزام التناقض على صاحب النهاية والدراية . وإنما حملناه على ذلك لتصريحهم بالتفصيل في باب حد القذف - والله الموفق - بخلاف قوله وجدت معها رجلاً يجامعها فإنه ليس بقذف لأن الجماع لا يستلزم الزنا. وقيد بطلبها لأنها لو لم تطالبه فلا لعان لأنه حقها لدفع العار عنها فيشترط طلبها، ولا بد من كونه في مجلس القاضي ؛ كذا في البدائع ومراده طلبها إذا كان القذف بصريح الزنا أما بنفي الولد فالطلب حقه أيضاً لاحتياجه إلى نفي من ليس ولده عنه. وأشار بعدم اشتراط الفور في الطلب إلى أن سكوتها لا يبطل حقها وإن طالت المدة لأن تقادم الزمان لا بطلان الحق في القذف والقصاص كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وزاد في الجوهرة وحقوق العباد، وفي خزانة الفقه، ولو سكتت ولم ترفع إلى الحاكم كان أفضل وينبغي للحاكم أن يقول لها اتركي وأعرضي عن هذا لأنه دعاء إلى الستر فإن تركت مدة ثم خاصمت فلها ذلك كما في ليس له أب معروف فكان شبهة الزنا، أما لو كان بعدما أكذب نفسه فالشبهة منتفية فيلا عن الزوج الثاني تأمل .
Or if he denies the lineage of the child and she demands the consequence of the accusation, li'an becomes obligatory. If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an. It stands in place of the hadd for qadhf in his right if he is lying and she is truthful, and it stands in place of the hadd for zina in her right if she is lying and he is truthful, so understand. In al-Bada'i': As for the conditions for li'an related to the accuser, some are particular to obligation, some to the accused, some to both, some to the object of accusation, some to the place of accusation, and some to the accusation itself. The first is one: not establishing evidence of his truthfulness. The second: her denial of having committed zina and her being chaste from it. The third: marriage between them, freedom, sanity, Islam, puberty, speech, and not having been subjected to hadd for qadhf. So there is no li'an for accusing a woman married in a fasid marriage, nor for accusing a divorced woman irrevocably (ba'in), even if once, unlike accusing a revocably divorced woman. If he accuses his wife of zina before marriage, li'an is obligatory, and there is no li'an for accusing his deceased wife. Al-Shafi'i said: He performs li'an upon her grave. As for what relates to the object of accusation, it is zina; as for the place of accusation, it is the abode of Islam; as for the accusation itself, it is hurling an accusation of explicit zina, and it will come in the chapter of hudud. Until his statement: (If he accuses his wife of zina while they are both fit as witnesses, and she is one whose accuser would be subject to hadd, or he denies the lineage of the child and she demands the consequence of the accusation, li'an is obligatory) i.e., by explicit zina that necessitates hadd in the case of a non-mahram woman. So if he accuses her of the act of the people of Lut, there is no li'an according to him (Abu Hanifa), while according to them (the two disciples) li'an is obligatory based on the hadd, as in al-Bada'i'. In al-Tatarakhaniyya: A man accused another man's wife, and the husband said, 'You are truthful; she is as you said' – he is an accuser and he performs li'an. If he said, 'You are truthful' absolutely without addition, he is not an accuser. The pronoun 'salaha' refers to the spouses. He (the author) used an absolute expression, so it includes one who has not been consummated, and the intent is their fitness to perform it (the accusation) as a Muslim, not to bear testimony. So there is no li'an between two disbelievers, even if the testimony of some of them is accepted against others according to us, because li'an is testimony emphasized by oaths, so the capacity for testimony alone is insufficient; rather the capacity for oath is also required, and the disbeliever is not capable of expiation; thus in al-Bada'i'. Nor between a disbelieving woman and a Muslim, nor between two slaves, nor if one of them is a slave, a child, insane, or has been subjected to hadd for qadhf. And li'an of a blind person and a sinful person is not rejected; it occurs between two blind persons and two sinful persons, even though their testimonies are not accepted, because they are people of capacity (ahl al-ada') except that it is not accepted in the case of the sinful due to sinfulness, and in the case of the blind due to lack of discrimination. So much so that if a judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a sinful person or a blind person, his judgment is valid, unlike if he passes judgment based on the testimony of a slave or a child, for it is not valid. And discrimination is not needed because the one being testified against (the husband) is capable of separating between himself and his wife. Ibn al-Mubarak narrated from the Imam: The blind person does not perform li'an. And it is restricted by 'she whose accuser would be subjected to hadd' as a precaution against the case where she has been entered into a fasid marriage, or she has a child without a known father, or she has committed zina even once in her life, or she has been entered into unlawful intercourse even once due to doubt – in such cases li'an does not occur. With the precedence of the first – he is the subject of 'claimed'. His statement 'uzimahu' means the child is obligated to the first husband. His statement 'wa in waladat min al-thani' means she accuses him of denying the child. His statement 'la shay'a 'alayhi' means nothing is upon the second for that accusation if it was before the denial of the first, i.e., before the first husband himself denied the claim of the child. And the reason nothing is upon the second is that she has a child without a known father, so it was doubt of zina. However, if it was after he denied himself, then the doubt is eliminated, so he (the second husband) performs li'an – reflect. His statement: 'fa al-talabu haqqahu aydan' means it is the right of the accuser, not the right of the child as understood by the commentator of al-Tanwir. His statement: 'la yujibu al-li'an'. And branching from this condition: If he accused her, and she married another, and the first claimed the child, the child is obligated to him and he is subject to hadd for qadhf, and if she gave birth from the second, nothing is upon him if it was before the denial of the first. If it was after the denial, he performs li'an, as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. Since the woman is the accused, not the husband, she is specifically conditioned by being one whose accuser would be subjected to hadd, after the condition of capacity for testimony. And since the husband is not accused but is a witness, capacity for testimony is conditioned for him as for her, but his chastity is not conditioned because if he is sinful by zina, li'an operates between him and her, even though his accuser would not be subjected to hadd, due to what we mentioned earlier of it operating between two sinful persons. So this is the reason for specifying her with this condition, as the commentator clarified in refutation of the author of al-Nihaya. And what is meant by 'she whose accuser would be subjected to hadd' is that she is chaste from zina only, because her being among those capable of testimony indicates the condition of freedom, legal capacity, and Islam, so nothing remains of the conditions of ihsan except chastity, as stated in Sharh al-Wiqaya. And what is meant by 'denial of lineage' is denial of the lineage of her child, and it is absolute, so it includes her child from him or from another, whether he says 'this child is from zina' or 'this child is not from me', and whether he explicitly mentions zina or not, according to the chosen view of the author of al-Hidaya and the commentator, contrary to what is in al-Muhit and al-Mubtagha. And the correct view is absoluteness because cutting off lineage from every aspect necessarily implies zina, so the possibility that the child is from another by doubt intercourse is disregarded. Thus it is said in al-Bada'i': This possibility is rejected by consensus, because there is consensus that if he denies the child from a well-known father by saying 'you are not your father's son', he becomes an accuser of his mother such that the hadd for qadhf is obligated upon him despite this possibility. And it has become clear to me that the statement of those who say that hadd and li'an are not obligatory by denial of lineage from a father if he does not explicitly mention zina is interpreted as a case of contentment, and the statement of those who oblige it even without explicit mention is interpreted as a case of anger. With this, the accusation of contradiction against the author of al-Nihaya and al-Diraya is refuted. We interpret it that way because of their explicit detail in the chapter on hadd for qadhf – and Allah is the granter of success – unlike his statement 'I found a man having intercourse with her', for it is not qadhf because intercourse does not necessarily imply zina. And it is restricted by her demand because if she does not demand it, there is no li'an, for it is her right to remove shame from herself, so her demand is conditioned, and it must be in the court of the judge; thus in al-Bada'i'. And his intent is her demand when the qadhf is by explicit zina. As for denial of lineage, the demand is also his right because he needs to deny someone who is not his child. And his indication that immediacy is not a condition in the demand shows that her silence does not nullify her right even if the period is long, because the passage of time does not nullify a right in qadhf and qisas as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. And in al-Jawhara, Huquq al-'Ibad, and Khizanat al-Fiqh it is added: If she remained silent and did not present it to the judge, it is better, and it is recommended for the judge to tell her to leave it and refrain from it because it is an invitation to concealment. If she left it for a period and then disputed, she has the right to do so, as in the case where a child has no known father, so it is doubt of zina. But if it was after he denied himself, the doubt is eliminated, so the second husband performs li'an – reflect.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the conditions for li'an (mutual imprecation) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating that if a husband accuses his wife of zina or denies the paternity of her child, and she demands the legal consequences, li'an becomes obligatory. If the husband refuses to perform li'an, he is imprisoned until he does so. This is because li'an substitutes for the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf) in the husband's case if he is lying and she is truthful, and for the hadd of zina in her case if she is lying. The commentary then cites al-Bada'i' to enumerate the conditions for li'an, classifying them into categories: conditions relating to the accuser (e.g., not having established evidence of his truthfulness), the accused (her denial of zina and chastity), both (marriage, freedom, sanity, Islam, puberty, speech, and not having been previously punished for qadhf), the object (zina), the place (abode of Islam), and the accusation itself (explicit accusation of zina). The passage then discusses specific rulings: li'an does not occur if the marriage is invalid (fasid), if the wife is irrevocably divorced (ba'in), or if the wife is deceased. The Shafi'i opinion that li'an can be performed over the grave is noted. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears regarding accusation of sodomy (act of the people of Lut): Abu Hanifa holds that li'an is not required because such an accusation does not explicitly entail zina, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that li'an is obligatory based on the hadd. The commentary also addresses the fitness of the spouses to testify: they must be capable of bearing witness as Muslims, which excludes disbelievers, slaves, children, and the insane. However, li'an can occur between blind persons and sinners despite their testimony not being generally accepted, because they are capable of performing the oaths. The passage then delves into denial of lineage (nafi al-nasab), clarifying that explicit mention of zina is not necessary for li'an; the denial itself implies zina. This is supported by consensus and the ruling in qadhf cases. Finally, the passage stresses that the demand for li'an must be made in court and silence does not invalidate the right. It is recommended for the judge to encourage reconciliation. The commentary reconciles apparent contradictions by distinguishing between cases of contentment and anger.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'an): Mutual imprecation between husband and wife when he accuses her of zina or denies paternity; consists of oath and imprecation statements.
القذف (al-qadhf): False accusation of zina or denying lineage, which incurs hadd punishment.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on li'an if a husband accuses his wife of the act of the people of Lut (sodomy)?
A) Li'an is wajib according to all Hanafi scholars.
B) Li'an is not wajib according to Abu Hanifa, but wajib according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad.
C) Li'an is not wajib according to any Hanafi scholar.
D) Li'an is wajib only if the wife demands it.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is wajib when a husband accuses his wife of explicit zina; the accusation of sodomy creates an intra-Hanafi dispute, with the mufta bihi being the Sahibayn position that li'an is required.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Further Conditions: Witness Capacity, Denial of Lineage, and Procedural Right
Detailed conditions for witness capacity and denial of lineage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions related to witness capacity (e.g., for slaves, blind persons) and explain the rulings on denial of lineage and the wife's right to demand li'an.

Core Idea
Li'an requires both spouses to be fit for testimony and oath; denial of lineage inherently implies zina, and the wife's demand is a right that does not lapse with time.

Beyond the basic conditions, li'an has nuanced requirements regarding the legal capacity of the spouses, the nature of the denial of paternity, and the procedure for demanding li'an. This lesson explores these details as presented in the commentary, including the treatment of slaves, disbelievers, blind persons, and the significance of explicit vs. implicit denial.

Guided Path
1
Identify the capacity requirements for witnesses
Read the text: both spouses must be fit (salah) as witnesses, i.e., free, Muslim, sane, adult. Li'an does not occur between disbelievers, slaves, a Muslim with a disbeliever, or if one is a child, insane, or hadd for qadhf.
The key is that they must be capable of performing the oath (yamin), which disbelievers cannot do in the required form.
2
Analyze the exception for blind and sinful persons
Despite their testimony being generally unacceptable, li'an runs between two blind or two sinful persons because they are still capable of performing the oath. The judge's decision based on their testimony is valid.
The text cites a narration from Ibn al-Mubarak that the blind do not perform li'an, but the dominant Hanafi view allows it.
3
Examine the ruling on denial of lineage (nafi al-nasab)
Denial of a child's lineage (e.g., 'this child is not from me') is treated as an accusation of zina even without explicit mention. This is based on consensus that cutting lineage implies zina.
The text resolves an apparent contradiction by distinguishing between cases of anger (where li'an is wajib) and contentment (where it is not).
4
Understand the wife's right of demand
The wife must demand li'an in the judge's court; silence does not nullify her right even after a long time. The judge may advise her to refrain for the sake of concealment.
This right is personal to her and not inherited by the child.

أو نفى نسب الولد وطالبته بموجب القذف وجب اللعان فإن أبى حبس حتى يلاعن يرجع مقام حد القذف في حقه إن كان كاذباً وهي صادقة وقائم مقام حد الزنا في حقها إن كانت كاذبة وهو صادق فافهم. وفي البدائع : وأما شرائط إلى القاذف اللعان فبعضها. وجوب خاصة، وبعضها إلى المقذوف خاصة، وبعضها إليهما جميعاً، وبعضها إلى المقذوف به، وبعضها إلى المقذوف فيه وبعضها إلى نفس القذف. أما الأول فواحدة وهو عدم إقامة البينة على صدقه، وأما الثاني فإنكارها وجود الزنا منها وعفتها عنه وأما الثالث فالزوجية بينهما والحرية والعقل والإسلام والبلوغ والنطق وعدم الحد في قذف، فلا لعان في قذف المنكوحة فاسداً، ولا بقذف المبانة ولو واحدة بخلاف قذف المطلقة رجعياً، ولو قذف زوجته بزنا كان قبل الزوجية وجب اللعان ولا لعان بقذف زوجته الميتة . وقال الشافعي: يلاعن على قبرها . وأما ما يرجع إلى المقذوف به فهو الزنا، وأما المقذوف فيه فدار الإسلام، وأما نفس القذف فالرمي بصريح الزنا وسيأتي في الحدود. حتى قوله : (ولو قذف زوجته بالزنا وصلحا شاهدين وهي ممن يحد قاذفها أو نفى نسب الولد وطالبته بموجب القذف اللعان) أي بصريح الزنا الموجب للحد في الأجنبية، فلو قدفها وجب بعمل قوم لوط فلا لعان عنده وعندهما يجب اللعان بناء على الحد كما في البدائع. وفي التتارخانية : رجل قذف امرأة رجل فقال الزوج صدقت هي كما قلت كان قاذفاً يلاعن، ولو قال صدقت مطلقاً من غير زيادة لم يكن قاذفاً هـ. وضمير «صلحاً» للزوجين . وأطلقها فشمل غير المدخولة والمراد صلاحيتهما لأدائها على المسلم لا للتحمل فلا لعان بين كافرين وإن قبلت شهادة بعضهم على بعض عندنا لأن اللعان شهادات مؤكدات بالأيمان فلا يكتفي بأهلية الشهادة بل لا بد معها من أهلية اليمين والكافر ليس من أهل الكفارة؛ كذا في البدائع. ولا بين كافرة ومسلم ولا بين مملوكين ولا إذا كان أحدهما مملوكاً أو صبياً أو مجنوناً أو محدوداً في قذف ولا يرد عليه لعان الأعمى والفاسق فإنه يجري بين الأعميين والفاسقين مع أنهما لا تقبل شهادتهما لأنهما من أهل الأداء إلا أنه لا تقبل للفسق في الفاسق ولعدم التمييز في الأعمى حتى لو قضى قاض بشهادة الفاسق والأعمى صح قضاؤه بخلاف ما إذا قضى بشهادة المملوك أو الصبي فإنه لا يصح، ولم يحتج إلى التمييز لأن المشهود عليه الزوجية قادر على أن يفصل بين نفسه وامرأته. وروى ابن المبارك عن الإمام الأعمى لا يلاعن . وهو وقيد بكونها ممن يحد يقاذفها احترازاً عما لو كانت وطئت بنكاح فاسد او كان لها ولد وليس له أب معروف أو زنت في عمرها ولو مرة أو وطئت وطئاً حراماً ولو مرة بشبهة لا يجري بتقديم الأول وهو فاعل ادعى». وقوله لزمه ) أي لزم الولد الزوج الأول. وقوله «وإن ولدت من الثاني أي وقذفها بنفي الولد . وقوله لا شيء عليه أي على الثاني بذلك القذف إن كان قبل إكذاب الأول أي قبل إكذاب الزوج الأول نفسه بدعوى الولد وإنما كان لا شيء على الثاني لأن لها ولداً ليس له أب معروف فكان شبهة الزنا، أما لو كان بعدما أكذب نفسه فالشبهة منتفية فيلا عن الزوج الثاني تأمل . قوله : (فالطلب حقه أيضاً أي حق القاذف لا حق الولد كما فهمه شارح التنوير قوله: (لا يوجب اللعان. وتفرع على هذا الشرط لو قذفها فتزوجت غيره فادعى الأول الولد لزمه وحد للقذف وإن ولدت من الثاني لا شيء عليه إن كان قبل إكذاب الأول، وإن كان بعد الإكذاب لا عن كما في التتارخانية. ولما كانت المرأة هي المقذوفة دونه اختصت باشتراط كونها ممن يحد قاذفها بعد اشتراط أهلية الشهادة ولما كان الزوج ليس مقذوفاً وإنما هو شاهد اشترط في حقه كما اشترط في حقها أهلية الشهادة ولم تشترط عفته لأنه لو كان فاسقاً بالزنا جرى اللعان بينه وبينها وإن كان لا يحد قاذفه لما قدمنا من جريانه بين الفاسقين فهذا وجه تخصيصها بهذا الشرط كما حققه الشارح رداً على صاحب النهاية. وأراد بكونها ممن يحد قاذفها أن تكون عفيفة عن الزنا فقط لأن كونها من أهل الشهادة يدل على اشتراط الحرية والتكليف والإسلام فلم يبق من شرائط الإحصان إلا العفة كما أفاده في شرح الوقاية وأراد بنفي نسب الولد نفي نسب ولدها، وأطلقه فشمل ولدها منه أو من غيره بأن يقول هذا الولد من الزنا أو هذا الولد ليس مني وما إذا صرح معه بالزنا أو لم يصرح على مختار صاحب الهداية والشارح خلافاً لما في المحيط والمبتغى. والحق الإطلاق لأن قطع النسب من كل وجه يستلزم الزنا فلا عبرة باحتمال كون الولد من غيره بوطء بشبهة ولهذا قال في البدائع : هذا الاحتمال ساقط بالإجماع للإجماع على أنه إن نفاه عن الأب المشهور بأن قال له لست لأبيك يكون قاذفاً لأمه حتى يلزمه حد القذف مع وجود هذا الاحتمال وقد ظهر لي أن قول من قال لا يجب حد ولا لعان بنفي الولد عن أبيه إذا لم يصرح بالزنا محمول على حالة الرضا، وقول من أوجبه وإن لم يصرح به محمول على حالة الغضب وبه يندفع إلزام التناقض على صاحب النهاية والدراية . وإنما حملناه على ذلك لتصريحهم بالتفصيل في باب حد القذف - والله الموفق - بخلاف قوله وجدت معها رجلاً يجامعها فإنه ليس بقذف لأن الجماع لا يستلزم الزنا. وقيد بطلبها لأنها لو لم تطالبه فلا لعان لأنه حقها لدفع العار عنها فيشترط طلبها، ولا بد من كونه في مجلس القاضي ؛ كذا في البدائع ومراده طلبها إذا كان القذف بصريح الزنا أما بنفي الولد فالطلب حقه أيضاً لاحتياجه إلى نفي من ليس ولده عنه. وأشار بعدم اشتراط الفور في الطلب إلى أن سكوتها لا يبطل حقها وإن طالت المدة لأن تقادم الزمان لا بطلان الحق في القذف والقصاص كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وزاد في الجوهرة وحقوق العباد، وفي خزانة الفقه، ولو سكتت ولم ترفع إلى الحاكم كان أفضل وينبغي للحاكم أن يقول لها اتركي وأعرضي عن هذا لأنه دعاء إلى الستر فإن تركت مدة ثم خاصمت فلها ذلك كما في ليس له أب معروف فكان شبهة الزنا، أما لو كان بعدما أكذب نفسه فالشبهة منتفية فيلا عن الزوج الثاني تأمل .
Or if he denies the lineage of the child and she demands the consequence of the accusation, li'an becomes obligatory. If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an. It stands in place of the hadd for qadhf in his right if he is lying and she is truthful, and it stands in place of the hadd for zina in her right if she is lying and he is truthful, so understand. In al-Bada'i': As for the conditions for li'an related to the accuser, some are particular to obligation, some to the accused, some to both, some to the object of accusation, some to the place of accusation, and some to the accusation itself. The first is one: not establishing evidence of his truthfulness. The second: her denial of having committed zina and her being chaste from it. The third: marriage between them, freedom, sanity, Islam, puberty, speech, and not having been subjected to hadd for qadhf. So there is no li'an for accusing a woman married in a fasid marriage, nor for accusing a divorced woman irrevocably (ba'in), even if once, unlike accusing a revocably divorced woman. If he accuses his wife of zina before marriage, li'an is obligatory, and there is no li'an for accusing his deceased wife. Al-Shafi'i said: He performs li'an upon her grave. As for what relates to the object of accusation, it is zina; as for the place of accusation, it is the abode of Islam; as for the accusation itself, it is hurling an accusation of explicit zina, and it will come in the chapter of hudud. Until his statement: (If he accuses his wife of zina while they are both fit as witnesses, and she is one whose accuser would be subject to hadd, or he denies the lineage of the child and she demands the consequence of the accusation, li'an is obligatory) i.e., by explicit zina that necessitates hadd in the case of a non-mahram woman. So if he accuses her of the act of the people of Lut, there is no li'an according to him (Abu Hanifa), while according to them (the two disciples) li'an is obligatory based on the hadd, as in al-Bada'i'. In al-Tatarakhaniyya: A man accused another man's wife, and the husband said, 'You are truthful; she is as you said' – he is an accuser and he performs li'an. If he said, 'You are truthful' absolutely without addition, he is not an accuser. The pronoun 'salaha' refers to the spouses. He (the author) used an absolute expression, so it includes one who has not been consummated, and the intent is their fitness to perform it (the accusation) as a Muslim, not to bear testimony. So there is no li'an between two disbelievers, even if the testimony of some of them is accepted against others according to us, because li'an is testimony emphasized by oaths, so the capacity for testimony alone is insufficient; rather the capacity for oath is also required, and the disbeliever is not capable of expiation; thus in al-Bada'i'. Nor between a disbelieving woman and a Muslim, nor between two slaves, nor if one of them is a slave, a child, insane, or has been subjected to hadd for qadhf. And li'an of a blind person and a sinful person is not rejected; it occurs between two blind persons and two sinful persons, even though their testimonies are not accepted, because they are people of capacity (ahl al-ada') except that it is not accepted in the case of the sinful due to sinfulness, and in the case of the blind due to lack of discrimination. So much so that if a judge passes judgment based on the testimony of a sinful person or a blind person, his judgment is valid, unlike if he passes judgment based on the testimony of a slave or a child, for it is not valid. And discrimination is not needed because the one being testified against (the husband) is capable of separating between himself and his wife. Ibn al-Mubarak narrated from the Imam: The blind person does not perform li'an. And it is restricted by 'she whose accuser would be subjected to hadd' as a precaution against the case where she has been entered into a fasid marriage, or she has a child without a known father, or she has committed zina even once in her life, or she has been entered into unlawful intercourse even once due to doubt – in such cases li'an does not occur. With the precedence of the first – he is the subject of 'claimed'. His statement 'uzimahu' means the child is obligated to the first husband. His statement 'wa in waladat min al-thani' means she accuses him of denying the child. His statement 'la shay'a 'alayhi' means nothing is upon the second for that accusation if it was before the denial of the first, i.e., before the first husband himself denied the claim of the child. And the reason nothing is upon the second is that she has a child without a known father, so it was doubt of zina. However, if it was after he denied himself, then the doubt is eliminated, so he (the second husband) performs li'an – reflect. His statement: 'fa al-talabu haqqahu aydan' means it is the right of the accuser, not the right of the child as understood by the commentator of al-Tanwir. His statement: 'la yujibu al-li'an'. And branching from this condition: If he accused her, and she married another, and the first claimed the child, the child is obligated to him and he is subject to hadd for qadhf, and if she gave birth from the second, nothing is upon him if it was before the denial of the first. If it was after the denial, he performs li'an, as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. Since the woman is the accused, not the husband, she is specifically conditioned by being one whose accuser would be subjected to hadd, after the condition of capacity for testimony. And since the husband is not accused but is a witness, capacity for testimony is conditioned for him as for her, but his chastity is not conditioned because if he is sinful by zina, li'an operates between him and her, even though his accuser would not be subjected to hadd, due to what we mentioned earlier of it operating between two sinful persons. So this is the reason for specifying her with this condition, as the commentator clarified in refutation of the author of al-Nihaya. And what is meant by 'she whose accuser would be subjected to hadd' is that she is chaste from zina only, because her being among those capable of testimony indicates the condition of freedom, legal capacity, and Islam, so nothing remains of the conditions of ihsan except chastity, as stated in Sharh al-Wiqaya. And what is meant by 'denial of lineage' is denial of the lineage of her child, and it is absolute, so it includes her child from him or from another, whether he says 'this child is from zina' or 'this child is not from me', and whether he explicitly mentions zina or not, according to the chosen view of the author of al-Hidaya and the commentator, contrary to what is in al-Muhit and al-Mubtagha. And the correct view is absoluteness because cutting off lineage from every aspect necessarily implies zina, so the possibility that the child is from another by doubt intercourse is disregarded. Thus it is said in al-Bada'i': This possibility is rejected by consensus, because there is consensus that if he denies the child from a well-known father by saying 'you are not your father's son', he becomes an accuser of his mother such that the hadd for qadhf is obligated upon him despite this possibility. And it has become clear to me that the statement of those who say that hadd and li'an are not obligatory by denial of lineage from a father if he does not explicitly mention zina is interpreted as a case of contentment, and the statement of those who oblige it even without explicit mention is interpreted as a case of anger. With this, the accusation of contradiction against the author of al-Nihaya and al-Diraya is refuted. We interpret it that way because of their explicit detail in the chapter on hadd for qadhf – and Allah is the granter of success – unlike his statement 'I found a man having intercourse with her', for it is not qadhf because intercourse does not necessarily imply zina. And it is restricted by her demand because if she does not demand it, there is no li'an, for it is her right to remove shame from herself, so her demand is conditioned, and it must be in the court of the judge; thus in al-Bada'i'. And his intent is her demand when the qadhf is by explicit zina. As for denial of lineage, the demand is also his right because he needs to deny someone who is not his child. And his indication that immediacy is not a condition in the demand shows that her silence does not nullify her right even if the period is long, because the passage of time does not nullify a right in qadhf and qisas as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. And in al-Jawhara, Huquq al-'Ibad, and Khizanat al-Fiqh it is added: If she remained silent and did not present it to the judge, it is better, and it is recommended for the judge to tell her to leave it and refrain from it because it is an invitation to concealment. If she left it for a period and then disputed, she has the right to do so, as in the case where a child has no known father, so it is doubt of zina. But if it was after he denied himself, the doubt is eliminated, so the second husband performs li'an – reflect.
Source pages p. 190

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the conditions for li'an (mutual imprecation) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins by stating that if a husband accuses his wife of zina or denies the paternity of her child, and she demands the legal consequences, li'an becomes obligatory. If the husband refuses to perform li'an, he is imprisoned until he does so. This is because li'an substitutes for the hadd punishment for false accusation (qadhf) in the husband's case if he is lying and she is truthful, and for the hadd of zina in her case if she is lying. The commentary then cites al-Bada'i' to enumerate the conditions for li'an, classifying them into categories: conditions relating to the accuser (e.g., not having established evidence of his truthfulness), the accused (her denial of zina and chastity), both (marriage, freedom, sanity, Islam, puberty, speech, and not having been previously punished for qadhf), the object (zina), the place (abode of Islam), and the accusation itself (explicit accusation of zina). The passage then discusses specific rulings: li'an does not occur if the marriage is invalid (fasid), if the wife is irrevocably divorced (ba'in), or if the wife is deceased. The Shafi'i opinion that li'an can be performed over the grave is noted. A key intra-Hanafi dispute appears regarding accusation of sodomy (act of the people of Lut): Abu Hanifa holds that li'an is not required because such an accusation does not explicitly entail zina, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that li'an is obligatory based on the hadd. The commentary also addresses the fitness of the spouses to testify: they must be capable of bearing witness as Muslims, which excludes disbelievers, slaves, children, and the insane. However, li'an can occur between blind persons and sinners despite their testimony not being generally accepted, because they are capable of performing the oaths. The passage then delves into denial of lineage (nafi al-nasab), clarifying that explicit mention of zina is not necessary for li'an; the denial itself implies zina. This is supported by consensus and the ruling in qadhf cases. Finally, the passage stresses that the demand for li'an must be made in court and silence does not invalidate the right. It is recommended for the judge to encourage reconciliation. The commentary reconciles apparent contradictions by distinguishing between cases of contentment and anger.

Key Terms
الصلاحية (al-salahiyyah): Legal capacity or fitness; in li'an, it refers to the spouses being fit to perform the oath (yamin) as Muslims.
نفي النسب (nafi al-nasab): Denial of lineage (paternity); the husband's claim that a child is not his.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a husband denies paternity by saying 'this child is not from me' without mentioning zina?
A) Li'an is not wajib because explicit zina is required.
B) Li'an is wajib because denial of lineage implies zina.
C) Li'an is wajib only if the husband says it in anger.
D) Li'an is not wajib because the child may be from a previous marriage.

Key Takeaway
Li'an requires both spouses to be fit for oath; denial of lineage inherently implies zina and triggers li'an even without explicit accusation; the wife's right to demand li'an does not expire with time.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Denial of Lineage as Qadhf: The Hanafi Position on Li'an and Hadd
Expanding on condition for li'an and the ruling on nafi al-walad

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school considers denial of lineage (nafi al-walad) as qadhf triggering li'an, and distinguish between the conditions for the wife versus the husband.

Core Idea
Denying a child's lineage necessarily implies zina, so it triggers li'an even without explicit accusation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expands on a key condition for li'an: the wife must be 'chaste' (afifa) so that her accuser is liable for hadd. The commentator then delves into a disputed issue: whether a husband who simply says 'this child is not mine' must perform li'an, even if he does not mention zina. The Hanafi school's relied-upon view, supported by consensus, is that denial of lineage alone suffices because it inevitably implies zina. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the intra-madhhab disagreement, and the reconciliation offered by the commentator.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for the wife
Recognize that the wife must be 'one whose accuser is hadded' – meaning she is chaste (afifa) from zina. This adds to the general eligibility for testimony (freedom, Islam, legal capacity).
The condition of 'being haddable' is specifically about chastity; other conditions are already covered by eligibility to testify.
2
Differentiate the husband's condition
The husband is not required to be chaste; even a known fornicator can initiate li'an. He only needs eligibility to testify.
Li'an occurs between two fasiqs as well, as mentioned in the text.
3
Understand nafi al-walad as qadhf
Denial of lineage (e.g., 'this child is not from me') is legally equivalent to accusing the wife of zina. This is based on the fact that cutting off lineage necessarily implies zina.
The commentator adopts the absolute view (al-haqq al-itlaq) – no explicit mention of zina required.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute
Some Hanafi sources (al-Muhit, al-Muntagha) require explicit mention of zina. The commentator rebuts this by citing consensus (ijma') that denying lineage from a well-known father is qadhf against the mother.
The possibility of dubious intercourse (wat' bi shubha) is discarded by ijma'.
5
Evaluate the thamarah al-khilaf and reconciliation
Practical difference: a husband who says 'this child is not mine' must do li'an; a husband who says 'I found a man with her' does not (since intercourse does not necessitate zina). The commentator reconciles the conflicting views by context: the view requiring explicit zina applies to a state of contentment (rida), while the absolute view applies to anger (ghadab).
This reconciliation resolves an apparent contradiction in al-Nihayah and al-Dirayah.

وتفرع على هذا الشرط لو قذفها فتزوجت غيره فادعى الأول الولد لزمه حد للقذف وإن ولدت من الثاني لا شيء عليه إن كان قبل إكذاب الأول، وإن كان بعد الإكذاب لاعن كما في التتارخانية. ولما كانت المرأة هي المقذوفة دونه اختصت باشتراط كونها ممن يحد قاذفها بعد اشتراط أهلية الشهادة ولما كان الزوج ليس مقذوفاً وإنما هو شاهد اشترط في حقه كما اشترط في حقها أهلية الشهادة ولم تشترط عفته لأنه لو كان فاسقاً بالزنا جرى اللعان بينه وبينها وإن كان لا يحد قاذفه لما قدمنا من جريانه بين الفاسقين فهذا وجه تخصيصها بهذا الشرط كما حققه الشارح رداً على صاحب النهاية. وأراد بكونها ممن يحد قاذفها أن تكون عفيفة عن الزنا فقط لأن كونها من أهل الشهادة يدل على اشتراط الحرية والتكليف والإسلام فلم يبق من شرائط الإحصان إلا العفة كما أفاده في شرح الوقاية وأراد بنفي نسب الولد نفي نسب ولدها، وأطلقه فشمل ولدها منه أو من غيره بأن يقول هذا الولد من الزنا أو هذا الولد ليس مني وما إذا صرح معه بالزنا أو لم يصرح على مختار صاحب الهداية والشارح خلافاً لما في المحيط والمبتغى. والحق الإطلاق لأن قطع النسب من كل وجه يستلزم الزنا فلا عبرة باحتمال كون الولد من غيره بوطء بشبهة ولهذا قال في البدائع : هذا الاحتمال ساقط بالإجماع للإجماع على أنه إن نفاه عن الأب المشهور بأن قال له لست لأبيك يكون قاذفاً لأمه حتى يلزمه حد القذف مع وجود هذا الاحتمال وقد ظهر لي أن قول من قال لا يجب حد ولا لعان بنفي الولد عن أبيه إذا لم يصرح بالزنا محمول على حالة الرضا، وقول من أوجبه وإن لم يصرح به محمول على حالة الغضب وبه يندفع إلزام التناقض على صاحب النهاية والدراية . وإنما حملناه على ذلك لتصريحهم بالتفصيل في باب حد القذف - والله الموفق - بخلاف قوله وجدت معها رجلاً يجامعها فإنه ليس بقذف لأن الجماع لا يستلزم الزنا.
And branched from this condition: if he accused her of zina and she married another, and the first claimed the child, then he is obligated to the hadd for qadhf. If she gave birth from the second, nothing is upon him if it was before the first's self-confirmation of lying; if after the self-confirmation, he performs li'an, as in al-Tatarakhaniyyah. Since the woman is the one accused, not him, she is distinguished by the condition that she be one whose accuser is hadded, after stipulating eligibility for testimony. Since the husband is not accused but rather a witness, he is conditioned as she is conditioned with eligibility for testimony, and his 'iffah is not stipulated because if he were a fasiq due to zina, li'an would still occur between him and her even though his accuser would not be hadded, as we mentioned about li'an occurring between two fasiqs. This is the way of specifying her with this condition, as verified by the commentator in refutation of the author of al-Nihayah. What is meant by 'she is one whose accuser is hadded' is that she is only chaste from zina, because being among those eligible for testimony indicates stipulation of freedom, legal responsibility, and Islam, leaving nothing of the conditions of ihsan except chastity, as stated in Sharh al-Wiqayah. What is meant by 'denial of lineage of the child' is denial of the lineage of her child, and it is absolute, so it includes her child from him or from another. This is by saying 'this child is from zina' or 'this child is not from me', whether he explicitly mentions zina with it or not, according to the chosen view of the author of al-Hidayah and the commentator, contrary to what is in al-Muhit and al-Muntagha. The truth is the absolute view because cutting off lineage from every aspect necessitates zina, so no consideration is given to the possibility that the child is from another through dubious intercourse. For this reason, it is said in al-Bada'i': this possibility is discarded by consensus. Because by consensus, if he denies the child regarding the well-known father by saying 'you are not the son of your father', he becomes an accuser of his mother so that the hadd for qadhf is obligated on him despite this possibility. And it has become clear to me that the saying of whoever said 'no hadd and no li'an are obligated by denying lineage from the father if he does not explicitly mention zina' is interpreted as the case of contentment, and the saying of whoever obliged it even without explicit mention is interpreted as the case of anger. With this, the charge of contradiction against the author of al-Nihayah and al-Dirayah is repelled. We interpreted it that way because they explicitly detail it in the chapter of the hadd for qadhf. And Allah is the giver of success. Unlike his saying 'I found a man having intercourse with her', for this is not qadhf because intercourse does not necessitate zina.
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage is a detailed expansion of the conditions for li'an (mutual imprecation) and the ruling on denying lineage. The commentator begins by branching from the earlier condition that the woman must be such that her accuser would be liable for hadd of qadhf. He presents a scenario: if a man accuses his wife of zina, she then marries another, and the first husband later claims the child (from the second marriage) as his own, then he is liable for the hadd of qadhf (for the original accusation). If the second husband's wife gives birth and the first husband denies the child (i.e., claims it is not his), then if he had not already confessed to lying (ikdhab nafsih) about the original accusation, he must perform li'an; if he already confessed to lying, then li'an is not valid because he has already admitted to qadhf. The commentator then explains why the condition for the woman is stricter: she must be one whose accuser is hadded, meaning she must be 'afifa (chaste from zina). This is in addition to being eligible to testify (free, Muslim, adult). The husband is not required to be 'afif; even if he is known as a fornicator, li'an can still occur between them. The key point is that denying lineage (nafi al-walad) is considered qadhf even if the husband does not explicitly say 'zina'. The commentator prefers the view of al-Hidayah and the commentator (likely al-Marghinani and the author of al-Hidayah's commentary) over the view of al-Muhit and al-Muntagha, which require explicit mention. The proof is that denying lineage necessarily implies zina, and this is supported by ijma' (consensus): if a man says to a child 'you are not the son of your father', he is liable for hadd qadhf against the mother, even though the denial could be interpreted as the child being born from dubious intercourse. The commentator then reconciles the conflicting views by distinguishing between the state of contentment (rida) and anger (ghadab): in a state of contentment, denial without explicit zina may not trigger hadd/li'an, but in anger, it does. This resolves an apparent contradiction in al-Nihayah and al-Dirayah. Finally, the commentator notes that saying 'I found a man having intercourse with her' is not qadhf because intercourse does not necessarily mean zina (it could be through a dubious contract).

Key Terms
نفي الولد (nafi al-walad): The husband's statement denying that a child is his, which constitutes an implicit accusation of zina against the wife.
قذف (qadhf): Accusing a chaste person of zina or denying lineage, which incurs the hadd punishment.
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation between spouses when the husband accuses wife of zina without witnesses, involving specific oaths and curses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the basis for the absolute view that nafi al-walad alone triggers li'an?
A) The hadith 'al-walad lil-firash'
B) Consensus that denying lineage from a well-known father constitutes qadhf against the mother
C) Analogy to divorce
D) The Qur'anic verse on li'an

Key Takeaway
Denial of lineage (nafi al-walad) is legally equivalent to accusing the wife of zina and triggers the li'an procedure, even without explicit mention of zina.

Condition of Wife's Demand and Effect of Silence on Li'an
Detailing the requirement that the wife must demand li'an and the effect of her silence over time

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the condition that the wife must demand li'an in court and explain why her silence over time does not forfeit her right.

Core Idea
Silence does not nullify the wife's right to demand li'an; the passage of time does not invalidate the claim.

This passage from Bahr al-Raiq addresses a critical procedural point for li'an: the wife must personally demand the process in the judge's court. However, if she remains silent for a long period, she does not lose her right. The text expands on the wisdom of encouraging concealment and clarifies when li'an is no longer possible.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for li'an
The wife must demand li'an because it is her right to clear her name (deflect disgrace). The demand must be made in court.
For explicit qadhf, the wife's demand is required. For denial of lineage, the husband also has the right.
2
Distinguish the types of accusations
Explicit qadhf (accusation of zina) requires the wife's demand; nafi al-walad (denial of paternity) requires the husband's demand as well.
The phrase 'أما بنفي الولد فالطلب حقه أيضاً' indicates the husband's right.
3
Analyze the effect of silence
Silence does not invalidate the right even over a long period. Reason: passage of time does not nullify rights in qadhf and qisas, as cited from al-Ashbijabi.
The text says 'سكوتها لا يبطل حقها وإن طالت المدة'.
4
Appreciate the recommendation for concealment
It is better (afdal) for the wife to remain silent and for the judge to encourage her to drop the matter. However, if she later demands li'an, she retains her right. Exception: if the husband confesses to lying, then li'an is not available.
The addition from al-Jawharah and Khizanat al-Fiqh recommends concealment (satr).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقيد بطلبها لأنها لو لم تطالبه فلا لعان لأنه حقها لدفع العار عنها فيشترط طلبها، ولا بد من كونه في مجلس القاضي ؛ كذا في البدائع ومراده طلبها إذا كان القذف بصريح أما بنفي الولد فالطلب حقه أيضاً لاحتياجه إلى نفي من ليس ولده عنه. وأشار بعدم اشتراط الفور في الطلب إلى أن سكوتها لا يبطل حقها وإن طالت المدة لأن تقادم الزمان لا بطلان الحق في القذف والقصاص كما ذكره الأسبيجابي. وزاد في الجوهرة وحقوق العباد، وفي خزانة الفقه، ولو سكتت ولم ترفع إلى الحاكم كان أفضل وينبغي للحاكم أن يقول لها اتركي وأعرضي عن هذا لأنه دعاء إلى الستر فإن تركت مدة ثم خاصمت فلها ذلك كما في ليس له أب معروف فكان شبهة الزنا، أما لو كان بعدما أكذب نفسه فالشبهة منتفية فيلا عن الزوج الثاني تأمل .
And it is conditioned by her demand because if she does not demand it, there is no li'an, because it is her right to repel disgrace from herself, so her demand is stipulated. It must be in the court of the judge; as in al-Bada'i'. What is meant is her demand when the qadhf is explicit. As for denial of lineage, the demand is his right as well because he needs to deny from himself one who is not his child. He indicated by not stipulating immediacy in the demand that her silence does not nullify her right even if the period is long, because the passage of time does not nullify the right in qadhf and qisas, as mentioned by al-Asbijabi. And it is added in al-Jawharah and Huquq al-'Ibad, and in Khizanat al-Fiqh: if she remains silent and does not raise it to the judge, it is better. It is befitting for the judge to say to her: 'Leave it and turn away from this' because it invites concealment. If she leaves it for a period then disputes, she has that right, as in the case of one who has no known father, so it is a doubt (shubha) of zina. But if it is after he has confessed himself to be lying, then the doubt is removed, so no li'an for the second husband. Consider (ta'ammul).
Source pages p. 191

Commentary
This passage establishes that li'an is only initiated at the demand of the wife when the accusation is explicit qadhf. It is her right to clear her name, so she must request it. The demand must be made in the judge's court. For denial of lineage, the husband also has the right to demand li'an because he needs to disown a child that is not his. Importantly, the wife's silence over time does not forfeit her right to demand li'an later; the passage of time does not invalidate claims in cases of qadhf or qisas (retaliation). In fact, it is recommended (afdal) that she remain silent and not take the matter to court, and the judge should encourage her to do so, as it leads to covering (satr) of sins. However, if the husband has already confessed to lying (akdhaba nafsahu), then the possibility of zina is removed, and thus no li'an is needed. The text ends with 'ta'ammul' (consider), indicating the need for reflection on a nuance.

Key Terms
الطلب (al-talab): The demand by the wife (or husband) for the procedure of li'an, which must be made in court.
السكوت (al-sukut): The wife's silence and failure to immediately demand li'an; does not invalidate her right.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Yes, because the passage of time does not invalidate the right in qadhf.
C) Only if she has a valid excuse for the delay.
D) She must first obtain a renewal of the accusation from the judge.

Key Takeaway
The wife's right to demand li'an is not lost by silence; it is permanent until the matter is resolved, except if the husband confesses to lying before the procedure.

Scenarios of Li'an and Hadd When Witnesses Are Brought
Detailed expansion of witness scenarios affecting li'an and hadd.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions that trigger or avert li'an when witnesses are brought, and identify the rulings for various combinations of witnesses and accusations.

Core Idea
Li'an is averted when the husband brings sufficient witnesses to zina or when the wife confirms his accusation, but the details are intricate.

This lesson explores the detailed scenarios from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on how the presence of witnesses affects the obligation of li'an and the application of hadd penalties. Understanding these branches is essential for a judge or mufti dealing with accusations of zina.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditions for li'an obligation
The passage states that li'an becomes wajib only when the husband is unable to produce four male witnesses to the wife's zina, he has not confessed to lying (ikdhab al-nafs), and the wife does not confirm his accusation. Determine whether these conditions are met in a given scenario.
These three conditions are prerequisites for li'an to be wajib.
2
Classify the witness scenarios
Analyze the different witness configurations: four male witnesses (full proof of zina), two male witnesses on the wife's confession (insufficient for zina but averts li'an), and one man with two women testifying to the wife's confirmation (no hadd, no li'an). For each, state the ruling.
The number and gender of witnesses matter critically.
3
Analyze the husband's own testimony and children's testimony
When the husband testifies along with three other witnesses (without having previously accused her), his testimony is accepted, and he must perform li'an. If the witnesses are non-just, no hadd or li'an. Two children testifying against their father for accusing their stepmother is accepted only if the father has already been hadded.
The husband's testimony counts as a witness, not an accusation.
4
Evaluate composite accusation and priority of punishments
When an accusation targets both the wife and her mother (e.g., 'O zaniyah, daughter of a zaniyah'), hadd for the mother's accusation is executed first, dropping the need for li'an. If the mother does not demand, li'an is done first, then hadd after. The general rule: when two conflicts collide, begin with the one that drops the other.
Al-Tahawi's view that no hadd after li'an is rejected; the apparent narration allows both.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يخفى أن وجوب اللعان مقيد بعجزه عن إقامه البينة على زناها وعدم إكذاب نفسه بعده وعدم تصديقها له فإن أقام بينة على زناها فإن كانوا أربعة رجال رجمت لو محصنة، وجلدت لو غير محصنة، وإن كانا رجلين فقط على إقرارها بالزنا يندرئ اللعان ولا تحد المرأة، وكذا لو كانا رجلاً وامرأتين شهدوا على تصديقها فلا حد عليهما ولا لعان. وهذا كله إذا أقر بالقذف، فإن أنكره فأقامت رجلين وجب اللعان لا رجلاً وامرأتين وإن لم يكن لها بينة لا يستحلف الزوج ؛ ذكره الإمام الأسبيجابي رحمه الله. وتقبل شهادة الزوج على زناها مع ثلاثة إن لم يكن قذفها وإلا فلا تقبل وتحد الثلاثة حد القذف ويلاعن الزوج ولو لم يقذفها وشهد مع ثلاثة غير عدول فلا حد عليه ولا على الثلاثة ولا لعان؛ كذا في المحيط . وفيه أيضاً : ولو شهدا على أبيهما أنه قذف ضرة أمهما لا تقبل لأنهما بشهادتهما يشهدان لأمهما بخلوص الفراش لها لأن اللعان سبب الفرقة حتى لو كان أبوهما محدوداً في تقبل لأن هذا القذف أن لا اللعان للحد دون اللعان قال : ولا بد في وجوب موجب يقذف أمها فلو قال لها يا زانية بنت الزانية وجب الحد لقذف أمها واللعان لقذفها فإن اجتمعا على المطالبة بدأ بحده ليسقط اللعان بخروجه عن أهلية الشهادة وإن لم تطالب الأم وطالبته اللعان ويحد للأم بطلبها بعده في ظاهر الرواية. وذكر الطحاوي أنه لا يحد بعد اللعان وهذا غير سديد لعدم المانع من إقامته وإن كانت أمها ميتة فلها المطالبة بهما، فإن خاصمته فيهما بدأ بالحد ليسقط اللعان، وإن بدأت بالخصومة لنفسها وجب اللعان ثم لها المطالبة بقذف أمها فيحد له. وعلى هذا التفصيل لو قدف أجنبيه بالزنا ثم نكحها ثم قذفها فلها المطالبة باللعان والحد ؛ كذا في البدائع والحاصل أنه إذا اجتمع قذفان وفي تقديم أحدهما إسقاط الآخر بدأ بالمسقط كما إذا قذفها وقذفته فإنه يبدأ بحدها ليسقط اللعان الحد كما سيأتي في باب حد القذف.
And it is not hidden that the obligation of li'an is conditioned by his inability to establish evidence of her zina, his not confessing himself to be lying afterwards, and her not believing him. If he brings evidence of her zina: if the witnesses are four men, she is stoned if she is muhsana and flogged if not. If they are only two men upon her confession of zina, li'an is averted and the woman is not hadded. Similarly, if they are one man and two women testifying to her confirmation, there is no hadd on them and no li'an. All this is if he confesses to the qadhf. If he denies it, and she brings two men, li'an is obligatory, not one man and two women. If she has no evidence, the husband is not sworn (yastahlif). Mentioned by Imam al-Asbijabi. The testimony of the husband about her zina is accepted along with three others if he did not accuse her; otherwise, it is not accepted, and the three are hadded for qadhf, and the husband performs li'an. Even if he did not accuse her and testifies with three non-just witnesses, there is no hadd on him or on the three, and no li'an; as in al-Muhit. Also in it: if two testify against their father that he accused their stepmother (durrah) of zina, it is not accepted because by their testimony they testify for their mother to clear the bed for her, because li'an is a cause of separation. Even if their father is hadded, it is accepted because this qadhf leads to hadd, not li'an. He said: there must be a cause necessitating the effect. If he says to her, 'O you zaniyah, daughter of a zaniyah,' the hadd is obligatory for accusing her mother and li'an for accusing her. If both demand together, he begins with her hadd so that li'an is dropped because he becomes disqualified from testimony. If the mother does not demand and she demands li'an, he does li'an, and then the hadd for the mother is done at her demand after that, according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah). Al-Tahawi mentioned that he is not hadded after li'an, but this is not sound because there is no impediment to establishing it. Even if her mother is dead, she can demand both. If she litigates both, she begins with hadd to drop li'an. If she begins with litigation for herself, li'an is obligatory, then she can demand hadd for her mother's qadhf, and he is hadded. On this detail, if he accused an alien woman of zina then married her then accused her, she can demand both li'an and hadd; as in al-Bada'i'. The summary: if two qadhfs are combined and presenting one drops the other, he begins with the dropper, as if he accused her and she accused him: he begins with her hadd to drop his li'an due to hadd, as will come in the chapter of the hadd for qadhf.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage covers the interplay between witnesses, li'an, and hadd punishments. The obligation of li'an is conditioned by the husband's inability to produce four male witnesses to his wife's zina, his not having confessed to lying, and his wife's denial of his accusation. If he brings four male witnesses, she receives the full hadd for zina (stoning if muhsana, flogging if not). If he brings only two men (insufficient for zina), and the wife confesses to zina, li'an is averted and she is not hadded for zina (since confession requires four? Actually two witnesses plus her confession may suffice to avert li'an). If he brings one man and two women (the women are not accepted in hadd cases), and they testify that the wife confirmed the zina, still no hadd and no li'an. The next part discusses when the husband denies making the accusation (i.e., he says he did not accuse her of zina). In that case, if the wife brings two male witnesses to prove that he did accuse her, li'an becomes obligatory. One man and two women are not sufficient because li'an involves hadd-like elements. If the wife cannot produce evidence, the husband is not put under oath. The passage then addresses the husband's own testimony: if he testifies along with three other (male) witnesses that his wife committed zina, and he himself did not previously accuse her (i.e., he is a witness, not an accuser), then his testimony is accepted, the three other witnesses are not hadded for qadhf, and the husband himself must perform li'an (since his own testimony counts as one of the four? Actually the logic is that if he acts as a witness, he avoids being a qadhif, but still implicates himself in the accusation, so li'an is needed). If he testifies with three non-just (ghayr 'udul) witnesses, there is no hadd on anyone and no li'an. The passage then gives a detailed scenario: two children testify that their father accused their stepmother (the mother's co-wife) of zina. Their testimony is not accepted because they are testifying for their mother's benefit (to clear the bed for her, since li'an would cause separation). However, if the father had already been hadded for qadhf (i.e., he was punished for the accusation), then their testimony is accepted because the hadd has been applied and the purpose is not li'an but just evidence. The passage then discusses a composite accusation: 'O zaniyah, daughter of a zaniyah!' This contains two qadhfs: one against the wife and one against her mother. If both demand punishment, the hadd for the mother is executed first, because that disqualified the husband from testimony, thus dropping the li'an. If only the mother demands, the husband does li'an with the wife, then the mother's hadd is done later. Al-Tahawi's view that no hadd after li'an is rejected. If the mother is dead, the daughter can demand both. If she starts with her own case, li'an happens first, then hadd for the mother. The same principle applies if he accused an alien woman, then married her, then accused her again: she can demand both hadd (for pre-marriage qadhf) and li'an (for post-marriage qadhf). The general rule: when two punishments conflict and one drops the other, the one that drops the other is performed first (e.g., wife's hadd for qadhf drops husband's li'an).

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): Legal evidence, typically witnesses, required to prove zina (four men) or other matters.
إكذاب النفس (ikdhab al-nafs): The husband's confession that he lied in his accusation, which nullifies the need for li'an and subjects him to hadd for qadhf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) The husband is hadded for qadhf.

Key Takeaway
The obligation of li'an is intricately linked to the availability and credibility of witnesses, and multiple accusations require careful ordering.

Compelling the Husband to Perform Li'an: Imprisonment as a Legal Sanction
Explaining the consequence of the husband's refusal to perform li'an and the imprisonment until compliance or confession

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling that the husband is imprisoned if he refuses to perform li'an, and identify the legal rationale involving cause (sabab) and condition (shart).

Core Idea
If a husband refuses li'an, he is imprisoned until he performs it or confesses to lying.

In the previous lesson, we studied the procedure of li'an. But what happens when the husband simply refuses? This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that the court does not leave the matter unresolved. Instead, it compels the husband through imprisonment until he either fulfills his obligation to perform li'an or confesses to slander (qadhf), which then triggers the hadd punishment. The commentator also clarifies the legal theory: qadhf is the cause, and mutual accusation (takadhib) is the condition. Let us unpack the legal mechanics.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for refusal
The base text states: if the husband refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an or confesses to lying (which then incurs hadd).
This is a coercive measure, not a punishment for refusal itself.
2
Understand the rationale
The commentator explains that li'an is a right due upon the husband and he is capable of fulfilling it, so imprisonment is valid to compel performance.
Imprisonment continues until the right is fulfilled, not for a fixed term.
3
Distinguish sabab and shart
The commentator provides a tahqiq: qadhf (slander) is the cause (sabab) that makes li'an necessary, while takadhib (mutual accusation) is the condition (shart) for the procedure to begin.
This precision helps avoid confusion in legal reasoning.
4
Note the evidentiary correction
The passage corrects an error from another source: for hadd cases, the required witnesses are two men, not one man and two women, since women's testimony is not accepted in hadd.
This is a separate point but shows the commentator's attention to detail.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن أبى حبس حتى يلاعن أو يكذب نفسه فيحد) لأنه حق مستحق عليه وهو قادر على إيفائه فيحبس حتى يأتي بما هو عليه أو يكذب نفسه ليرتفع السبب في اللعان التكاذب هكذا قالوا . والتحقيق أن القذف هو السبب فإن التكاذب شرط . قيد وجوب الحد رجلاً وامرأتين لأنه حد ولا تقبل شهادة النساء في الحدود كما في كافي الحاكم وغيره فقوله في النهر أو رجلاً وامرأتين سبق قلم.
His saying: 'If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an or confesses himself to be lying, then he is hadded.' Because it is a right due upon him, and he is able to fulfill it, so he is imprisoned until he does what is upon him or confesses himself to be lying so that the cause is removed. In li'an, the mutual accusation (takadhib) is the condition. Thus they said. The investigation (tahqiq) is that qadhf is the cause, and takadhib is the condition. He restricted the obligation of hadd to two men or one man and two women because it is a hadd, and the testimony of women is not accepted in hadd cases, as in Kafi al-Hakim and others. So his saying in al-Nahr 'or one man and two women' is a slip of the pen.
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage explains the legal mechanism when the husband refuses to perform li'an. The base text (likely Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states: 'If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an or confesses to lying, then he is hadded.' The commentator explains that this is because li'an is a right due upon him (the husband's duty to clear the accusation) and he is capable of fulfilling it. Therefore, the court compels him through imprisonment. He can either perform li'an or admit he falsely accused his wife (which incurs the hadd for qadhf). The commentator then provides a tahqiq (investigation): the cause (sabab) of li'an is the qadhf itself, while the mutual accusation (takadhib) is a condition (shart) for the procedure. This clarifies the legal theory. The final note corrects an error in a previous source: in hadd cases, women's testimony is not accepted; therefore, evidence for hadd requires two men, not one man and two women. The mention of 'one man and two women' in al-Nahr is considered a scribal error.

Key Terms
الحبس (al-habs): Imprisonment by the judge to compel the husband to perform li'an or confess to qadhf.
التكاذب (al-takadhib): The mutual accusation between spouses: the husband accuses and the wife denies; this is a condition for li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position in this passage, what happens if a husband who accused his wife of zina refuses to perform li'an and also refuses to confess to lying?
A) The wife is divorced immediately.
B) The husband is imprisoned until he performs li'an or confesses.
C) The case is dismissed after a certain period.
D) The wife is given the right to divorce herself.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school imposes imprisonment on a husband who refuses li'an, as a coercive measure to enforce his wajib duty, until he either performs the li'an oaths or confesses to slander.
