Conditions for Li'an and Its Consequences
Exposition of Hanafi rulings on li'an procedure and consequences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which li'an becomes wajib and describe the consequences for both spouses.

Core Idea
Li'an is wajib when a husband accuses his wife of zina without four witnesses.

The passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that li'an is not automatic; it is conditioned on the husband's inability to produce evidence. This lesson will walk through the key conditions and what happens if the husband can produce witnesses, if he cannot, and the role of the wife's response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Li'an is a mutual imprecation procedure. Its ruling is wajib under specific conditions.
It is not a punishment but a mechanism to avoid hadd.
2
List the conditions for wajib li'an
The husband must accuse his wife of zina without four witnesses, he must not retract, and the wife must not confirm his accusation.
Confirmation by the wife drops the need for li'an but does not impose punishment on her.
3
Explain the consequences if husband produces evidence
If he brings four upright witnesses, the wife is stoned (if muhsan) or flogged. No li'an.
If fewer than four, li'an may still apply depending on the case.
4
Explain the consequences if husband cannot produce evidence
He must perform li'an. If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he does or retracts (then punished for qadhf). After his li'an, the wife must perform li'an or be imprisoned.
The wife's refusal leads to imprisonment, not flogging, per Hanafi interpretation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

اللعان
قوله : (إنهما يحبسان إذا امتنعا الخ) قال في النهر : وعندي في حبسها بعد امتناعه نوع إشكال وهذا لأنه لا يجب عليها إلا بعده فقبله ليس امتناعاً لحق وجب وكأن هذا هو السر في إغفال المصنف البحر الرائق ج ٤/ م ١٣
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Li'an. From al-Bada'i'. It is not hidden that the obligation of li'an is conditioned upon his inability to produce evidence of her zina, and his not contradicting himself afterwards, and her not confirming him. If he produces evidence of her zina, if they are four men, she is stoned if muhsanah, and flogged if non-muhsanah; if only two men, based on her confession of zina, li'an is averted and the woman is not punished; likewise if two men and two women testify to her confirmation, then no punishment on them and no li'an. All this is if he confesses to qadhf; if he denies it, and she produces two men, li'an is obligatory, not one man and two women. If she has no evidence, the husband is not made to take an oath, mentioned by Imam al-Asbijabi. The testimony of the husband regarding her zina with three [others] is accepted if he did not accuse her; otherwise it is not accepted and the three are punished with the punishment of qadhf, and the husband performs li'an. If he did not accuse her and testified with three non-upright [witnesses], then no punishment on him nor on the three, and no li'an; as in al-Muhit. Also in it: If two testify against their father that he accused their stepmother of zina, it is not accepted because by their testimony they testify for their mother to free the bed for her, because li'an is a cause of separation; so even if their father was punished, it would be accepted because this qadhf is not li'an but punishment without li'an. He said: It is necessary for the obligation of the cause that he accuses her mother; so if he said to her: 'O adulteress, daughter of an adulteress,' punishment is obligatory for accusing her mother and li'an for accusing her. If both demand, he starts with punishment to drop li'an by his loss of eligibility for testimony; if the mother does not demand and she demands li'an, he is punished for the mother upon her demand afterward in the apparent narration. Al-Tahawi mentioned that he is not punished after li'an, but this is unsound due to the absence of an impediment to establishing it. Even if her mother is dead, she has the right to demand both. If she litigates for both, he starts with punishment to drop li'an; if she starts with litigation for herself, li'an is obligatory, then she has the right to demand for accusing her mother, and he is punished accordingly. And on this detail, if he accused a foreign woman of zina, then married her, then accused her, she has the right to demand li'an and punishment; as in al-Bada'i'. The conclusion: when two accusations gather and prioritizing one drops the other, he starts with the one that drops the other, as if he accused her and she accused him, he starts with her punishment to drop li'an, as will come in the chapter on the punishment of qadhf. In al-Muhit: If he said to her: 'You are thrice divorced, O adulteress,' punishment is obligatory and no li'an; if he said: 'O adulteress, you are thrice divorced,' then no punishment and no li'an. And if he said: 'I accused you before marrying you,' or 'you committed zina before I married you,' it is a current accusation, so he performs li'an. What is in Khizanat al-Akmal that he performs li'an for saying 'you committed zina' and is punished for saying 'I accused you before marrying you' is a [؟] possibility; as in Fath al-Qadir. His saying: 'If he refuses, he is imprisoned until he performs li'an or accuses himself and is punished' because it is a right owed to him and he is able to fulfill it, so he is imprisoned until he does what is upon him or accuses himself to remove the cause. In li'an the cause is mutual denial; thus they said. But the verification is that qadhf is the cause, and mutual denial is a condition. The restriction of the obligation of punishment to a man and two women is because it is a punishment and women's testimony is not accepted in punishments, as in Kafi al-Hakim and others; so his saying in al-Nahr 'or a man and two women' is a slip of the pen. Or he accuses himself and is punished. If he performs li'an, li'an becomes obligatory upon her; if she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms him, by the denial of obligation by mere refusal from li'an, and this is what is mentioned in the apparent narration as stated by al-Hakim in al-Kafi. By this it is known that what al-Walwaliji mentioned about the obligation of punishment upon him by mere refusal is an error and not the madhhab of our companions, and carrying it to be the saying of some shaykhs is far-fetched because it depends on transmission, and because al-Walwaliji mentioned that if she refuses after his li'an, she is punished with the punishment of zina, and our companions did not say that, as we will clarify. His saying: 'If he performs li'an, li'an becomes obligatory upon her' as we have presented; it shows that her li'an is postponed after his li'an because he is in the position of a witness against her by his accusation, and she by her testimony drops what he has established against her of zina, so she cannot begin [li'an] just as the defendant cannot begin with what drops the claim. It is sound in Sharh al-Aqta'. In al-Ikhtiyar: If the woman begins first, then the husband repeats it to be in the prescribed order; if they separate before repetition, it is permissible because the purpose is the mutual imprecation and it has occurred. His saying: 'If she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms him' as we have presented. He did not say 'or confirms him and is punished for zina' as occurred in some copies of al-Quduri because it is an error, since the punishment is not obliged by one confession, so how is it obliged by one confirmation? And it is not obliged by four confirmations because confirmation is not a confession by intent, so it is not considered for obligation but considered for averting [punishment] to remove li'an, and punishment is not obliged by it. If she confirms him regarding the negation of the child, there is no punishment and no li'an, and the child is theirs because they cannot intentionally nullify his right, and lineage is only negated by li'an, which has not occurred. By this it becomes clear that what was said in Sharh al-Wiqayah and followed by the commentator of al-Niqayah that if she confirms him, the lineage of her child from him is negated, is incorrect, as pointed out in Sharh al-Durar wa al-Ghurrar. The author did not mention the ruling if both refuse li'an after they have resorted to judgment. Al-Asbijabi stated in Sharh al-Tahawi that both are imprisoned if they refuse li'an after affirmation, and it should be understood as when the woman does not forgive; if she forgives, then they are not imprisoned, as if the accused forgives, for even if we say forgiveness is not valid in the punishment of qadhf and li'an, they are only established by demand, as we will clarify in the chapter on punishment of qadhf. If you say: The apparent meaning of the verse supports al-Shafi'i who says that if she refuses li'an, she is punished with the punishment of zina, and it is His saying: 'And it averts from her the punishment if she testifies' (al-Nur: 8), meaning the punishment because the definite article indicates the previously mentioned punishment, which is the punishment. We say: What is meant is imprisonment, like His saying in the verse of the hoopoe: 'I will punish him severely' (al-Naml: 21), and it came in the tafsir: 'I will imprison him.' The difference is built on the fact that the basis in accusing wives according to al-Shafi'i is the punishment, acting on the first verse: 'And those who accuse chaste women and then do not bring four witnesses, flog them' (al-Nur: 4). And it is explained by the verse of li'an that if the accuser is a husband, he can avert the punishment from himself by li'an, and if the accused is the wife of the accuser, she can avert the punishment of zina from herself by her li'an. So whichever of them refuses the li'an... His saying: 'Both are imprisoned if they refuse, etc.' Al-Nahr said: I have some hesitation about imprisoning her after his refusal, because it is not obligatory upon her except after his [li'an], so before that it is not a refusal of an obligation that has become due. And this is perhaps the secret behind the author's omission [of mentioning this case]. (Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, vol. 4, p. 13)
Source pages p. 192

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the chapter of Li'an. It begins by clarifying that the obligation of li'an (mutual imprecation) is conditional upon the husband's inability to produce four male witnesses to his wife's zina, his not retracting his accusation, and the wife's not confirming his accusation. If the husband can produce four witnesses, the wife is stoned if she is muhsan (married) or flogged if not. If only two witnesses come forward, and the wife confesses, li'an is averted and the wife is not punished. Similarly, if two men and two women witness the wife's confirmation, no punishment or li'an occurs. These rulings apply only if the husband admits to making a false accusation (qadhf). If he denies making the accusation, and the wife produces two male witnesses, li'an becomes obligatory. However, if she produces only one man and two women, li'an is not obligatory. If the wife has no witnesses, the husband is not required to take an oath. The testimony of the husband against his wife regarding zina is accepted only if he did not previously accuse her; otherwise, he and his three witnesses are punished for qadhf, and the husband must also perform li'an. There is a discussion about cases where multiple accusations are involved: if a husband accuses his wife and also her mother, the punishment for the mother takes precedence if both demand, because after the punishment the husband becomes ineligible to testify and li'an is dropped. After performing li'an, the husband may still be punished for accusing the mother if she demands it. If the wife refuses to perform li'an after her husband has done so, she is imprisoned until she either performs li'an or confirms his accusation. The commentary also addresses a potential objection from the Shafi'i school: according to the verse 'and it averts from her the punishment' (24:8), the 'punishment' referred to is the hadd punishment for zina, implying that if she refuses li'an, she should be flogged. The Hanafi response is that 'punishment' here means imprisonment, as in the verse about the hoopoe where 'punishment' is interpreted as imprisonment. The difference stems from the Shafi'i view that the default for accusing one's wife is the hadd punishment, which can be averted by li'an. In the Hanafi view, the default is not punishment but the obligation of li'an. Finally, there is a note about imprisonment when both parties refuse: the author of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq expresses some doubt about imprisoning the wife before the husband performs li'an, as her obligation only arises after his. This might explain why the original author (al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah) omitted this detail.

Key Terms
لعان (li'an): Mutual imprecation: a procedure where the husband and wife take oaths invoking Allah's curse if they are lying, used when a husband accuses his wife of zina without four witnesses.
قذف (qadhf): False accusation of zina against a chaste person, which entails a hadd punishment of 80 lashes.
حد (hadd): Fixed punishment prescribed by Sharia for specific crimes, such as flogging for qadhf or for zina.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what happens to the wife if she refuses to perform li'an after the husband has done so?
A) She is flogged 80 lashes for zina.
B) She is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms the accusation.
C) She is divorced immediately.
D) She is required to pay compensation.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is a specific procedure that replaces the hadd of qadhf when a husband accuses his wife without witnesses.

Consequences of Refusing Li'an: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Hanafi ruling on wife's refusal of li'an and dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a wife refuses li'an after her husband's li'an, explain the Shafi'i objection, and evaluate the Hanafi response based on Quranic interpretation and abrogation.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, refusal to perform li'an results in imprisonment, not flogging, because the specific li'an verses abrogate the general hadd verses for spouses.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a key point of difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: what happens when a wife refuses to perform li'an after her husband has done so? The Hanafi school holds that she is imprisoned until she either performs li'an or confirms his accusation, while the Shafi'i school says she must be flogged for zina. The disagreement turns on the interpretation of the word 'al-‘adhāb' in the li'an verses and the principle of abrogation (naskh). Let us examine the textual reasoning behind each position.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi ruling on wife's refusal
Identify the exact ruling from the passage: if she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms (ikdhāb). No hadd is imposed because confirmation is not a legal admission (iqrār).
2
Identify the Shafi'i counter-position
The Shafi'i school argues that if she refuses, she should be flogged for zina, based on their interpretation of 'العذاب' in the verse as hadd and their view that the general verse on slander (24:4) still applies to spouses.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof from Quranic interpretation
The Hanafis interpret 'العذاب' in Q. 24:8 as 'imprisonment', citing the usage in Q. 27:21 (story of Hudhud) where 'أعذبنه' is explained in tafsir as 'أحبسنه'. This is a key linguistic argument.
This is a dalīl naqlī based on the Arabic usage of the word.
4
Analyze the Hanafi proof from abrogation (naskh)
The Hanafis hold that the li'an verses (Q. 24:6-9) abrogate the general hadd verse (Q. 24:4) for spouses because the specific later revelation limits the general earlier rule. Hence, the original obligation of hadd is replaced by li'an, and refusal does not revert to hadd but to compulsion (imprisonment).
The principle: 'al-khāss al-muta'akhkhir yansakhu al-‘āmm'. Also cited is the hadith of Hilāl where the Prophet initially threatened hadd before revelation of li'an verses.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The practical outcome of the dispute: under Hanafi law, the wife is imprisoned; under Shafi'i law, she is flogged. The Hanafi position is the relied-upon (muftā bihi) ruling.

وهو لا يجب بالتصديق أربع مرات لأن التصديق ليس بإقرار قصداً فلا يعتبر في حق وجوب ويعتبر في درئه ليندفع به اللعان ولا يجب به الحد ولو صدقته في نفي الولد فلا حد ولا وهو ولدهما لأنهما لا يملكان إبطال حقه قصداً، والنسب إنما ينتفي باللعان ولم يوجد. وبهذا ظهر أن ما قاله في شرح الوقاية وتبعه شارح النقاية من أنها إذا صدقته ينتفي نسب ولدها منه غير صحيح كما نبه عليه في شرح الدرر والغرر. ولم يذكر المؤلف حكم الله ﷺ: البينة وإلا حد في ظهرك، فدل على أنه كان في الحد كقذف الأجنبيات ثم لما نزلت آية اللعان انتسخ في حق الزوجات كما في البدائع والعناية.
Book of Divorce, Chapter of Li'an. Or he accuses himself so he is flogged; if he performs li'an, li'an becomes obligatory on her; if she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms him with false accusation because it is not obligatory by mere refusal from li'an, and this is what is mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah as al-Hakim stated in al-Kafi. By this it is known that what al-Walwaliji mentioned about obligation of hadd upon him by mere refusal is an oversight, not a madhhab of our companions... His saying: (If he performed li'an, li'an becomes obligatory on her) because her li'an is subsequent to his li'an... His saying: (If she refuses, she is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms him) as we have stated. He did not say 'or confirms him so she is flogged for zina' as occurs in some copies of al-Quduri because it is an error... If you say: The apparent verse supports al-Shafi'i who says that if she refuses li'an she is flogged for zina, as His statement 'and the punishment is averted from her' [an-Nur: 8] meaning the hadd because the lam is for previous reference, i.e., the previously mentioned punishment which is hadd. We say: What is meant is imprisonment, as His statement in the verse of the hoopoe 'I will surely punish him' [an-Naml: 21] and it came in tafsir 'I will surely imprison him'... According to us, the verse of li'an abrogates the first verse with respect to spouses because the specific later than the general abrogates the general to its extent, so the first verse no longer includes spouses, so the obligation upon slandering a spouse is li'an, so whichever of them refrains from it is imprisoned until he performs it, like the debtor who refrains from fulfilling a right upon him.
Source pages p. 193

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafis and Shafi'is regarding the consequence of a wife's refusal to perform li'an after her husband has performed it. The Hanafi position, as stated in the base text, is that she is imprisoned until she either performs li'an or confirms his accusation. The author clarifies that if she confirms, she does not face hadd because confirmation is not the same as admission (iqrar). The author refutes a statement by Al-Walwaliji who claimed that hadd is obligatory upon mere refusal. The core of the dispute is the interpretation of the verse 'ويدرأ عنها العذاب' (Q. 24:8). The Shafi'is interpret 'العذاب' as hadd, while the Hanafis interpret it as imprisonment, citing the usage in the story of Hudhud (Q. 27:21) where 'أعذبنه' means imprisonment. The Hanafi reasoning is based on abrogation: the general verse on flogging for slander (Q. 24:4) is abrogated by the specific verse on li'an (Q. 24:6-9) for the case of spouses. Thus, the original obligation of hadd is replaced by li'an, and refusal leads to imprisonment to compel its performance, similar to a debtor who refuses to pay. The hadith of Hilal ibn Umayyah is cited as evidence that before the revelation of the li'an verses, the Prophet ﷺ told him to bring evidence or face hadd, showing that the general ruling applied until abrogation.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li'ān): Mutual invocation of curses between spouses when husband accuses wife of adultery without witnesses, as per Quran 24:6-9.
العذاب (al-ʿadhāb): In the context of li'an verses, interpreted by Hanafis as imprisonment, not flogging.
الإكذاب (al-ikdhāb): The wife's confirmation of the husband's accusation, which negates li'an and does not incur hadd.
الناسخ والمنسوخ (al-nāsikh wa al-mansūkh): The principle that a later revelation abrogates an earlier one. Here, li'an verses abrogate the hadd verse for spouses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) She is imprisoned until she performs li'an or confirms the accusation.
C) The marriage is dissolved immediately.
D) She is given a warning only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that refusal to perform li'an results in imprisonment, not flogging, based on the interpretation of 'العذاب' as imprisonment and the abrogation of the general hadd verse by the specific li'an verses for spouses.

When Hadd for Qadhf Replaces Li'an: Husband's Witness Eligibility
Rulings on hadd when li'an is impossible due to husband's disqualification as a witness

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions under which hadd for qadhf becomes wajib when li'an is impossible due to the husband's disqualification as a witness, and apply the principle that the cause of li'an's failure determines the obligation of hadd.

Core Idea
Hadd for qadhf replaces li'an only when the husband's own lack of witness eligibility prevents li'an, but his slander is legally valid.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key Hanafi rule: li'an is the default mechanism for a husband who accuses his wife of zina without witnesses. However, if the husband cannot perform li'an because he is not a fit witness (e.g., slave, hadd-punished for qadhf, or disbeliever), the original punishment for slander—hadd—becomes wajib. But this only applies if his slander itself is valid (i.e., he is not a minor or insane). The text also explores cases involving the wife's eligibility and an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf between Abu Yusuf and Zufar.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act under discussion? It is the husband's accusation of zina against his wife (qadhf). When li'an is impossible due to a reason from the husband's side, the ruling shifts from li'an to hadd (flogging for false accusation) — provided the slander itself is legally valid.
The key distinction: li'an is a special oath procedure; if it cannot be performed due to the husband's fault, we revert to the general punishment for slander.
2
Determine the principle (الضابط)
The author states: 'إذا تعذر اللعان لمعنى من جهته، فإن كان القذف صحيحاً وجب الحد عليه، وإن لم يكن القذف صحيحاً فلا حد ولا لعان.' This principle governs all cases: if li'an fails due to a reason from the husband's side, and the slander was valid (i.e., the husband is legally capable of committing slander), then hadd is obligatory. If the slander is invalid (e.g., husband is minor or insane), no hadd and no li'an.
This principle is from al-Bada'i, a foundational Hanafi text.
3
Apply the principle to specific scenarios
The text applies this to: husband is a slave, hadd-punished for qadhf, or a disbeliever who slanders after his wife's conversion but before being invited to Islam → hadd is wajib. If husband is a minor or insane → no hadd (and no li'an) because his slander is not valid.
These scenarios illustrate that the cause of li'an's failure (husband's disqualification) combined with valid slander triggers hadd.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar regarding a case where a disbelieving husband slanders his wife after she converts, then some hadd is carried out, and then he converts. Abu Yusuf says: complete the rest of hadd, then they perform li'an. Zufar says: no li'an at all. The mufta bihi is Abu Yusuf's view.
This shows the importance of whether the obstacle (kufr) is removed during the process.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن لم يصلح شاهداً (حد) لأنه لما تعذر اللعان لمعنى من جهته لا من جهتها صير إلى الموجب الأصلي وهو حد القذف، وعدم صلاحيته للشهادة بكونه عبداً أو محدوداً في قذف أو كافراً بأن أسلمت ثم قذفها قبل عرض الإسلام عليه. قيدنا به لأن الزوج لو كان صبياً أو مجنوناً فلا حد ولا لعان، والأصل أن اللعان إذا سقط لمعنى من جهته، فإن كان القذف صحيحاً وجب الحد عليه، وإن لم يكن القذف صحيحاً فلا حد ولا لعان؛ كذا البدائع. فلو قال: فإن لم يصلح شاهداً وكان أهلاً للقذف حد لكان أولى. وفي الينابيع: زوجان كافران أسلمت المرأة ولم يسلم الزوج ولم يعرض القاضي الإسلام عليه حتى قذفها بالزنا وجب عليه الحد فإن أقيم بعض الحد ثم أسلم فقذفها ثانياً قال أبو يوسف: أقيم عليه بقية الحد ثم يلاعنا وقال زفر لا لعان بينهما. وفي النافع وإن كانا ذميين فأسلمت المرأة وقذفها قبل أن يعرض الإسلام عليه فلا لعان ويجد الزوج؛ كذا في التتارخانية. قوله: (وإن صلح وهي ممن لا يحد قاذفها فلا حد ولا لعان لأنها إن لم تكن عفيفة فهو صادق في قوله وإن كانت صغيرة أو مجنونة أو محدودة في قذف فلفقد أهليتها للشهادة، أما في الصغيرة والمجنونة فظاهر، وأما في المحدودة العفيفة فلأن قذفه أهلية اللعان إنما يوجب اللعان فإذا امتنع لعدم أهليتها له امتنع الحد أيضاً. وإن كانت ممن يحد قاذفها فلو قال: وإن صلح وهي ليست أهلاً للشهادة لكان أولى ليدخل المحدودة في قذف ولم تدخل في عبارته لأنها ممن يحد قاذفها كما لا يخفى. ولم يتعرض صريحاً لما إذا لم يصلحا لأداء الشهادة وقد فهم من اشتراطه أولاً أنه لا لعان. وأما الحد فإن كانا صغيرين أو مجنونين أو كافرين أو مملوكين فلا يجب، وأما إذا كانا محدودين في قذف فإنه يجب الحد عليه لأن امتناع اللعان لمعنى من جهته.
His saying: (If he is not fit as a witness, he is flogged) because when li'an is prevented due to a reason from his side, not from her side, we revert to the original obligation which is hadd for slander. His lack of fitness for testimony is by being a slave, or one flogged for slander, or a disbeliever such as if she became Muslim and then he slandered her before presenting Islam to him. We qualify this because if the husband is a minor or insane, then no hadd and no li'an. The principle is that if li'an falls due to a reason from his side, if the slander was valid, hadd is obligatory on him; if the slander was not valid, then no hadd and no li'an; as in al-Bada'i. So if he said: 'If he is not fit as a witness but is eligible for slander, he is flogged' would be better. In al-Yanabi': Two disbelieving spouses, the woman becomes Muslim and the man does not, and the judge did not present Islam to him before he slandered her of zina: hadd is obligatory on him. If some of the hadd is carried out then he becomes Muslim and slanders her again, Abu Yusuf says: The rest of the hadd is carried out on him then they perform li'an, and Zufar says there is no li'an between them. In al-Nafi': If they were dhimmis and the woman became Muslim and he slandered her before presenting Islam to him, then no li'an and the husband is flogged; as in al-Tatarakhaniyya. His saying: (And if he is fit and she is one whose slanderer is not flogged, then no hadd and no li'an) because if she is not chaste, he is truthful in his statement; if she is a minor, insane, or one who was flogged for slander, then due to her lack of eligibility for testimony. As for the minor and insane, it is apparent; as for the chaste person who was flogged for slander, because his slander (which necessitates li'an) only obligates li'an, so when it is prevented due to her lack of eligibility, hadd is also prevented. And if she is one whose slanderer is flogged, then if he said: 'If he is fit and she is not eligible for testimony' would be better to include the one flogged for slander, who is not included in his expression because she is one whose slanderer is flogged, as is not hidden. He did not explicitly address the case where both are not fit to perform testimony, and it is understood from his condition first that there is no li'an. As for hadd, if both are minors, insane, disbelievers, or slaves, then it is not obligatory; if they are both flogged for slander, then hadd is obligatory on him because the prevention of li'an is due to a reason from his side.
Source pages p. 194

Commentary
This passage explains the conditions under which hadd (the fixed punishment for false accusation of zina) applies when li'an is not possible because the husband lacks the eligibility to be a witness. The base ruling is that if the husband is not fit to testify (e.g., slave, hadd-punished for qadhf, disbeliever), then the original punishment for slander—hadd—is applied because li'an cannot function. However, if the husband is also not legally capable of committing slander (e.g., minor, insane), then no hadd and no li'an. The author elaborates on various scenarios: if the wife becomes Muslim before the husband and he slanders her before being invited to Islam, hadd is obligatory. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Yusuf and Zufar regarding the case where a disbeliever accepts Islam. Abu Yusuf holds that if some hadd was already carried out, the rest is completed and then li'an is performed; Zufar says no li'an. Regarding the wife: if she is not chaste, the husband is truthful and no hadd; if she is a minor, insane, or was previously flogged for slander, she lacks eligibility for testimony, so no li'an and no hadd. The author notes that the matn's wording could be improved for clarity. Finally, if both parties are not eligible for testimony (e.g., both slaves), then no li'an, and hadd is only obligatory if the husband is the cause of the prevention (e.g., he is a slave but the wife is free), but if both are equal in ineligibility, hadd is not obligatory.

Key Terms
صلح شاهداً (ṣaluḥa shāhidan): Being legally fit to serve as a witness in court, requiring freedom, integrity, and not having been punished for false accusation.
أهلية اللعان (ahliyyat al-liʿān): The legal capacity to perform li'an, which requires being a fit witness (for the husband) and being eligible to be accused of zina (for the wife, requiring chastity or sanity, etc.).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband is a slave (thus not a fit witness) and he accused his wife of zina, what is the ruling?
A) He must perform li'an despite being a slave.
B) He is flogged for false accusation (hadd al-qadhf).
C) No punishment because he is a slave.
D) The wife is flogged instead.

Key Takeaway
When li'an is impossible due to the husband's lack of witness eligibility, hadd for qadhf becomes wajib if his slander is valid; otherwise (minor, insane) no hadd and no li'an.

Li'an Separation Requires Judge's Decree: The Hanafi Position
States the definition of li'an and the basic ruling that separation requires the judge's decision

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that li'an separation requires a judge's decree and identify the condition under which the husband receives hadd instead.

Core Idea
Li'an does not separate the spouses; only the judge's decree does.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies a critical point in Hanafi li'an law: the mutual oaths do not automatically dissolve the marriage. Instead, a judge's ruling is required. The text also addresses a special scenario where the husband is a slave or the wife has been punished for false accusation, in which case the husband faces hadd punishment for qadhf rather than li'an. Understanding this distinction is essential for correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the central ruling on li'an separation
The passage states that after li'an, the wife becomes separated only by the judge's decree, not by the oaths alone. Locate the phrase 'بانت بتفريق الحاكم ولا تبين قبله'.
This is the key Hanafi position: separation requires judicial intervention.
2
Recognize the exception for slave husband or muhaddada wife
If the husband is a slave (unable to testify) or the wife has been previously punished for qadhf (muhaddada), the husband cannot perform valid li'an and receives hadd for his accusation instead.
The text says 'يحد' meaning he is punished by the prescribed hadd for false accusation.
3
Understand the rationale for ta'zir
The passage explains that ta'zir is obligatory in some cases to prevent harm and disgrace. Note that the hadd applies to the chaste woman absolutely, even if she was previously punished.
This reflects the principle of protecting honor and preventing harm.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وصفته ما نطق به النص فإن التعنا بانت بتفريق الحاكم ولا تبين قبله وإن قذف بولد إذا كان هو عبد أو هي محدودة في قذف يحد لأن قذف العفيفة ولو كانت محدودة موجب للحد مطلقاً. قيد بنفي الحد واللعان لأن التعزير واجب لأنه إذا أذاها وألحق الشين بها فيجب حسماً لهذا الباب؛ كذا في الاختيار.
Its description is what the text has spoken of: if they perform li'an, she becomes separated by the judge's separation, and she does not become separated before it. And if he accuses of a child, if he [the husband] is a slave or she [the wife] is one who has been punished for false accusation, he is punished by hadd, because accusing a chaste woman, even if she has been punished [for false accusation], necessarily entails the hadd punishment absolutely. It is restricted by the negation of hadd and li'an because ta'zir is obligatory, because if he harms her and brings disgrace upon her, it becomes obligatory to suppress this case; thus in al-Ikhtiyar.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the sharh, explaining the basic rule of li'an: the marital separation does not occur simply by the spouses performing the oaths; rather, it requires a decree from the judge. The text also addresses a condition regarding the husband or wife being eligible for hadd punishment for false accusation. If the husband is a slave (who cannot be a witness in li'an) or the wife has previously been punished for false accusation (muhaddada), then the husband is subject to hadd for his accusation, because his accusation is not a valid basis for li'an. The commentary from al-Ikhtiyar adds that ta'zir (discretionary punishment) is imposed to prevent harm and disgrace.

Key Terms
اللعان (al-li‘ān): The mutual oaths of condemnation between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery without witnesses.
التعزير (al-ta‘zīr): Discretionary punishment not fixed by the Shari'ah, applied for offenses that do not have a prescribed hadd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is required for li'an to result in separation of the spouses in Hanafi fiqh?
A) The mere performance of the oaths by the husband and wife.
B) A decree from the judge after the oaths.
C) The husband's triple divorce pronouncement.
D) The wife's acceptance of the accusations.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, li'an oaths do not automatically dissolve the marriage; a judge's decree is essential for separation, and under certain conditions (slave husband or muhaddada wife) the husband receives hadd instead.

Eligibility Conditions for Li'an: Dispute with al-Kafi
Resolves an intra-madhhab dispute about liability for hadd when both spouses are muhaddada

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on hadd liability when both spouses are muhaddada and explain the principle that a preventer (mani') only blocks a ruling when the requisite (muqtadi) exists.

Core Idea
A preventer only blocks a ruling when the legal requisite exists—otherwise no effect.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq resolves an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the liability for hadd (the fixed punishment for false accusation) when both spouses have been punished for qadhf (muhaddada). The key analytical tool is the usul principle that a preventer (mani') is only considered effective when the requisite (muqtadi) is present. The commentary verifies that the husband's eligibility for testimony determines whether the wife's status as muhaddada can prevent the hadd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
The scenario is when both husband and wife have previously been punished for false accusation (qadhf). The dispute is whether the husband is liable for hadd when he accuses his wife.
2
State the view in al-Kafi and the objection
Al-Kafi suggests hadd is due on the husband because his accusation does not warrant li'an (since he is muhaddada). A potential objection says that the wife's muhaddada status should prevent li'an, leading to hadd.
The objection focuses on the wife's condition.
3
Apply the usul principle of mani' and muqtadi
The commentator clarifies that a preventer (mani') is only considered when the requisite (muqtadi) exists. If the husband lacks eligibility for testimony, his accusation never becomes a requisite for li'an, so the wife's status cannot act as a preventer.
This is the central analytical move.
4
Distinguish the two cases based on husband's eligibility
If the husband is eligible (e.g., free, Muslim, just), his accusation creates a muqtadi for li'an. Then if the wife lacks ihsan (e.g., muhaddada, slave, non-Muslim), hadd is not imposed. If the husband is not eligible, hadd is imposed on him.
The wife's status is only relevant after the husband's eligibility is established.
5
Derive the practical ruling
The mufta bihi position: The husband is liable for hadd if he is not eligible for shahadah. If he is eligible, then the wife's ihsan status determines hadd. This resolves the apparent conflict in al-Kafi.
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وفي الكافي : وإن كانا محدودين في قذف فعليه الحد لأن قذفه باعتبار حاله غير موجب للعان فيكون موجباً للحد، ولا يجوز أن يقال امتناع جريان اللعان لكونها محدودة لأن أصل القذف من الرجل فإنما يظهر حكم المانع في حقها بعد قيام الأهلية في جانبه فأما بدون الأهلية في جانبه معتبر بحالها اهـ. وتحقيقه كما في العناية أن المانع من الشيء إنما يعتبر مانعاً إذا وجد المقتضي لأنه عبارة عما ينفي به الحكم مع وجود المقتضي، وإذا لم يكن الزوج أهلاً للشهادة لم ينعقد قذفه مقتضياً للعان فلا يعتبر المانع للحد فيحد بخلاف ما إذا وجدت الأهلية من جانبه فإنه ينعقد قذفه والقذف في نفسه موجب مقتضياً له، فإذا ظهر عدم أهليتها بطل المقتضي فلا يجب الحد لأنه إنما انعقد اللعان وقد ثم الإحصان يعتبر عند القذف حتى لو قذفها وهي أمة أو كافرة ثم أسلمت أبطله المانع أو أعتقت لا حد ولا لعان كذا ذكره الشارح .
And in al-Kafi: If both of them have been punished for false accusation, then the hadd is due on him because his accusation, considering his condition, does not necessitate li'an, so it necessitates hadd. And it is not permissible to say that the running of li'an is prevented because she is muhaddada, because the origin of the accusation is from the man; the ruling of the preventer appears regarding her only after the eligibility is established on his side. But without eligibility on his side, her condition is considered. Its verification is as in al-'Inayah: the preventer of a thing is only considered a preventer when the requisite exists, because it is that by which the ruling is negated together with the existence of the requisite. If the husband is not eligible for testimony, his accusation does not become a requisite for li'an, so the preventer of hadd is not considered, and he is punished by hadd. In contrast, if eligibility exists on his side, then his accusation becomes a requisite for li'an; if her lack of eligibility appears, the requisite is nullified, so hadd is not obligatory, because li'an has already been established and ihsan is considered at the time of accusation. So even if he accuses her while she is a slave or disbeliever, then she becomes Muslim, the preventer nullifies it, or she is freed: no hadd and no li'an. Thus mentioned the commentator.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the scenario where both spouses have previously been punished for qadhf (false accusation of adultery). The view in al-Kafi states that the husband is subject to hadd because his accusation does not warrant li'an (since he himself is not eligible for shahadah). The commentator then refutes a potential objection that the wife's status as muhaddada prevents li'an. The verification from al-'Inayah clarifies the legal principle: a preventer (mani') is only effective when the requisite (muqtadi) exists. If the husband lacks the capacity to witness, his accusation never rises to the level of a muqtadi for li'an, so the preventer of hadd (the wife's ihsan) is not considered. If the husband is eligible, then the muqtadi exists, and if the wife lacks ihsan (e.g., she is a slave or non-Muslim) at the time of accusation, the muqtadi fails and no hadd. The principle of 'consideration at time of accusation' is emphasized.

Key Terms
المانع (al-māni‘): A legal impediment that prevents a ruling from taking effect even when the requisite is present.
المقتضي (al-muqtadī): The legal cause or requisite that would lead to a ruling if no preventer exists.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the verification in al-'Inayah, when does a preventer (mani') become effective in preventing a ruling?
A) Always, regardless of the existence of the requisite.
B) Only when the requisite (muqtadi) exists.
C) Only when the preventer is mentioned in the text.
D) Only when both parties agree.

Key Takeaway
The effectiveness of a preventer (mani') depends on the existence of the requisite (muqtadi); in li'an, the husband's eligibility for shahadah is the key requisite.

What Nullifies Li'an After Its Obligation
Lists nullifiers of li'an

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the five events that nullify li'an and apply the maxim 'al-sāqiṭ lā ya‘ūdu' to determine whether li'an can be reinstated after nullification.

Core Idea
Li'an drops by five things: divorce, her zina, shubhah, apostasy, and witness death — and does not return.

Li'an is a serious process between spouses, but once it becomes obligatory, certain events can cause it to lapse. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq enumerates the specific nullifiers and clarifies what does not nullify it. Understanding these exceptions ensures correct application of hadd penalties and marital consequences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the obligation of li'an
Recall that li'an becomes obligatory when a husband accuses his wife of zina without witnesses, and he wishes to avoid the hadd penalty for false accusation.
Li'an is a sworn mutual cursing between spouses.
2
List the events that nullify li'an
From the passage, extract the five specific events that cause li'an to lapse after it has become obligatory: (1) divorce, (2) wife's actual zina, (3) intercourse under shubhah, (4) wife's apostasy, (5) death or absence of the witness who would testify.
Each of these events completely drops the obligation of li'an.
3
Note what does NOT nullify li'an
The passage distinguishes between nullifying and non-nullifying events. The husband's retraction of his accusation before completing li'an does not nullify it. Similarly, the witness becoming blind, sinful, or apostate does not nullify li'an.
Retraction after li'an has special rules; the passage notes that retraction after li'an does lead to hadd.
4
Apply the maxim 'al-sāqiṭ lā ya‘ūdu'
Once li'an is nullified, it cannot be reinstated. For example, if the husband divorces his wife before completing li'an, he cannot reinitiate li'an after remarrying her. The maxim reinforces that the dropped obligation does not return.
This principle applies broadly in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Distinguish borderline scenarios
Consider the extra cases: accusing a formerly minor/insane wife does not require li'an because the accusation is implausible, whereas accusing a dhimmi or older woman may require li'an due to possibility.
These nuances show that li'an is only relevant when the accusation is plausible.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم اعلم أن اللعان بعد وجوبه يسقط بالطلاق ولا يجب الحد ولا يعود اللعان يتزوجها بعده لأن الساقط لا يعود ويسقط بزناها ووطئها بشبهة ،وبردتها وإن أسلمت بعده لا يعود بإكذابه نفسه ولا يحد بخلاف ما إذا أكذب نفسه بعد اللعان وبموت شاهد القذف وغيبته بخلاف ما لو عميا أو فسقا أو ارتدا كما في الآن أهل القدير. ولو أسند الزنا بأن قال زنيت وأنت صبية أو مجنونة وهو معهود وهي فتح فلا لعان بخلاف وأنت ذمية أو أمة أو منذر أربعين سنة وعمرها أقل تلاعنا لاقتصاره كما في فتح القدير أيضاً.
Then know that li'an after its obligation is dropped by divorce, and hadd (false accusation punishment) is not obligatory, and li'an does not return if he marries her afterwards because the dropped does not return. And it is dropped by her committing zina, by intercourse under uncertainty, by her apostasy, and if she becomes Muslim afterwards, it does not return. It is not dropped by him retracting his own accusation, and he is not punished by hadd, contrary to if he retracts after li'an. And it is dropped by the death of the witness of the accusation and his absence, contrary to if they become blind or sinful or apostatize, as in 'Ahl al-Qadir' [likely 'Fath al-Qadir']. And if he attributes the zina by saying 'you committed zina while you were a young girl or insane' while he is accustom [؟] and she is a virgin, then no li'an, contrary to if he says 'while you were a dhimmi or a slave or one who reached forty years while her age is less' then they perform li'an due to the restriction, as in Fath al-Qadir also.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement enumerating the factors that nullify li'an after it has become obligatory. Once the husband initiates the process of li'an, it can be invalidated by: (1) the husband divorcing his wife before completing li'an; (2) the wife committing actual zina; (3) the wife having intercourse under shubhah; (4) the wife's apostasy (even if she later returns to Islam); (5) the death or absence of the witness whose testimony would have supported the accusation. Conversely, the husband's retraction of his accusation after li'an does not nullify it, nor does the witness becoming blind, sinful (fasiq), or apostate. The passage also notes a subtle distinction: if the husband accuses his wife of zina while she was a minor or insane, and he is accustomed to her being a virgin, no li'an is required because the accusation is inherently false. But if he accuses a dhimmi or a woman over forty while she is younger, li'an is performed because the accusation is plausible.

Key Terms
الساقط لا يعود (al-sāqiṭ lā ya‘ūdu): A legal maxim: once an obligation is dropped, it does not become obligatory again.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In Hanafi fiqh, which of the following does NOT nullify li'an after it has become obligatory?
A) The divorce of the wife by the husband.
B) The wife's apostasy.
C) The husband's retraction of his accusation before completing li'an.
D) The death of the witness who would have testified.

Key Takeaway
Li'an is nullified by divorce, her zina or shubhah, her apostasy, and witness death; the maxim 'al-sāqiṭ lā ya‘ūdu' ensures it does not return.

Description and Order of Li'an: The Husband's Precedence as an Integral Element
Parsing the definition and order of li'an oaths

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the integral elements (arkan) of li'an according to the Hanafi school and explain the ruling when the wife begins the oaths before the husband.

Core Idea
In li'an, the husband's precedence is an integral part (rukn), not merely a condition.

The commentator unpacks the term 'sifah' in the matn, showing that it refers to the essential structure of li'an: the husband must begin with four oaths and the fifth invocation, followed by the wife. This order is not just recommended but constitutive. However, a nuance arises if the wife starts first: does the husband need to repeat, and may the judge rule before that repetition? The digest of this lesson clarifies these points through a close reading of the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the key term 'sifah'
The commentator says 'sifah' means the essential description, analogous to 'sifat al-salah' meaning the essence of prayer. Here it denotes the integral elements (arkan) of li'an: the husband's quadruple oaths and fifth curse, followed by the wife's quadruple oaths and fifth invocation of wrath.
Do not confuse with recommended attributes; sifah here is structural.
2
Recognize the default order
The text emphasizes that the husband must begin; otherwise, the natural order is disrupted. This is the default ruling (mufta bihi).
Hanafi position: the husband's commencement is rukn.
3
Analyze the case of the wife starting first
If the wife initiates, the husband must repeat the oaths after her. However, if the judge pronounces a separation before the husband's repetition, the separation is valid (sahih).
This is the relied-upon view as per Fath al-Qadir.
4
Consider the contrary opinion from al-Ghayah
Al-Ghayah holds that repetition is obligatory (wajib) and the judge cannot separate beforehand. The commentator notes this is a deviation (from the Sunnah?).
Fath al-Qadir rejects this, siding with Malik.
5
Connect to the analogy of wudu
The commentator draws an analogy to the dropping of order (tartib) in wudu: although the verse 'When you rise for prayer, wash your faces...' uses 'fa' (then), which implies order, the Hanafi school does not require sequentiality in wudu. Similarly, the 'fa' in the li'an verses does not necessitate rigid order but indicates a sequence that can be remedied.
This analogy helps understand the flexibility in li'an.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وصفته ما نطق به النص أي صفة اللعان ما دلت عليه الة اللعان من الابتداء بالزوج ثم بالزوجة بالألفاظ المخصوصة، وظاهره أنه متعين وقدمنا أن المرأة لو بدأت ثم الزوج أعادت، ولو فرق القاضي قبل إعادتها صح، وفي الغاية تجب الإعادة وقد أخطأ السنة ورجحه في فتح القدير بأنه الوجه وهو قول مالك لأن النص أعقب الرمي بشهادة أحدهم وشهادتها الدارئة للحد عنها بقوله ويدرأ عنها العذاب ولأن الفاء دخلت على شهادته على وزان ما قلنا في سقوط الترتيب في الوضوء من أنه أعقب جملة الأفعال للقيام إلى الصلاة وإن كان دخول الفاء على غسل الوجه فانظره ثمة ا.هـ. والظاهر أنه أراد بالصفة الركن كقولهم باب صفة الصلاة أي ماهيتها فيكون بياناً للشهادات الأربع ، وإنما أولناه بذلك لأن صفته على قوله : (فلو قال وإن صلح وهي ليست أهلاً للشهادة لكان أولى فيه أنه لو قال كذلك لا يشمل ما إذا كانت غير عفيفة فإنها من أهل الشهادة لكنها ممن لا يحد قاذفها وعن هذا قال في النهر : في كلام المصنف جملة حالية مطوية أي وإن صلح شاهداً ولم تصلح اهـ. تأمل .
His statement: 'And its description is what the text has spoken of' i.e. the description of li'an is what the tool of li'an indicates: beginning with the husband, then with the wife, with specific utterances. Its apparent meaning is that it is determined, and we have already mentioned that if the woman begins, then the husband repeats, and if the judge separates before her repetition, it is valid. In al-Ghayah, repetition is obligatory, and it is a deviation from the Sunnah [؟]. And the matter is preferred in Fath al-Qadir that it is the correct view and it is the saying of Malik, because the text followed the accusation with the testimony of one of them and her testimony that repels the hadd from her by His saying 'and the punishment is repelled from her' and because the fa entered upon his testimony in analogy to what we said regarding the dropping of order in wudu: that it followed the sequence of actions for standing for prayer even though the fa entered upon washing the face. Look at it there. It is apparent that he intended by 'description' the integral (rukn), as they say 'chapter on the description of prayer' i.e. its essence. Thus it is an explanation of the four testimonies. We only interpreted it thus because its description according to his statement: 'if he said and is fit' and she is not fit for testimony, it would be more appropriate. But if he said like that, it would not include when she is unchaste, for she is from the people of testimony but not from those whose accuser is punished by hadd. About this, in al-Nahr, it is said: In the author's speech, there is an implied circumstantial clause i.e. 'if he is fit as a witness and she is not'. Reflect.
Source pages p. 195

Commentary
This passage is a parsing exercise where the commentator explains the meaning of the word 'description' (sifah) in the matn. He clarifies that it refers to the essential elements (arkan) of li'an: the husband begins with four oaths and the fifth invoking the curse, then the wife does the same with four oaths and the fifth invoking wrath. The text discusses the obligatory order: the husband must begin. However, there is a nuance: if the wife starts, the husband must repeat, and if the judge separates before the husband's repetition, the separation is valid. The commentator notes a view in al-Ghayah that repetition is obligatory, but Fath al-Qadir prefers that it is not, aligning with the Maliki school. The commentator also interprets the matn's phrase 'its description' to mean the integral elements, analogous to 'description of prayer' meaning the essence of prayer. The text ends with a subtle point about the wife's qualification for testimony and chastity, citing al-Nahr.

Key Terms
الصفة (al-ṣifa): In this context, the essential description or integral elements (arkan) of a legal act, as opposed to mere attributes.
اللعان (al-li‘ān): Mutual cursing between spouses when the husband accuses the wife of adultery without witnesses.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The husband must repeat his oaths before the judge can separate.
B) The judge can separate without the husband repeating, but the husband must still repeat later.
C) The judge can separate immediately, and the husband does not need to repeat.
D) The li'an is invalid and must be restarted from the beginning.

Key Takeaway
The husband's precedence in li'an is an integral element (rukn), yet if the wife starts first, the separation can still be valid before his repetition.

The Procedure of Li'an According to the Sunnah
Ruling statement with expansion and proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the precise Hanafi procedure for li'an, explain the rationale for using 'ghadab' for the wife, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference regarding direct address.

Core Idea
The li'an procedure is a prescribed oath-swearing ceremony; deviations from the sunnah method are makruh tanzihi but do not invalidate.

This lesson unpacks the detailed method of li'an as transmitted by the Hanafi mashayikh. You will learn the exact wording for each spouse, the wisdom behind invoking 'wrath' for the woman, and the difference of opinion between Imam al-Hasan and the majority regarding direct address. The lesson also clarifies that standing is recommended, not obligatory.

Guided Path
1
Identify the overall ruling of li'an procedure
Recognize that the described procedure is the sunnah method; any deviation is makruh tanzihi but li'an remains valid.
The ruling is sunnah muakkadah, not wajib.
2
Trace the husband's oath sequence
Follow the text: four oaths of 'I bear witness by Allah that I am truthful' followed by the fifth: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am a liar'. Note the pointing gesture each time.
The fifth oath invokes la'nah (curse) on himself.
3
Trace the wife's oath sequence
Follow the text: four oaths of 'I bear witness by Allah that he is a liar' followed by the fifth: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is truthful'.
The wife uses ghadab (wrath) instead of la'nah.
4
Analyze the rationale for using ghadab for the wife
Understand the textual explanation: women curse frequently, so wrath is a stronger deterrent. Also, her position is more suspect due to circumstantial evidence against her.
Al-Biqa'i noted that ghadab is more effective than la'nah.
5
Evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute on direct vs indirect address
Compare Imam al-Hasan's requirement for direct address (mukhatabah) with the majority view (zahir al-riwayah) that indirect address with pointing suffices. Note the weight given to the majority and the mufta bihi position.
The indirect method is relied upon because pointing is the strongest means of identification.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وجه السنة لم ينطق به النص وإنما ورد في السنة فالذي نقله المشايخ أن القاضي يقيمهما متقابلين ويقول له التعن فيقول الزوج أشهد بالله إني لمن الصادقين فيما رميتها به من الزنا ويقول في الخامسة لعنة الله عليه إن كان من الكاذبين فيما رماها به من الزنا يشير إليها في كل مرة ثم تقول المرأة أربع مرات اشهد بالله إنه لمن الكاذبين فيما رماني به من الزنا وتقول في الخامسة غضب الله عليها إن كان من الصادقين فيما رماني به من الزنا. وإنما ذكر الغضب في جانبها في الخامسة لأنهن يستعملن اللعن كثيراً كما في الحديث يكثرن اللعن» (۱) فكان الغضب أردع لها ؛ هكذا ذكر المشايخ. وذكر البقاعي في المناسبات أن الغضب أبلغ من اللعن الذي هو الطرد لأنه قد يكون بسبب غير الغضب وسبب التغليظ عليها الحث على اعترافها بالحق لما يعضد الزوج من القرينة من أنه لا يتجشم فضيحة أهله المستلزم لفضيحته إلا وهو صادق ولأنها مادة الفساد وهاتكة الحجاب وخالطة الأنساب وفي رواية الحسن أنه لا بد أن يقول إني لمن الصادقين فيما رميتك به من الزنا وهي تقول إنك لمن الكاذبين فيما رميتني به من الزنا بالخطاب لأن في الغيبة شبهة واحتمالاً وفي ظاهر الرواية لم يعتبر هذا لأن كل واحد منهما يشير إلى صاحبه والإشارة أبلغ أسباب التعريف؛ كذا في الكافي هذا كله إذا كان القذف بالزنا، وإن كان بنفي الولد ذكراه وإن كان بهما ذكراهما، وزاد بعضهم بعد القسم الذي لا إله إلا هو. والقيام ليس بشرط لأنه إما شهادة وإما يمين والقيام ليس بشرط فيهما إلا أنه مندوب إليه لقوله : يا عاصم قم فاشهد وللمرأة قومي فاشهدي ولأن الحدود مبناها على الشهر .
The form of the Sunnah is not spoken of by the text but is mentioned in the Sunnah. What the mashayikh have transmitted is that the judge makes them stand facing each other and says to him 'perform li'an', so the husband says: 'I bear witness by Allah that I am among the truthful in what I have accused her of regarding zina', and he says in the fifth: 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am among the liars in what he accused her of regarding zina', pointing to her each time. Then the woman says four times: 'I bear witness by Allah that he is among the liars in what he accused me of regarding zina', and she says in the fifth: 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if he is among the truthful in what he accused me of regarding zina'. And the mention of wrath in her side in the fifth is because women frequently use curses, as in the hadith 'they curse frequently', so wrath is more deterring for her; thus the mashayikh mentioned. And al-Biqa'i mentioned in al-Munasabat that wrath is more effective than cursing which is expulsion, because it may be for other than anger. The reason for severity upon her is to urge her to confess the truth because the husband is supported by circumstantial evidence that he would not expose his family's dishonor leading to his own disgrace unless he is truthful, and because she is the source of corruption, the one who tears the veil and mixes lineages. And in a narration of al-Hasan, it is necessary that he says 'I am among the truthful in what I accused you of regarding zina' and she says 'You are among the liars in what you accused me of regarding zina' using direct address, because in indirect speech there is ambiguity and possibility. In the apparent narration, this is not considered because each one points to the other, and pointing is the strongest means of identification; thus in al-Kafi. All this is if the accusation is of zina; if it is of denying a child, he mentions that, and if it is of both, he mentions both. And some added after the oath 'There is no god but Allah'. Standing is not a condition because it is either testimony or an oath, and standing is not a condition in either of them, except that it is recommended, due to his saying: 'O 'Asim, stand and bear witness' and to the woman 'stand and bear witness'. And because hudud are based on publicity.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the actual procedure of li'an as practiced by the Companions and transmitted by the Hanafi mashayikh. The procedure involves: the judge positioning both spouses facing each other, the husband reciting four oaths (beginning with 'I bear witness by Allah that I am truthful' and the fifth invoking the curse), then the wife reciting four oaths (beginning 'I bear witness by Allah that he is a liar' and the fifth invoking wrath). The passage explains the wisdom of using 'wrath' (ghadab) for the woman instead of 'curse' (la'n), as it is more deterrent. The commentator also notes a variant from Imam al-Hasan who required direct address, but the majority view accepts indirect address because the spouses gesture towards each other. Standing is recommended, not obligatory, because the oath or testimony does not require standing. The procedure also applies if the accusation includes denial of paternity. Some jurists add the phrase 'there is no god but Allah' (i.e., the oath of tahlil) after the fourth oath according to some reports.

Key Terms
الغضب (al-ghaḍab): The wrath of Allah, invoked in the wife's fifth oath as a stronger deterrent than curse.
اللعان (al-li‘ān): Mutual imprecation; a procedure where a husband accuses his wife of zina or denies paternity without witnesses, leading to oaths and curses.
شهادة (shahādah): Testimony; the oaths begin with 'I bear witness by Allah'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the Hanafi procedure of li'an, what does the husband say in his fifth oath?
A) 'The wrath of Allah be upon me if I am a liar'
B) 'The curse of Allah be upon me if I am a liar'
C) 'The curse of Allah be upon her if she is truthful'
D) 'I am truthful in my accusation'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi sunnah method for li'an involves specific oaths and gestures; standing is recommended but not obligatory, and indirect address with pointing is sufficient.

Accepting Testimony After Li'an: A Qiyas Analysis
Determines if testimony after li'an can be accepted.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi qiyas method to evaluate whether evidence presented after li'an can be accepted for the purpose of remarriage.

Core Idea
Li'an acts like a hadd, but the husband's later evidence or confession can lift its prohibition by analogy.

The passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced question: after a couple has performed li'an, can the husband later bring proof that his accusation was true? The initial response, based on analogy to hadd, suggests rejection. However, a deeper analysis using qiyas—comparing to the case where the husband admits lying—leads to a different conclusion. This lesson walks through the reasoning, showing how Hanafi jurists use analogical reasoning (qiyas) to resolve unsettled issues.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue
The husband brings proof after li'an: is it accepted by the court?
This is a novel question not explicitly addressed in earlier texts.
2
Initial position and its basis
The first answer: not accepted, because li'an is like a hadd, so no second penalty.
Analogy to hadd: once the hadd is executed, it cannot be repeated.
3
Refutation by counterexample
The case of the husband admitting lying: li'an also like a hadd, yet he is still hadded. So the analogy fails.
This shows the 'alla is not simply 'no second hadd'.
4
Refined analogy
The underlying 'illa: in both cases, the husband becomes unqualified for li'an. When he admits lying, it's explicit; when he brings evidence, it implicitly establishes the wife's unchastity, thus the same 'illa applies.
The 'illa is extracted by tanqih al-manat.
5
Practical consequence
The benefit is remarriage becomes permissible.
This is the key outcome: solving the prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد سئلت في حين قرأت باب اللعان من الهداية أنهما لو تلاعنا ثم وجد الزوج بينة على صدقه هل تقبل؟ فأجبت بأني لم أر فيها نقلاً وينبغي أن لا تقبل لأن القذف أخذ موجبه من وكأنها حدت للزنا فلا تحد ثانياً إلا أن يوجد نقل فيجب اتباعه. قلت: هذا منقوض بما إذا أكذب نفسه بعد اللعان فإنه أخذ اللعان وكأنه حد فلا يحد مع أن الحكم أنه يحد. فإن قيل: قد وقع نسبته إياها إلى الزنا في شهادته عند الحاكم فإذا أكذب نفسه يحد لذلك قلت: هذا ضمني لا قصدي ومثله لا يوجب، وكيف نقول بإيجابه الحد مع أنه مأمور به من الشارع صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم بقوله: قم فاشهد. وذكروا أن من قال فلان قال عنك إنك زنيت لم يحد لأنه لم ينسبه إلى الزنا قصداً. قلت: فينبغي أن تقبل ويترتب عليه فائدة حل نكاحها. قال في خزانة الإكمال: إذا رجع المتلاعنان إلى حال لا يتلاعنان فيه جاز أن يتزوجها والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم .اهـ. ومثله في النهر حيث قال: ولقائل أن يقول لم لا يجوز أن يقبل ليترتب عليه حل نكاحها له وقد علل في الهداية حل نكاحها فيما إذا كذب نفسه فحد بأنه لما حد لم يبق أهلاً للعان فارتفع بحكمه المنوط به وهو التحريم، وهذا يتأتى هنا فإنه إذا ثبت أنها غير عفيفة لم يبق أهلاً للعان فارتفع حكمه فتدبره.
And I was asked while reading the chapter of li'an from al-Hidayah: If they performed li'an, then the husband found evidence of his truthfulness, is it accepted? So I answered that I have not seen a transmission in it, and it should not be accepted because the accusation took its consequence, and it is as if she was hadded for adultery, so she is not hadded a second time unless a transmission exists, then it must be followed. I said: This is refuted by the case where he accuses himself of lying after li'an, for he took li'an as if it were a hadd, so he is not hadded, yet the ruling is that he is hadded. If it is said: He attributed her to adultery in his testimony before the judge, so when he accuses himself of lying, he is hadded for that. I said: This is implicit, not explicit, and such does not necessitate. How can we say it necessitates a hadd while he was commanded to do so by the Lawgiver (SAW) saying: 'Stand and testify.' And they mentioned that he who said: 'So-and-so said about you that you committed adultery' is not hadded because he did not directly attribute adultery to her. So I say: Then it should be accepted, and from it follows the benefit of making her marriage permissible to him. It is said in Khizanat al-Ikmal: If the two who performed li'an revert to a state where they cannot perform li'an again, it is permissible for him to marry her. And Allah knows best. Similar is in al-Nahr where he said: One could say why is it not accepted so that the benefit of making her marriage permissible to him follows? And it is reasoned in al-Hidayah that when he accuses himself of lying and is hadded, because he is no longer qualified for li'an, the ruling attached to it (prohibition) is lifted. This applies here too: if it is established that she is not chaste, he is no longer qualified for li'an, so its ruling is lifted. So ponder it.
Source pages p. 196

Commentary
This passage addresses a question: If a couple performs li'an, and later the husband finds proof of his accusation, can that proof be accepted? The author initially says it should not be accepted, comparing it to a second hadd after a first hadd (the li'an itself acts like a hadd). However, the author then presents a counterargument: if the husband admits lying after li'an, he is hadded, even though li'an is like a hadd. So why not accept evidence? The author refines: the admission of lying is an explicit attribution, whereas the evidence after li'an is implicit. The author then leans toward accepting the evidence because it would allow the couple to marry again (if they separate). The commentary from Khizanat al-Ikmal and al-Nahr supports this by analogy: if after li'an the husband becomes unqualified for li'an (e.g., because the wife is proven unchaste), the prohibition arising from li'an lifts.

Key Terms
الحد (al-hadd): Fixed penalty for a specific crime; here li'an is compared to a hadd in its effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the main benefit of accepting the husband's evidence after li'an, according to the passage?
A) To prove the wife's guilt and have her punished.
B) To allow the husband to remarry her if they had separated.
C) To avoid the hadd punishment for the wife.
D) To confirm that the li'an was valid.

Key Takeaway
Evidence presented after li'an can be accepted by analogy to the husband's admission of lying, if it lifts the prohibition on remarriage.

Effect of Li'an: Separation Requires Judge's Decree
Explains when li'an causes separation and subsequent marital rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that li'an does not automatically separate the couple but requires a judge's decree, and identify the conditions under which separation is or is not decreed.

Core Idea
Li'an does not dissolve marriage; separation requires a judge's decree, and the marriage remains valid until then.

A common misconception is that li'an automatically ends the marriage. The Hanafi school clarifies that li'an itself only prohibits intimacy; the marriage remains intact until a judge decrees separation. This lesson explores the ruling, its evidence, and exceptional cases where separation is not decreed due to loss of legal qualification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main ruling
Focus on the statement: 'If they perform li'an, she becomes separated by the judge's decree, and she does not become separated before that.' Understand that the li'an ritual alone does not dissolve the marriage; a judicial decree is necessary.
This is the central point of the passage.
2
Examine the intra-Hanafi difference
Note that if the original judge dies or is dismissed before decreeing, the second judge must repeat the entire li'an according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad holds that repetition is unnecessary. This shows how different assumptions about the finality of li'an affect procedure.
The text says 'khilafan li Muhammad'.
3
Analyze the exceptions
If the qualification for li'an is lost permanently (e.g., the husband admits lying, becomes mute, or one commits adultery), separation is not decreed. If it is temporarily lost (e.g., insanity), separation is still decreed because restoration is hoped for.
The loss of ihsan (chaste status) prevents the separation.
4
Review the evidence
The passage cites two hadith: 'Uwaymir divorced after li'an without the Prophet's disapproval, and the Prophet separated Hilal and his wife after li'an. These prove that the marriage continues until the judge decrees.
The Prophet's approval of 'Uwaymir's divorce shows the marriage was still valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن التعنا بانت بتفريق الحاكم ولا تبين قبله أي الحاكم الذي وقع اللعان عنده حتى لو لم يفرق الحاكم حتى عزل أو مات فالحاكم الثاني يستقبل اللعان عندهما خلافاً لمحمد؛ كذا في الاختيار. وأفاد أنه لو مات أحدهما قبل التفريق ورثه الآخر وأنه لو زالت أهلية اللعان في الحال بما لا يرجى زواله بأن أكذب نفسه أو قذف أحدهما انساناً فحد للقذف أو وطئت وطاً حراماً أو خرس أحدهما لم يفرق بينهما بخلاف ما إذا جن قبل التفريق حيث يفرق بينهما لأنه يرجى عود الإحصان، وأنه لو ظاهر منها في هذه الحالة أو طلقها أو آلى صح لبقاء النكاح، وأشار إلى أن القاضي يفرق بينهما ولو لم يرضيا بالفرقة كما في شرح النقاية. وفي التتارخانية : ولو تلاعنا فجن أحدهما يفرق ولو تلاعنا فوكل أحدهما بالتفريق وغاب يفرق، ولو زنت لا يفرق لزوال الإحصان، وإنما توقفت البينونة على التفريق لأنه لما حرم الاستمتاع بينهما باللعان فات الامساك بالمعروف فوجب عليه التسريح، وإذا لم يسرح ناب القاضي منابه لأنه نصب لدفع الظلم ويدل عليه أنه عليه الصلاة والسلام لاعن بين عويمر وبين امرأته فقال عويمراً كذبت عليها إن أمسكتها هي طالق ثلاثاً فأوقع الثلاث بعد التلاعن ولم ينكر عليه، وكذا في واقعة هلال قال الراوي: فلما فرغ فرق النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم بينهما. فدل على قيام النكاح قبل التفريق وهي تطليقة بائنة وهو خاطب إذا أكذب نفسه عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف هي حرم مؤبدة كما سيأتي.
His saying: (If they perform li'an, she becomes separated by the judge's decree, and she does not become separated before that) meaning the judge before whom the li'an took place. So if the judge did not decree separation until he was dismissed or died, the second judge must redo the li'an according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad. This is in al-Ikhtiyar. And he indicated that if one of them died before separation, the other inherits from him. And if the qualification for li'an is removed immediately in a way that its return is not hoped for, such as if he accuses himself of lying, or if one of them accuses a third person of adultery and is hadded for that, or if she commits illicit intercourse, or if one becomes mute, then separation is not decreed. Unlike if one becomes insane before separation, then separation is decreed because the restoration of chaste status is hoped for. And if he performs dhihar, or divorces, or ila in this state, it is valid because the marriage remains. He indicated that the judge decrees separation even if they do not consent to it, as in Sharh al-Niqayah. In al-Tatarakhaniyya: If they performed li'an then one becomes insane, separation is decreed. If they performed li'an then one appoints a proxy to effect separation and is absent, separation is decreed. If she commits adultery, separation is not decreed because the status of ihsan is removed. The separation is dependent on the decree because when intimacy became prohibited between them by li'an, retention (imsaak) with kindness is lost, so it becomes obligatory for him to release her. If he does not release her, the judge acts on his behalf because he is appointed to remove injustice. This is supported by the fact that the Prophet (SAW) performed li'an between 'Uwaymir and his wife, and 'Uwaymir said: 'If I kept her, I would be lying; she is divorced thrice.' So he pronounced triple divorce after the li'an, and the Prophet did not disapprove. Similarly, in the incident of Hilal, the narrator said: 'When he finished, the Prophet (SAW) separated them.' This indicates the marriage remained until separation. And (the divorce) is a final irrevocable divorce (bainunah). He is a suitor if he accuses himself of lying according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). According to Abu Yusuf, she becomes permanently prohibited (hurmat mu'abbada) as will come later.
Source pages p. 197

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq details the effect of li'an on the marriage. The key point: li'an itself does not dissolve the marriage; it only becomes effective when the judge decrees separation. Until then, the marriage is valid—they inherit from each other, and the husband can still divorce, perform dhihar, etc. The judge must decree separation even if the couple does not want it, because after li'an, intimacy is prohibited and 'retention with kindness' is impossible, so the husband must release her; if he fails, the judge steps in. The passage cites the hadith of 'Uwaymir who divorced after li'an, indicating the marriage was intact before separation. The passage also discusses various scenarios: if the husband admits lying after li'an, the marriage becomes final (bainunah) and he is a suitor (can remarry with a new marriage contract). According to Abu Yusuf, it is permanent prohibition (like a third divorce). Also, if the qualification for li'an is lost (e.g., becomes mute, or one commits adultery), separation is not decreed because the condition for li'an is absent. The passage also notes an intra-Hanafi difference: if the original judge dies before decree, a second judge must repeat the li'an according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, but Muhammad says the children are already established and separation is not needed? Actually, the text says the second judge must redo li'an according to them, contrary to Muhammad.

Key Terms
البينونة (al-bainunah): Final irrevocable divorce; after li'an, the separation is considered a final divorce (bainunah sughra or kubra depending on the case).
الإحصان (al-ihsan): Chastity or the condition of being in a valid marriage; loss of ihsan affects the applicability of hadd and li'an.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if the husband dies after li'an but before the judge decrees separation?
A) The wife inherits from him because the marriage is still valid.
B) The wife inherits only if they had children.
C) The wife does not inherit because li'an invalidated the marriage.
D) The inheritance is suspended until a judge rules.

Key Takeaway
Li'an does not dissolve marriage; separation requires a judge's decree, and the marriage remains valid until that decree is issued.

Separation in Li'an Only by Judge's Decree
Ruling with proof from hadith and fiqh reasoning

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that separation after li'an occurs only by judge's decree and distinguish it from the Shafi'i view based on the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Marriage continues after li'an until the judge formally separates the spouses.

Many assume that the mutual cursing in li'an immediately ends the marriage, but the Hanafi school requires a judge's decree. This lesson unpacks the ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, examining the textual evidence and the conditions that affect separation. By understanding this, you'll grasp how the Hanafi school prioritizes the continuity of marriage until an official nullification.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
Locate the key phrase that states when separation occurs. Note that the author explicitly says separation does not happen before the judge's decree.
Look at the beginning of the passage: 'فإن التعنا بانت بتفريق الحاكم ولا تبين قبله'.
2
Analyze the dalil from hadith
Examine the two hadith incidents cited: 'Uwaymir's divorce after li'an without Prophet's objection, and the Prophet's active separation in Hilal's case. Understand how they prove the marriage remains before the decree.
The Prophet's non-objection is key—if the marriage had ended, divorce would be meaningless.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
Identify the difference among the Hanafi imams regarding the new judge's role, and the broader disagreement with other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) on whether li'an itself causes separation.
The text mentions a dispute between Muhammad and the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) on restarting li'an; and the overall difference with those who hold li'an as automatic separation.
4
Evaluate the practical consequences
Apply the ruling to scenarios: inheritance, validity of zihar/divorce/ila during the interval, and the effect of conditions like insanity or loss of ihsan.
The passage lists many conditions; focus on how each affects the judge's ability to decree separation.
